Taharah — Purification
beginner
10 min
The Sunnah Acts of Wudu: A Detailed Exposition
Detailed enumeration and definition of sunnan of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list all the sunnah muakkadah acts of wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling and manner of performing each.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of wudu complete and perfect purification, but only the fard acts are required for validity.

In this passage from Nur al-Idah, the author enumerates the sunnah acts of wudu, providing definitions, rulings, and practical methods. These acts are confirmed sunnahs (sunnah muakkadah) that enhance the quality of wudu but are not required for its validity. Understanding these details helps a Muslim perfect his worship and avoid common misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the List
Read through the Arabic text and find the explicit mention of sunnah acts. They are: rinsing nose, exaggerating in mouth and nose (for non-fasting), combing beard, combing fingers, washing thrice, covering head, wiping ears, rubbing, continuity (wala'), and intention.
Some like 'rubbing' and 'combing fingers' are additional sunan.
2
Classify Each Act
Each act is generally sunnah muakkadah. Note that washing thrice: first wash is fard, second and third are sunnah. Mubalaghah is sunnah but restricted to non-fasting persons.
The ruling differs based on the act.
3
Understand the Methodology
For each sunnah, the text describes the specific method, e.g., combing beard from below with a handful of water, interlocking fingers for hands, using a finger for feet, wiping ears with thumbs and index fingers.
Method is important for correct practice.
4
Note Exceptions
Some sunan have conditions: mubalaghah is only for non-fasting, continuity depends on normal drying time, intention is after istinja.
Exceptions prevent nullification of other acts like fasting.
5
Appreciate Cross-Madhhab Differences
Compare Hanafi positions with other schools, e.g., Shafi'i considers intention fard and wiping the head fard. Understand that these differences are based on usul principles.
These are legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
سنن الوضوء: والاستنشاق بثلاث غرفات، والمبالغة في المضمضة والاستنشاق لغير الصائم، وتخليل اللحية الكثة بكف ماء من أسفلها، وتخليل الأصابع، وتثليث الغسل، واستيعاب الرأس بالمسح مرة، ومسح الأذنين ولو بماء الرأس، والدلك، والولاء، والنية ... كمسح الجبيرة والتيمم.

والاستنشاق لغة: النشق: جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إليه، واصطلاحاً: إيصال الماء إلى المارن، وهو ما لان من الأنف. أفاد أن الجذب بريح الأنف ليس شرطاً فيه شرعاً. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٦٩]

والمبالغة: قال الإمام خواهر زاده هي في المضمضة الغرغرة، وهي تردد الماء في الحلق، وفي الاستنشاق أن يجذب الماء بنفسه إلى ما اشتد أنفه. قال في "البحر": وهو الأولى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٠] وقيد بغير الصائم، فإن الصائم لا يبالغ في المضمضة ولا في الاستنشاق؛ خشية إفساد الصوم، ولو كان الصوم صوم نفل.

وتخليل اللحية: هو تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق، ويكون بعد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً بكف ماء. فقوله: "بكف" متعلق بـ"يكون" المقدر. (مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي)

وتخليل الأصابع: وكيفيته في اليدين: إدخال بعضها في بعض، وفي الرجلين: بإصبع من يده، ويكفي عنه إدخالها في الماء الجاري ونحوه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧١]

وتثليث الغسل: وفي "البحر": السنة تكرار الغسلات المستوعبات لا الغرفات، والمرة الأولى فرض، والثنتان بعدها سنتان مؤكدتان على الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧١] وقيد بالغسل؛ لأن المسح لا يسن تكراره عندنا. (مراقي الفلاح)

واستيعاب الرأس إلخ: وكيفيته: أن يضع من كل واحدة من اليدين ثلاث أصابع على مقدم رأسه، ولا يضع الإبهام والمسبحة، ويجافي كفيه ويمدهما إلى القفا، ثم يضع كفيه على مؤخر رأسه ويمدهما إلى المقدم، ثم يمسح ظاهر أذنيه بإبهاميه وباطنهما بمسبحتيه. كذا في "المستصفى" [العناية: ۲۹/۱]

ومسح الأذنين: بأن يمسح ظاهرهما بالإبهامين، وداخلهما بالسبابتين، وهو المختار كما في "المعراج"، ويدخل الخنصرين في جحريهما ويحركهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢]

والولاء: هو بكسر الواو: المتابعة بغسل الأعضاء قبل جفاف السابق مع الاعتدال جسدا وزمانا ومكانا. فلو كان بدنه يتشرب الماء، أو كان الهواء شديداً، أو كان المكان حاراً يجفف الماء سريعا، فلا يعد تاركا له. ولو كان طرياً لا يجففه إلا في مدة مستطيلة وتأنى في الوضوء لا يكون آتياً بسنة الولاء. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٧٢]

والنية: وهي لغة: عزم القلب على الفعل، واصطلاحاً: توجه القلب لإيجاد الفعل جزماً. ووقتها بعد الاستنجاء؛ فعله قربة. وكيفيتها: أن ينوي رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة، أو ينوي الوضوء أو امتثال الأمر. ومحلها القلب، فإن نطق بها ليجمع بين فعل القلب واللسان استحبه المشايخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٣]
The Book of Purification. The Sunnah acts of wudu: and rinsing the nose with three handfuls, and exaggerating in rinsing the mouth and nose for the non-fasting person, and combing the thick beard with a handful of water from below, and combing the fingers, and washing thrice, and covering the entire head with wiping once, and wiping the ears even with water of the head, and rubbing, and continuity, and intention... like wiping over the splint and tayammum. And rinsing the nose linguistically: it is sniffling: drawing water etc. by breath of the nose to it, and terminologically: conveying water to the soft part of the nose. It indicates that drawing by breath of the nose is not a condition for it legally. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 69] And exaggeration: Imam Khwahar Zadeh said it is in mouth rinsing gargling, which is moving water in the throat, and in nose rinsing that he draws water by himself to the furthest part of his nose. He said in 'al-Bahr': it is the more appropriate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 70] And it is restricted to non-fasting person, for the fasting person does not exaggerate in mouth rinsing nor in nose rinsing for fear of breaking the fast, even if the fast is a supererogatory fast. And combing the beard: it is separating the hair from the bottom upwards, and it is after washing the face three times with a handful of water. So his saying: 'with a handful' is related to the implied 'is'. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And combing the fingers: its manner in the hands: interlocking them into each other, and in the feet: with a finger of his hand, and it is sufficient instead to insert them into flowing water and the like. [Maraqi al-Falah: 71] And washing thrice: And in 'al-Bahr': the sunnah is repeating comprehensive washings, not handfuls, and the first time is obligatory, and the two after it are confirmed sunnahs according to the correct opinion. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 71] And it is restricted to washing because wiping is not recommended to be repeated according to us. (Maraqi al-Falah) And covering the head etc.: Its manner: he places from each of his two hands three fingers on the front of his head, and does not place the thumb and index finger, and he spreads his palms and extends them to the nape, then he places his palms on the back of his head and extends them to the front, then he wipes the outside of his ears with his thumbs and their inside with his index fingers. As in 'al-Mustasfa' [al-Inayah: 29/1] And wiping the ears: he wipes their outside with the two thumbs, and their inside with the two index fingers, and it is the chosen opinion as in 'al-Mi'raj', and he inserts the little fingers into the ear canals and moves them. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 72] And continuity: it is with a kasra on the waw: following up by washing the limbs before the previous one dries with moderation in body, time, and place. So if his body absorbs water, or the air is strong, or the place is hot that dries water quickly, he is not considered leaving it. And if it is moist that does not dry except in a very long period and he takes time in wudu, he is not performing the sunnah of continuity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 72] And intention: linguistically: determination of the heart for the action, and terminologically: direction of the heart to perform the action decisively. And its time is after istinja; its performance is a supererogatory act of worship. And its manner: he intends to remove hadath or to perform the prayer, or he intends wudu or to obey the command. And its place is the heart, and if he utters it to combine between the action of the heart and the tongue, the mashayikh considered it recommended. [Maraqi al-Falah: 73]
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the sunnah acts of wudu as per the Hanafi school. It begins by listing the primary sunnan: rinsing the nose with three handfuls, exaggerating in rinsing the mouth and nose for non-fasting persons, combing a thick beard from below with a handful of water, combing fingers, washing each limb thrice, covering the entire head with wiping once, wiping ears even with the water of the head, rubbing the limbs, maintaining continuity (wala'), and intention. Each of these acts is then defined and explained with Hanafi rulings. For example, istinshaq is defined as the sniffling of water in the nose, but the formal requirement (shar'an) is simply to reach water to the soft part of the nose, not necessarily by sniffling. Mubalaghah (exaggeration) in mouth rinsing means gargling, and in nose rinsing means drawing water deep into the nose; this is not recommended for the fasting person. The combing of the beard is done from below after washing the face three times. The combing of fingers is done by interlocking in the hands and using a finger for the feet. Washing thrice means the first wash is obligatory (fard), and the second and third are confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah); this applies only to washing, not wiping. Covering the head involves a specific method of wiping. Wiping the ears combines the outside with thumbs and inside with index fingers. Continuity (wala') means washing each limb before the previous one dries; if it would dry quickly, it is not a sin to take time, but if it would take a long time, deliberately delaying would contradict the sunnah. Intention (niyyah) is defined as the heart's determination and is performed after istinja; it can be expressed verbally for extra reward.

Key Terms
الاستنشاق (al-istinshāq): The sunnah act of rinsing the nose by drawing water to the soft part of the nose, though sniffling is not a legal condition.
المبالغة (al-mubālaghah): Exaggeration in rinsing the mouth (gargling) and nose (drawing water deep), recommended for non-fasting persons only.
الولاء (al-walā'): Continuity in wudu: washing each limb before the previous one dries, with moderation in body, time, and place.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention: the heart's determination to perform wudu for worship; its time is after istinja, and it is a sunnah act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on washing thrice in wudu?
A) All three washes are sunnah muakkadah.
B) The first wash is fard, the second and third are sunnah muakkadah.
C) Only the first wash is recommended.
D) Washing thrice is not part of the sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of wudu are confirmed but not required; they perfect the act of purification and are part of following the Prophet's practice.

The Hanafi Definitions of Adab and Sunnah in Wudu
Definitional passage clarifying adab vs sunnah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of adab and sunnah and distinguish between them based on the Prophet's persistence and the consequence of omission.

Core Idea
Adab is occasional practice with no blame for leaving; sunnah persists with reproach for leaving.

In the Hanafi school, not all recommended acts carry the same weight. This passage from Nur al-Idah provides clear definitions: adab is what the Prophet did once or twice without persistence, while sunnah is what he persisted in, leaving it only occasionally without excuse. Understanding this distinction is key to properly classifying the etiquettes of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definitions
Find the Arabic terms for adab and sunnah in the passage and read their descriptions.
The definitions appear after the list of fourteen etiquettes.
2
Identify the key difference
Note the operative distinction: adab involves occasional action with no blame for leaving; sunnah involves persistent action with reproach (not punishment) for leaving.
The text says: 'في تركها العتاب لا العقاب' for sunnah.
3
Apply to examples
The passage states 'the last four are mustahab (recommended)'. Connect this to the definition of adab.
4
Contrast with other schools
The Hanafi distinction is fine-tuned; other schools may not separate adab and sunnah as clearly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
آداب الوضوء
والترتيب كما نص الله تعالى في كتابه، والبداءة بالميامن ورؤوس الأصابع، ومقدم الرأس، ومسح الرقبة لا الحلقوم، ومسح العنق، وقيل: أصل مؤخره. وقيل إن الأربعة الأخيرة مستحبة.

فصل [ في آداب الوضوء ]
من آداب الوضوء أربعة عشر شيئا : الجلوس في مكان مرتفع، واستقبال القبلة، وعدم الاستعانة بغيره، وعدم التكلم بكلام الناس، والجمع بين نية القلب وفعل اللسان، والدعاء بالمأثور، والتسمية عند كل عضو.

[وشرح بعض الآداب: البداءة بالميامن: هي بتثليث الباء والمد والهمزة، وتبدل ياء. والميامن جمع ميمنة خلاف الميسرة في اليدين والرجلين، وهما عضوان مغسولان، فخرج العضو الواحد كالوجه، فلا يطلب فيه التيامن. والعضوان الممسوحان كالأذنين والخفين فالسنة مسحهما معاً.]

[وقيل: لا يسن مسح الحلقوم، بل هو بدعة.]

[وقيل: الأربعة الأخيرة مستحبة.]

[تعريف الأدب: عرّف بأنه وضع الأشياء موضعها، وقيل: الخصلة الحميدة، وقيل: الورع. وفي شرح ما فعله النبي مرة أو مرتين ولم يواظب عليه وحكمه الثواب بفعله، وعدم اللوم على تركه. وأما السنة: فهي التي واظب عليها النبي مع الترك بلا عذر مرة أو مرتين وحكمها الثواب وفي تركها العتاب لا العقاب.]

[ذكر أن العدد أربعة عشر ليس للحصر بل زيد عليها أشياء.]

[شرح بعض الآداب: الجلوس في مكان مرتفع حفظاً للثياب عن الماء المستعمل. عدم الاستعانة: قال الكرماني: لا كراهة في الصب، ولا يقال: خلاف الأولى، وساق عدة أحاديث دالة على أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فعله، وضعف ما يدل على الكراهة، وممن كان يستعين على وضوئه بغيره عثمان، وفعله ناس من كبار التابعين.]

[الدعاء بالمأثور: أي المنقول عن النبي والصحابة والتابعين.]

[عند كل عضو: أي الدعاء عند غسل كل عضو ومسحه وكذا التسمية. فيقول ناوياً: عند المضمضة: بسم الله، اللهم أعني على تلاوة القرآن وذكرك وشكرك وعبادتك، وحسن الاستنشاق: بسم الله، اللهم أرحني رائحة الجنة، ولا ترحني رائحة النار. وعند غسل الوجه: بسم الله، اللهم بيض وجهي يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه. وعند غسل اليمنى: بسم الله، اللهم أعطني كتابي بيميني وحاسبني حساباً يسيراً. وعند غسل اليسرى: بسم الله، اللهم لا تعطني كتابي بشمالي ولا من وراء ظهري. وعند مسح الرأس: بسم الله، اللهم أظلني تحت ظل عرشك يوم لا ظل إلا ظلك. وعند غسل الرجلين: بسم الله، اللهم ثبت قدمي على الصراط يوم تزل فيه الأقدام.]
The Book of Purification. Etiquette of wudu: and sequence as Allah the Exalted stated in His Book, and beginning with the right sides and tips of the fingers, and front of the head, and wiping the neck, not the throat, and wiping the back of the neck? It is said that the final four are recommended. Section [on the etiquette of wudu]. From the etiquette of wudu are fourteen things: sitting in an elevated place, facing the qibla, not seeking help from others, not speaking worldly speech, combining intention of the heart and action of the tongue, supplicating with transmitted invocations, and saying the basmalah at each limb. [Explanation of some etiquettes: beginning with the right sides: it is with the letter ba', alif mamduda, and hamza, and it can be changed to ya'. Al-mayamin is plural of maimana, opposite of maysara, in the hands and feet, and they are two limbs that are washed, so the single limb like the face is excluded, so starting with the right is not required for it. And the two limbs that are wiped like the ears and khuffs, the sunnah is to wipe them together.] [And it is said: wiping the throat is not sunnah, rather it is a bid'ah.] [And it is said: the last four are recommended.] [Definition of adab: it is defined as putting things in their places, and it is said: a praiseworthy characteristic, and it is said: piety. In explanation: what the Prophet ﷺ did once or twice and did not persist in, its ruling is reward for doing it, and no blame for leaving it. As for sunnah: it is what the Prophet ﷺ persisted in, with leaving it without excuse once or twice, its ruling is reward, and in leaving it there is reproach, not punishment.] [The number fourteen is not for exclusivity, rather additional things have been added.] [Explanation of some etiquettes: sitting in an elevated place to protect clothes from used water. Not seeking help: al-Kirmani said: there is no dislike in pouring, and it is not said that it is contrary to the better, and he cited several hadiths indicating that the Prophet ﷺ did it, and he weakened what indicates dislike, and among those who sought help for their wudu from others was 'Uthman, and it was done by many of the senior tabi'un.] [Supplication with the transmitted invocations: i.e., what is reported from the Prophet, the Companions, and the tabi'un.] [At each limb: i.e., supplication at washing and wiping each limb, and similarly the basmalah. So he says intending: at mouth rinse: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, help me to recite the Quran and remember You and thank You and worship You, and good rinsing of the nose: In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me the fragrance of Paradise and do not give me the smell of Hellfire.' At washing the face: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, whiten my face on the day faces become white and faces become black.' At washing the right [hand/foot]: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me my book in my right hand and make my reckoning easy.' At washing the left: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, do not give me my book in my left hand nor from behind my back.' At wiping the head: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me shade under Your Throne on the day when there is no shade but Your shade.' At washing the feet: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, make my feet firm on the Bridge on the day when feet slip.'
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage covers the etiquette (adab) of wudu. It first mentions general etiquettes like performing wudu in sequence (as in the Quran), starting with the right side, tips of fingers, and front of the head, and wiping the neck but not the throat. Then it lists fourteen specific adab: (1) sitting in a high place, (2) facing the qibla, (3) not seeking assistance from others, (4) not engaging in worldly talk, (5) combining heart intention with verbal utterance, (6) reciting the transmitted du'as, and (7) saying bismillah at each limb. The text then elaborates: the sequence of washing limbs is based on the Quranic order (2:239), and starting with the right side applies to two limbs (hands and feet); for the face and the head (single limbs) it is not required; for wiped parts (ears, khuffs), they should be wiped together. Wiping the throat is not sunnah but bid'ah. The final four (perhaps from the general list) are considered mustahab (recommended). The text also defines adab versus sunnah: adab is an action the Prophet did occasionally, with reward but no blame for leaving; sunnah is what he persisted in, with reward and reproach for leaving. The number fourteen is not exhaustive—many additional etiquettes exist. Specific adab: sitting in an elevated place protects clothes from used water. Regarding 'not seeking help', the Hanafi position is that there is no dislike in the assistant pouring water, supported by evidence that the Prophet himself was assisted and 'Uthman did so. The recommended du'as are then listed for each step: before each action, say bismillah, and specific supplications for the nose, face, right and left limbs, head, and feet.

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): A recommended practice that the Prophet did sometimes (once or twice) without persisting; reward for doing, no blame for leaving.
السنة (al-sunnah): A practice the Prophet persisted in, leaving only occasionally without excuse; reward for doing, reproach for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of leaving a sunnah according to the passage?
A) No blame at all
B) Reproach but not punishment
C) Punishment
D) The act becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes adab from sunnah by the Prophet's persistence and the consequence of omission.

Taharah — Purification

Rulings on Starting with the Right, Wiping the Neck, and Seeking Help in Wudu
Explanatory section on specific adab rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on starting with the right side, wiping the neck, and seeking help in wudu, and explain the position on the dispute regarding seeking help.

Core Idea
Starting with the right is sunnah for paired washed limbs, wiping neck is bid'ah, and seeking help is not disliked.

Among the fourteen etiquettes of wudu, three specific issues require careful attention: the rule of tayammun (beginning with the right) applies only to two-limb washed members; wiping the throat is considered an innovation; and seeking assistance is permissible without dislike. This lesson unpacks these rulings from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for starting with the right
The text explains that tayammun (beginning with the right) applies to the hands and feet (washed limbs), not to the face (single limb), and not to wiped limbs (ears, khuffs) which are wiped together.
2
Understand the ruling on wiping the neck
The text states explicitly: wiping the throat (al-halqum) is not sunnah, it is bid'ah.
3
Analyze the dispute on seeking help
The text presents a disagreement: some consider seeking help disliked, but al-Kirmani affirms it is not disliked, citing prophetic practice and weakening contrary narrations.
4
Summarize the practical implications
For each issue, state what a Hanafi should do: observe tayammun for hands/feet, avoid wiping throat, and feel free to ask for help as needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
آداب الوضوء
والترتيب كما نص الله تعالى في كتابه، والبداءة بالميامن ورؤوس الأصابع، ومقدم الرأس، ومسح الرقبة لا الحلقوم، ومسح العنق، وقيل: أصل مؤخره. وقيل إن الأربعة الأخيرة مستحبة.

فصل [ في آداب الوضوء ]
من آداب الوضوء أربعة عشر شيئا : الجلوس في مكان مرتفع، واستقبال القبلة، وعدم الاستعانة بغيره، وعدم التكلم بكلام الناس، والجمع بين نية القلب وفعل اللسان، والدعاء بالمأثور، والتسمية عند كل عضو.

[وشرح بعض الآداب: البداءة بالميامن: هي بتثليث الباء والمد والهمزة، وتبدل ياء. والميامن جمع ميمنة خلاف الميسرة في اليدين والرجلين، وهما عضوان مغسولان، فخرج العضو الواحد كالوجه، فلا يطلب فيه التيامن. والعضوان الممسوحان كالأذنين والخفين فالسنة مسحهما معاً.]

[وقيل: لا يسن مسح الحلقوم، بل هو بدعة.]

[وقيل: الأربعة الأخيرة مستحبة.]

[تعريف الأدب: عرّف بأنه وضع الأشياء موضعها، وقيل: الخصلة الحميدة، وقيل: الورع. وفي شرح ما فعله النبي مرة أو مرتين ولم يواظب عليه وحكمه الثواب بفعله، وعدم اللوم على تركه. وأما السنة: فهي التي واظب عليها النبي مع الترك بلا عذر مرة أو مرتين وحكمها الثواب وفي تركها العتاب لا العقاب.]

[ذكر أن العدد أربعة عشر ليس للحصر بل زيد عليها أشياء.]

[شرح بعض الآداب: الجلوس في مكان مرتفع حفظاً للثياب عن الماء المستعمل. عدم الاستعانة: قال الكرماني: لا كراهة في الصب، ولا يقال: خلاف الأولى، وساق عدة أحاديث دالة على أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فعله، وضعف ما يدل على الكراهة، وممن كان يستعين على وضوئه بغيره عثمان، وفعله ناس من كبار التابعين.]

[الدعاء بالمأثور: أي المنقول عن النبي والصحابة والتابعين.]

[عند كل عضو: أي الدعاء عند غسل كل عضو ومسحه وكذا التسمية. فيقول ناوياً: عند المضمضة: بسم الله، اللهم أعني على تلاوة القرآن وذكرك وشكرك وعبادتك، وحسن الاستنشاق: بسم الله، اللهم أرحني رائحة الجنة، ولا ترحني رائحة النار. وعند غسل الوجه: بسم الله، اللهم بيض وجهي يوم تبيض وجوه وتسود وجوه. وعند غسل اليمنى: بسم الله، اللهم أعطني كتابي بيميني وحاسبني حساباً يسيراً. وعند غسل اليسرى: بسم الله، اللهم لا تعطني كتابي بشمالي ولا من وراء ظهري. وعند مسح الرأس: بسم الله، اللهم أظلني تحت ظل عرشك يوم لا ظل إلا ظلك. وعند غسل الرجلين: بسم الله، اللهم ثبت قدمي على الصراط يوم تزل فيه الأقدام.]
The Book of Purification. Etiquette of wudu: and sequence as Allah the Exalted stated in His Book, and beginning with the right sides and tips of the fingers, and front of the head, and wiping the neck, not the throat, and wiping the back of the neck? It is said that the final four are recommended. Section [on the etiquette of wudu]. From the etiquette of wudu are fourteen things: sitting in an elevated place, facing the qibla, not seeking help from others, not speaking worldly speech, combining intention of the heart and action of the tongue, supplicating with transmitted invocations, and saying the basmalah at each limb. [Explanation of some etiquettes: beginning with the right sides: it is with the letter ba', alif mamduda, and hamza, and it can be changed to ya'. Al-mayamin is plural of maimana, opposite of maysara, in the hands and feet, and they are two limbs that are washed, so the single limb like the face is excluded, so starting with the right is not required for it. And the two limbs that are wiped like the ears and khuffs, the sunnah is to wipe them together.] [And it is said: wiping the throat is not sunnah, rather it is a bid'ah.] [And it is said: the last four are recommended.] [Definition of adab: it is defined as putting things in their places, and it is said: a praiseworthy characteristic, and it is said: piety. In explanation: what the Prophet ﷺ did once or twice and did not persist in, its ruling is reward for doing it, and no blame for leaving it. As for sunnah: it is what the Prophet ﷺ persisted in, with leaving it without excuse once or twice, its ruling is reward, and in leaving it there is reproach, not punishment.] [The number fourteen is not for exclusivity, rather additional things have been added.] [Explanation of some etiquettes: sitting in an elevated place to protect clothes from used water. Not seeking help: al-Kirmani said: there is no dislike in pouring, and it is not said that it is contrary to the better, and he cited several hadiths indicating that the Prophet ﷺ did it, and he weakened what indicates dislike, and among those who sought help for their wudu from others was 'Uthman, and it was done by many of the senior tabi'un.] [Supplication with the transmitted invocations: i.e., what is reported from the Prophet, the Companions, and the tabi'un.] [At each limb: i.e., supplication at washing and wiping each limb, and similarly the basmalah. So he says intending: at mouth rinse: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, help me to recite the Quran and remember You and thank You and worship You, and good rinsing of the nose: In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me the fragrance of Paradise and do not give me the smell of Hellfire.' At washing the face: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, whiten my face on the day faces become white and faces become black.' At washing the right [hand/foot]: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me my book in my right hand and make my reckoning easy.' At washing the left: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, do not give me my book in my left hand nor from behind my back.' At wiping the head: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, give me shade under Your Throne on the day when there is no shade but Your shade.' At washing the feet: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, make my feet firm on the Bridge on the day when feet slip.'
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage covers the etiquette (adab) of wudu. It first mentions general etiquettes like performing wudu in sequence (as in the Quran), starting with the right side, tips of fingers, and front of the head, and wiping the neck but not the throat. Then it lists fourteen specific adab: (1) sitting in a high place, (2) facing the qibla, (3) not seeking assistance from others, (4) not engaging in worldly talk, (5) combining heart intention with verbal utterance, (6) reciting the transmitted du'as, and (7) saying bismillah at each limb. The text then elaborates: the sequence of washing limbs is based on the Quranic order (2:239), and starting with the right side applies to two limbs (hands and feet); for the face and the head (single limbs) it is not required; for wiped parts (ears, khuffs), they should be wiped together. Wiping the throat is not sunnah but bid'ah. The final four (perhaps from the general list) are considered mustahab (recommended). The text also defines adab versus sunnah: adab is an action the Prophet did occasionally, with reward but no blame for leaving; sunnah is what he persisted in, with reward and reproach for leaving. The number fourteen is not exhaustive—many additional etiquettes exist. Specific adab: sitting in an elevated place protects clothes from used water. Regarding 'not seeking help', the Hanafi position is that there is no dislike in the assistant pouring water, supported by evidence that the Prophet himself was assisted and 'Uthman did so. The recommended du'as are then listed for each step: before each action, say bismillah, and specific supplications for the nose, face, right and left limbs, head, and feet.

Key Terms
الميامن (al-mayāmin): The right sides; in wudu, starting with the right hand and foot when washing.
الحلقوم (al-ḥalqūm): The throat (specifically the front part); wiping it is bid'ah in wudu.
الاستعانة (al-isti‘ānah): Seeking help from others, e.g., having someone pour water during wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wiping the throat (al-halqum) during wudu?
A) It is sunnah muakkadah.
B) It is mustahab (recommended).
C) It is not sunnah; it is bid'ah (innovation).
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wudu: start with the right for hands/feet, avoid wiping the throat, and feel free to ask for help.

Taharah — Purification

The 14 Adab (Etiquettes) of Wudu
Lists 14 recommended acts with commentary on adab vs sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 14 adab of wudu and explain the Hanafi distinction between adab and sunnah.

Core Idea
Adab in wudu: reward if done, no blame if left — a distinct Hanafi category below sunnah.

Wudu is not only about its obligatory parts; there are recommended etiquettes (adab) that enhance its completeness and reward. This passage from Nur al-Idah lists 14 such etiquettes, carefully distinguishing them from sunnah acts. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion: omitting an adab does not affect validity, but performing it brings extra reward.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the list of 14 adab
Read the Arabic passage and identify the 14 items: sitting in a high place, facing qibla, not seeking help (except for istinja), not speaking worldly talk, combining intention with utterance, supplicating, saying Bismillah at each limb, etc.
The number is not restrictive; more can be added.
2
Distinguish adab from sunnah
Note the Hanafi definition: adab is what the Prophet did once or twice without regularity; sunnah is what he did regularly. Omission of adab incurs no blame, omission of sunnah is blameworthy.
Other schools may classify some of these as sunnah.
3
Analyze specific etiquettes
Focus on details: beginning with the right applies to paired limbs (hands, feet) but not to the face; wiping the neck is not sunnah but bid'ah if done as such. The supplications are transmitted and recommended.
The commentary clarifies which parts are agreed upon.
4
Apply the ma'dhur exception
The text mentions that a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) should, if performing wudu before the time, repeat it within the time to avoid intra-Hanafi dispute.
This shows that adab can incorporate precautionary measures.

[مراقي الفلاح: ٧٧] اللهم إلخ زاد في 'فتح القدير' سبحانك الله وبحمدك أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، اللهم اجعلني إلخ. التوابين: أي الراجعين عن كل ذنب. (مراقي الفلاح)
Etiquettes of wudu: Order as Allah stated in His Book, beginning with the right side, tips of fingers, front of head, and wiping the neck – not the throat – and it is said that the last four are recommended. The neck, and it is said: its base from behind. Section [On the Etiquettes of Wudu]: Among the etiquettes of wudu are fourteen things: sitting in a high place, facing the qibla, not seeking help from others except in the case of istinja, not speaking about worldly matters, combining intention of the heart with utterance of the tongue, supplicating with transmitted supplications, and saying Bismillah at each limb...
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement enumerating the recommended etiquettes (adab) of wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author lists fourteen specific acts that are mustahabb (recommended) but not obligatory. The commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies that 'adab' here means an action the Prophet performed once or twice without regular practice; its reward is for doing it, and there is no blame for leaving it. This distinguishes it from sunnah, which is regularly practiced. The text also discusses details: e.g., beginning with the right side applies to the two limbs (hands and feet) but not the face; wiping the neck is not sunnah but a bid'ah if done as such. The supplications for each limb are given, though these are from later sources. The number fourteen is not restrictive; more can be added. Asking for help during wudu is not disliked, as proven by actions of the Prophet and companions. The commentary also addresses the issue of a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) performing wudu before the time, noting intra-Hanafi differences: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if there is an intervening time, it is valid; according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, it is not, so repetition is recommended to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
أدب (adab): In this text, adab refers to an action performed by the Prophet once or twice without regular practice; its performance brings reward, and omission incurs no blame.
سنة (sunnah): An action regularly practiced by the Prophet; omission is blameworthy but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on wiping the neck (masah al-raqaba) during wudu?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
C) It is not sunnah but rather bid'ah if done as sunnah.
D) It is mustahabb (recommended).

Key Takeaway
The 14 adab of wudu are recommended acts whose omission does not harm validity but whose performance brings reward.

Disliked Acts of Wudu (Makruhat al-Wudu)
Lists disliked acts of wudu with definition of makruh types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the disliked acts of wudu and distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, 'makruh' usually means tahrimi (omission is wajib); tanzihi is less severe.

This passage lists actions that are considered disliked (makruh) during wudu. While the matn simply states them, the commentary reveals an important Hanafi distinction: makruh is of two levels. Understanding this helps you avoid practices that reduce the perfection of wudu or incur sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed acts
Read the Arabic list carefully. Note each action: inserting pinky in ears, moving a loose ring, rinsing with the right hand, sniffing with right, blowing nose with left, wudu before time for non-excused, reciting shahadah after, drinking leftover water standing, and saying specific duas.
Some acts are localized to parts of wudu (e.g., ear wiping, hand washing).
2
Understand the two types of makruh
The commentary explains that 'makruh' in Hanafi texts usually refers to makruh tahrimi—an act whose avoidance is obligatory. The other type, makruh tanzihi, is merely recommended to avoid. Note that the passage does not specify which type applies to each act, but the jurists generally consider most of these tanzihi.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; tanzihi is close to mubah.
3
Apply the definition to your practice
When you encounter a ruling labeled 'makruh' in a Hanafi text, consider whether it might be tahrimi or tanzihi based on context and evidence. For these wudu acts, avoid them to gain the full reward.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
۲۸
مكروهات الوضوء
وإدخال خنصره في صماخ أذنيه، وتحريك خاتمه الواسع، والمضمضة، والاستنشاق بالكسر الثقب باليد اليمنى، والامتخاط باليسرى والتوضؤ قبل دخول الوقت لغير المعذور، إخراج ما في الأنف والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده ، وأن يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائماً، وأن يقول: اللهم الوضوء اجعلني من التوابين واجعلني من المتطهرين.
ويكره للمتوضئ .
عنقه
متنزهين عن الفواحش
فصل [ في مكروهات الوضوء]

قائما مستقبلا
- لا ظل إلا ظل عرشك، وعند مسح أذنيه : الله، اللهم اجعلني من الذين يستمعون القول فيتبعون أحسنه، الله، اللهم أعتق رقبتي من النار، وعند غسل رجله اليمنى: بسم الله، اللهم ثبت قدمي على الصراط يوم تزل الأقدام، وعند غسل اليسرى: بسم الله، اللهم اجعل ذنبي مغفوراً، وسعيي مشكوراً، وتجارتي لن تبور مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٦]
خنصره أي أنملة خنصره، وهو بكسر الخاء والصاد، قال الفارسي: الفصيح فتح الصاد، قال في 'المحيط': يدخل خنصره في صماخ أذنيه ويحركها [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٦ الواسع قيد به ؛ فإن الضيق إن علم وصول الماء تحته استحب تحريكه و إلا افترض لغير المعذور: قيد به؛ فإن وضوء المعذور ينتقض بخروج الوقت عندنا، وبدخوله عند زفر ، وبهما عند أبي يوسف ، فإذا توضأ في زمن قبل الوقت فلا يخلو إما أن يكون بين الوقتين وقت مهمل أو لا، فإن كان بينهما وقت مهمل وتوضأ فيه للوقت الثاني جاز ذلك عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف وزفرجا: لا يجوز، فتندب له إعادة الوضوء في الوقت خروجاً عن الخلاف، وإن لم يكن بينهما وقت مهمل وتوضأ في آخر الوقت للوقت الثاني لا يجوز إجماعاً، فتجب إعادة الوضوء، وحينئذ فلا فائدة في وضوئه قبل الوقت قال السيد وهذه إحدى المسائل الثلاث التي النفل فيها أفضل من الفرض، الثانية: إبراء المعسر أفضل من إنظاره، الثالثة: البدء بالسلام أفضل من رده مراقي الفلاح حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٧] يشرب قالوا ويقول عند شربه اللهم اشفني بشفائك وداوني بدوائك، واعصمني من الوهن والأمراض والأوجاع [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۷] قائماً مستقبل القبلة، أو قاعداً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٧٧] اللهم إلخ زاد في 'فتح القدير' سبحانك الله وبحمدك أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، اللهم اجعلني إلخ. التوابين: أي الراجعين عن كل ذنب. (مراقي الفلاح)
ويكره المكروه عند الفقهاء نوعان مكروه تحريما وهو المحمل عند إطلاقهم الكراهة وهو ما تركه واجب =
Book of Purification. Disliked acts of wudu: Inserting the pinky into the ear holes, moving a loose ring, rinsing the mouth, sniffing water, blowing the nose, performing wudu before the time for one without excuse, and reciting the two testimonies after it, and drinking leftover water standing, and saying: O Allah, make me among the oft-repenting and among the purified. It is disliked for the one performing wudu... (then commentary) ... Disliked (makruh) according to the jurists is of two types: makruh tahrimi, which is what is meant by their unrestricted use of the word, and it is that whose abandonment is obligatory.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage lists the disliked acts (makruhat) of wudu. The matn mentions: inserting the little finger into the ear canal during ear wiping, moving a loose ring (if water can reach under it, it is recommended to move it; otherwise it is obligatory), blowing the nose vigorously, performing wudu before the proper time for one without a chronic excuse, and reciting the two testimonies after wudu while standing. The commentary clarifies the types of makruh: makruh tahrimi (prohibited-adjacent) is what is usually meant by 'makruh' and its abandonment is wajib; makruh tanzihi is less severe. The text also revisits the issue of wudu before time for the ma'dhur, already discussed in adab. The definition of makruh at the end is cut off but establishes the distinction.

Key Terms
مكروه تحريمي (makruh tahrimi): An act whose omission is obligatory (wajib); it is close to haram and is what is meant by the unrestricted use of 'makruh' by Hanafi jurists.
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): An act whose avoidance is recommended but not obligatory; it is less severe than makruh tahrimi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary in this passage, what does 'makruh' mean when used unrestrictedly by Hanafi jurists?
A) Makruh tanzihi, which is better to avoid.
B) Makruh tahrimi, whose abandonment is obligatory.
C) Haram, which is sinful.
D) Mubah, which is permissible.

Key Takeaway
The 'makruh' in wudu acts are not all equal; the Hanafi school defines two levels, and the unqualified term refers to the more severe tahrimi.

Six Disliked Actions (Attributes) of Wudu
Six disliked actions in wudu with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six disliked actions (attributes) of wudu and explain the ruling of each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The six attributes of wudu are etiquettes; omitting them does not invalidate wudu, but extremes of extravagance or stinginess can be sinful.

This lesson explores the six 'attributes' (awṣāf) of wudu mentioned in classical Hanafi texts. These are not pillars (arkān) but recommended or disliked practices. Understanding them helps perfect one's wudu and avoid actions that reduce its reward or, in some cases, become sinful.

Guided Path
1
List the Six Attributes
Mentally recall or write down the six attributes: extravagance, stinting, striking the face, speaking, seeking help, and wiping three times with new water.
The text says the number is not exclusive but approximate for beginners.
2
Identify the Ruling for Each
For each attribute, determine the hukm (ruling). Most are makruh tanzihi, but stinginess that prevents dripping invalidates wudu, and extravagance with waqf water is haram.
Refer to the commentary for exceptions.
3
Distinguish Levels of Dislike
Understand that makruh tanzihi (disliked) is less severe than makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Extravagance from waqf water becomes haram.
The water source affects the ruling.
4
Apply the Principle of Moderation
The core theme is balance: use water in the sunnah amount, avoid both excess and deficiency.
Moderation is a key fiqh principle.
5
Recognize the Significance of Waqf
Understand that using waqf water beyond necessity is a violation of trust and becomes haram, even if the act itself is normally makruh.
This distinguishes between personal and public property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوصاف الوضوء ستة أشياء: الإسراف في الماء، والتقتير فيه وضرب الوجه به والتكلم بكلام الناس، والاستعانة بغيره من غير عذر، وتثليث المسح بماء جديد. ليس للحصر بل للتقريب للمبتدي. الإسراف : هو العمل فوق الحاجة الشرعية، في "فتاوى الحجة": يكره صب الماء في الوضوء زيادة على العدد المسنون والقدر المعهود، وفي "الدر": ويكره الإسراف فيه تحريماً لو بماء النهر أو المملوك له، أما الموقوف على من يتطهر به ومنه ماء المدارس - فحرام. والتقتير : أي بجعل الغسل مثل المسح فيه بأن يقرب الغسل إلى حد الدهن لكن لابد من أن يقطر ولو قطرتين حتى يكون غسلا، وإلا فلا يصح الوضوء أصلاً، والتقتير : هو عدم بلوغ الحد المسنون، فلو اقتصر على ما دون الثلاث قيل: يأثم، وقيل: لا، وقيل: يأثم بالاعتياد. ضرب ويرسل الماء على الوجه من أعلى الجبهة برفق، ثم يدلكه به. الوجه ومثله غيره من بقية الأعضاء. بكلام الناس: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن له حاجة تفوته بتركه، فإن كانت له حاجة وتفوته بترك التكلم في الوضوء فلا. ثلاثة: العدد لا يفيد الحصر، فلا ينافي أنه قد يكون مكروهاً، كالوضوء على الوضوء قبل تبدل المجلس الأول، أداؤه عبادة لا تصح بدونه به، وقد يكون حراما كما إذا كان من ماء الوقف والمدارس.
The attributes of wudu are six things: extravagance in water, stinting in it, striking the face with it, speaking with people's talk, seeking help from others without excuse, and wiping three times with new water. (Commentary:) Not for exclusivity but for approximation for the beginner. Extravagance: is doing above the legal need. In Fatawa al-Hujja: It is disliked to pour water in wudu in excess of the sunnah number and customary amount. In al-Durr: And it is disliked to be extravagant in it prohibitively if with river water or owned water, but if it is waqf water for those who use it for purification, like water of schools, then it is haram. Stinting: meaning making the washing like wiping, by bringing washing close to the limit of oiling, but it must drip even two drops so that it is washing, otherwise wudu is not valid at all. Stinting is not reaching the sunnah limit; if one suffices with less than three, it is said he sins, and it is said not, and it is said he sins by habit. Striking: he sends water onto the face from the top of the forehead gently, then rubs with it. The face and similarly the other limbs. Speaking with people's talk: it is unrestricted but restricted to when he has no need that escapes him by leaving it; if he has a need and it escapes him by leaving speaking in wudu then no. Three: the number does not indicate exclusivity, so it does not negate that it may be disliked, like wudu after wudu before the first gathering changes, performing it is worship but it is not valid without it, and it may be haram if from waqf or school water.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage introduces the six 'attributes' (awṣāf) of wudu—these are not pillars but rather recommended or disliked practices. The commentator clarifies that the number six is not restrictive but approximate for beginners. The first attribute, isrāf (extravagance), is using more water than necessary; depending on the water source it may be disliked (makruh tanzihi or tahrimi) or even haram if from waqf. The second, taqtīr (stinting), means using so little water that the limbs are not properly washed; it invalidates wudu if no dripping occurs. The third, striking the face, is the method of applying water gently. The fourth, speaking with people, is disliked unless one has a necessary need that would be missed. The fifth, seeking help without excuse, is also disliked. The sixth, wiping three times with new water, is discussed: the number three does not mean it is obligatory; excessive repetition may be disliked or even haram depending on the water source. The overall ruling is that these actions are makruh tanzihi (disliked) unless specified otherwise, and the student should understand that they do not invalidate wudu but reduce its perfection.

Key Terms
الإسراف (al-isrāf): Using water beyond the legally prescribed amount or customary measure in wudu.
التقتير (al-taqtīr): Using so little water that washing does not reach the sunnah limit; if no dripping occurs, wudu is invalid.
تثليث المسح (tathlīth al-masḥ): Wiping (or washing) a limb three times with new water each time; here it is not obligatory but a sunnah act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone uses water from a school waqf to wash more than three times in wudu?
A) It is makruh tanzihi.
B) It is haram.
C) It is permissible.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
The six attributes of wudu teach moderation; extravagance and stinginess are disliked, and using waqf water excessively is haram.

Three Categories of Wudu: Fard, Wajib, Mandub
Classifies wudu into three legal categories with associated rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three legal categories of wudu (fard, wajib, mandub) and state the ruling for each specific act (prayer, tawaf, sleep, touching Quran).

Core Idea
Wudu's obligation varies: fard for prayer, wajib for tawaf, mandub for sleep — each with distinct consequences.

This passage from Nur al-Idah classifies wudu into three levels: fard, wajib, and mandub. Each level triggers a different legal consequence — from invalidity of prayer without wudu to recommended reward for sleeping in a state of purity. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying wudu rulings in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
From the text, list each act for which wudu is mentioned: prayer, touching Quran, tawaf, sleep. Determine the hukm level (fard, wajib, mandub) for each.
Prayer and touching Quran are fard; tawaf is wajib; sleep is mandub.
2
Analyze the evidence level
Note that in the Hanafi school, fard is from qat'i evidence, wajib from zanni. The text explicitly states that fard is 'proven by definitive proof'.
This distinction is unique to Hanafis; other schools use fard/wajib interchangeably.
3
Determine the consequence of omission
For fard: omission invalidates the act and incurs sin. For wajib: the act is still valid but requires a dam (compensation). For mandub: no sin or compensation, only missed reward.
Example: skipping wudu for prayer makes it invalid; skipping for tawaf requires a sacrifice.
4
Understand the Hanafi definition of fard
The passage distinguishes between the overall fard of wudu and the ijtihad fard (e.g., washing a quarter of the head). This shows the layered nature of obligation.
Ijtihad fard is an obligation derived from speculative evidence but treated as fard in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [في أوصاف الوضوء] الوضوء على ثلاثة أقسام: الأول : فرض على المحدث للصلاة ولو كانت نفلاً، أي القسم الأول إذا أراد الشروع وصلي ة ولصلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة، والمس القرآن ولو آية. والثاني: واجب للطواف بالكعبة. والثالث : مندوب للنوم على طهارة، وإذا استيقظ منه، أي القسم الثالث أي القسم الثاني فيجب الدم بتركه ويثبت بما يثبت به الواجب كما في "الفتح"، ومكروه تنزيهاً وهو ما تركه أولى من فعله، وكثيراً ما يطلقوته، فلابد من النظر في الدليل، فإن كان نهياً ظنّيّاً يحكم بكراهة التحريم ما لم يوجد صارف عنه إلى التنزيه، وإن لم يكن الدليل نهياً، بل كان مفيداً للترك الغير الجازم، فهي تنزيهية، قاله صاحب "البحر". فرض : المراد بالفرض هنا الثابت بالقطعي، فالمراد الوضوء من حيث هو بقطع النظر عن أجزائه، وأما المحدود والمقدار، فهو ما يفوت الجواز بفوته ليشمل الفرض الاجتهادي كربع الرأس. ولو آية مكتوبة على درهم أو حائط مراقي الفلاح على طهارة ظاهره أنه لا يأتي بذلك المندوب، إلا إذا أخذه النوم وهو متطهر ، فلو تطهر ثم اضطجع وأحدث فنام لا يكون آتيا به
Section on the attributes of wudu. Wudu is of three types: First: fard upon the one in minor impurity for prayer, even if it is nafl, meaning for the first section when he intends to begin prayer, and for funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation, and touching the Quran even one verse. Second: wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba. Third: mandub for sleeping in a state of purity, and when he wakes from it, meaning the third section, meaning the second section, so a sacrifice (dam) is due by leaving it, and it is established by what establishes the wajib as in al-Fath, and it is makruh tanzihi, which is leaving it is better than doing it, and they often apply it, so one must look at the evidence, if it is a speculative prohibition it is ruled makruh tahrimi unless a reason diverts it to tanzih, and if the evidence is not a prohibition but indicates non-emphatic leaving, then it is tanzihi, said by the author of al-Bahr. Fard: what is intended by fard here is that established by definitive proof, so the intent is wudu in itself regardless of its parts, and as for the limited and measured, it is what if omitted causes invalidity, including ijtihad fard like a quarter of the head. And even one verse written on a dirham or wall, Maraqi al-Falah: on purity, apparently he does not perform that mandub unless sleep overtakes him while he is purified, so if he performs wudu then lies down and breaks wudu and then sleeps, he is not performing it.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage categorizes wudu into three levels of obligation. First: fard (obligatory) for prayer, including nafl, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, and touching the Quran. The commentator notes that 'fard' here means established by definitive evidence (qat'i). Second: wajib (necessary but less than fard) for tawaf; leaving it requires a sacrifice (dam) as compensation, similar to other wajib acts. Third: mandub (recommended) for sleeping in a state of purity, for maintaining that state upon waking, and for other acts like wudu after wudu, after backbiting, etc. The commentator clarifies that 'makruh tanzihi' is when leaving is better than doing, and distinguishes it from makruh tahrimi based on the strength of the evidence. The discussion on 'fard' distinguishes between the overall obligation of wudu and its parts (like washing a quarter of the head as ijtihad fard). The example of touching a verse on a dirham shows that the mandub wudu for sleep is only when one is already in the state of purity; otherwise, it is not considered.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligation established by definitive (qat'i) evidence; omission incurs sin and invalidates the act without it.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by speculative (zanni) evidence; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act that is not obligatory; doing it is rewarded, leaving it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone performs tawaf without wudu?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The tawaf is valid but a sacrifice (dam) is required.
C) The tawaf is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The tawaf is valid but sinful.

Key Takeaway
Wudu is not always fard; its obligation depends on the intended act: fard for prayer and Quran touching, wajib for tawaf, mandub for sleep and other purifying acts.

Recommended Acts of Wudu (Mustahabbat al-Wudu)
Lists recommended occasions for wudu with conditions for repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended occasions for performing wudu and explain the condition under which repeating wudu (wudu upon wudu) is recommended.

Core Idea
Wudu is recommended for many acts, but repeating it without cause is wasteful.

This lesson covers the occasions when performing wudu is recommended (mustahabb) even if one is already in a state of wudu. These include after committing sins, before sleep, before prayer times, and many others. The source explains that repeating wudu is only recommended if the first wudu has been followed by a worship act or the gathering has changed; otherwise it is considered wasteful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of recommended occasions
Scan the passage and note all situations where wudu is recommended. Make a mental list.
The list includes after sins, for prayer times, before ghusl, for the junub, etc.
2
Understand the ruling on wudu upon wudu
The passage states that wudu after wudu is recommended under specific conditions: if one has changed his gathering or performed a worship act with the first wudu. Otherwise, it is considered wasteful (israf).
This is a key condition that distinguishes Hanafi fiqh.
3
Distinguish between recommended and wasteful
Recognize that repeating wudu without the conditions is not just not recommended; it is considered israf, which is discouraged.
Israf is close to haram but not exactly; it is makruh tahrimi according to some.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., someone performs wudu for Fajr, remains in the same place, then wants to recite Quran), determine if wudu upon wudu is recommended or wasteful.
Apply the two conditions: change of gathering or worship act.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة نواقض الوضوء وللمداومة عليه، وللوضوء على الوضوء، وبعد غيبة وكذب ونميمة وكل خطيئة، كالشتيمة والنفاق وإنشاد شعر، وقهقهة خارج الصلاة وغسل ميت ،وحمله ولوقت كل صلاة، وقبل غسل الجنابة، وللجنب عند أكل وشرب ونوم ووطء والغضب وقرآن، وحديث وروايته، إرادة لقراءته ودراسة علم، وأذان، وإقامة، وخطبة، وزيارة النبي ، ووقوف بعرفة، وللسعي بين الصفا والمروة، وأكل لحم جزور ، وللخروج من خلاف العلماء، كما إذا مس امرأة. ثم قال: فصل في نواقض الوضوء] ينقض الوضوء اثنا عشر شيئا من الخرج وإن أقل مس أو فرجه امرأة. وللمداومة: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا تبدل مجلسه أو أدّى بالأول عبادة مقصودة من مشروعية الوضوء، وأما إذا لم يوجد أحد منهما فالوضوء على الوضوء إسراف وقيد بالوضوء؛ لأن الغسل على الغسل والتيمم على التيمم يكون عبثاً [مراقي الفلاح و حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸۳] وبعد غيبة: الغيبة: أن تذكر أخاك بما يكره، ولا تسمى غيبة إلا إذا كان صادقاً فيها وأما إذا كانت كذباً فبهتان، قال الخازن: وهو أشد من الغيبة، وكما تكون بالقول تكون بغيره من كل ما يفهم منه المقصود، وكما يحرم ذكرها باللسان يحرم اعتقادها بالقلب واستماعها. مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ۸۳] وكذب هو اختلاق ما لم يكن. (مراقي الفلاح) ونميمة: أي السعاية بنقل الحديث من قوم إلى قوم على جهة الإفساد [مراقي الفلاح: ٨٤] عند أكل إلخ: اعلم أن وضوء الجنب وضوءان أحدهما الوضوء بين الجماعين وعند النوم، وثانيهما: الوضوء عند إرادة أكل وشرب، فأما الأول فالمراد به الشرعي في قول أبي حنيفة ومالك والشافعي وأحمد والجمهور، وأما الثاني فالمراد به اللغوي، والبسط في حاشية الطحطاوي. واعلم أيضاً أن الأكل والشرب بدون ما ذكر سبب للفقر، قاله ابن أمير حاج. وللخروج إلخ أي الوضوء مندوب؛ ليخرج به من الخلاف بين العلماء، ويفتوا متفقين بجواز صلاته وغيرها من التي شرط لها الوضوء، كما إذا مس المرأة الأجنبية بعد ما توضأ وصلى من . أن يتوضأ بعد المس، فصلاته وإن كانت غير صحيحةً عندنا لكن عند بعضهم لا تصح فيستحب له الوضوء، لتكون صلاته صحيحة بالاتفاق. امرأة أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا كانت المرأة مشتهاة غير محرمة، فإن مس المحرمة أو غير المشتهاة لا ينقض الوضوء اتفاقاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸٥] ينقض: اعلم أن النقض إذا أضيف إلى الأجسام كنقض الحائط يراد به إبطال تأليفها، وإذا أضيف إلى المعاني كالوضوء يراد به إخراجها عن إقامة المطلوب بها والمطلوب من الوضوء استباحة الصلاة ونحوها مراقي الفلاح و حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٦] من السبيلين إلا ريح القبل في الأصح وينقضه ولادة من غير رؤية دم، ونجاسة سائلة من ذكر وفرج غيرهما كدم وقيح، وقيء طعام أو ماء أو علق أو مرة إذا ملأ الفم، وهو ما لا ينطبق عليه الفم إلا بتكلف على الأصح، ويجمع متفرق القيء إذا اتحد سببه، ودم غلب على البزاق، أو ساواه، ونوم ماض من المساواة. من السبيلين: سمي الأنف. القبل والدبر سبيلا؛ لكونه طريقا للخارج، وسواء المعتاد وغيره كالدودة والحصاة. مراقي الفلاح : ٨٦] إلا ريح القبل: أي الريح الخارج من قبل المرأة وذكر الرجل لا ينقض الوضوء؛ لأنه اختلاج وليس بريح، وعن محمد أنه حدث من قبلها قياساً على الدبر. [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٦/١] الأصح وفي رواية عن محمد الله: أنه لا ينقض. سائلة: اعلم أن السيلان في غير السبيلين بتجاوز النجاسة إلى محل يطلب تطهيره ولو ندباً، فلا ينقض دم سال في داخل العين إلى جانب آخر منها، بخلاف ما صلب من ا مراقي الفلاح: ۸۷] وقيء إلخ : أطلقه فشمل جميع أنواع القيء، سواء قاء من ساعته أم لا. [مراقي الفلاح: ٨٧] إذا ملأ الفم: أي انتقاض الوضوء بأحد هذه الأشياء بشرط كونه ملء الفم. لا ينطبق من الانطباق: انضمام بعضه إلى بعض الأصح يعني ما ذكر من تفسير ملء الفم هو الأصح من التفاسير فيه، وقيل: حده ما يمنع الكلام ويجمع أي إن قاء متفرقاً بحيث لو جمع ملأ الفم، فالمعتبر اتحاد السبب وهو الغثيان وتفسيره : إذا قاء ثانياً قبل سكون النفس من الغثيان فهو متحد، وإن قاء ثانياً بعد سكون النفس فهو مختلف، وهذا هو عند محمد، والمعتبر عند أبي يوسف له اتحاد المجلس. وقال في "مراقي الفلاح" : وقول محمد هو الأصح، وقال أبو علي الدقاق: يجمع كيفما كان مراقي الفلاح: ۸۹] ودم: اعلم أن الدم إذا نزل من الأنف انتقض وضوؤه إذا وصل إلى ما لان منه؛ لأنه يجب تطهيره، وإن خرج من نفس الفم تعتبر الغلبة بينه وبين الريق وإن تساويا انتقض الوضوء؛ لأن البصاق سائل بقوة نفسه، فكذا مساويه، بخلاف المغلوب؛ لأنه سائل بقوة الغالب، ويعتبر ذلك من حيث اللون، فإن كان أحمر انتقض، وإن كان أصفر لا ينتقض، وذكر الإمام علاء الدين أن من أكل خبزاً ورأى أثر الدم فيه من أصول أسنانه، أن ينبغي إصبعه أو طرف كمه على ذلك الموضع، فإن وجد فيه أثر الدم انتقض وضوؤه وإلا فلا. تبيين الحقائق: ٤٨/١] ونوم: اعلم أن النائم لا يخلو : إما أن يكون مضطجعاً فينتقض وضوؤه أو متوركاً، وهو ملحق به؛ لزوال المقعدة من الأرض، أو مستنداً إلى شيء لو أزيل عنه لسقط، فهذا لا يخلو إما أن تكون مقعدته زائلة عن الأرض أو لا، فإن كانت زائلة نقض بالإجماع، وإن كانت غير زائلة فقد ذكر القدوري أنه ينتقض وهو مروي عن الطحاوي، والصحيح أنه لا ينتقض أو يكون قائماً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً، فإنه إن كان في الصلاة لا ينتقض وضوؤه؛ لقوله ل: "لا" وضوء على من نام قائما أو راكعا أو ساجدا، وإن كان خارج الصلاة فكذلك في الصحيح إن كان يضع
Book of Purification. Nullifiers of Wudu. And for continuity on wudu, and wudu on wudu, and after backbiting, lying, slander, and every sin, like insult, hypocrisy, reciting poetry, laughter outside prayer, washing a dead person, carrying him, and for the time of every prayer, and before washing from janabah, and for the junub when eating, drinking, sleeping, intercourse, anger, Quran, hadith and its narration, intention to read it, study of knowledge, adhan, iqamah, sermon, visiting the Prophet, standing at Arafah, for sa'i between Safa and Marwa, eating camel meat, and to exit from disagreement of scholars, like if he touches a woman. Then he said: Section on nullifiers of wudu: Wudu is nullified by twelve things: whatever exits from the two passages even if little, touching a woman or his own private part. ... [continued with extensive commentary]
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, covers two main topics: recommended occasions for wudu (mustahabbat al-wudu) and the nullifiers of wudu (nawaqid al-wudu). The first part lists situations where performing wudu is recommended, such as after sins, before sleep, for eating, etc. The commentary explains that wudu after wudu is only recommended if one has changed one's gathering or performed an act of worship, otherwise it is wasteful. The second part, beginning with 'Fasl fi Nawaqid al-Wudu', lists the twelve nullifiers. The commentary elaborates on each: (1) anything exiting from the two passages (front and back) except wind from the front (prepuce) according to the soundest view, though Imam Muhammad analogically considers it a nullifier; (2) childbirth without blood; (3) flowing impurity from elsewhere; (4) vomiting of food, water, blood, or bile filling the mouth; (5) blood from nose or mouth that equals or exceeds saliva; (6) sleep that is deep (lying down, leaning, etc.) and in certain postures; and others. The commentary details conditions: for vomiting, it must fill the mouth and multiple vomits are combined if from one cause (nausea without pause). For sleep, it nullifies if one is lying, leaning without support, or sitting without the buttocks firmly on the ground. The Hanafi view is presented with intra-madhhab disputes, particularly regarding wind from the front and the combination of vomit. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions are noted: wind from the front does not nullify, and multiple vomits are combined if the nausea persists.

Key Terms
نقض (naqd): In physical objects, it means destruction of structure; in legal terms, it means rendering wudu invalid such that it no longer permits prayer.
حدث (hadath): Legal impurity that prevents worship; nullifiers produce hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it recommended to perform wudu upon wudu (renew wudu)?
A) Whenever one feels like it.
B) Only if one has changed his gathering or performed a worship act with the first wudu.
C) Only after committing a major sin.
D) Only before sleeping.

Key Takeaway
Wudu is recommended on many occasions, but redoing wudu without a change of state or worship is wasteful.

Module 3 · Lesson 59

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
15 min
Nullifiers of Wudu (Nawaqid al-Wudu)
Lists twelve nullifiers with detailed conditions and intra-Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve nullifiers of wudu according to the Hanafi school, explain the conditions for each, and resolve intra-Hanafi disputes such as wind from the front.

Core Idea
Wind from the front does not nullify wudu; the soundest view rejects qiyas with the back passage.

This lesson details the twelve nullifiers of wudu. Among them, the most debated is wind from the front (prepuce). The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, holds it does not nullify, while Imam Muhammad analogizes it to wind from the back. The soundest view (al-asahh) is the former. Other nullifiers include vomiting filling the mouth, flowing blood, and deep sleep.

Guided Path
1
List the twelve nullifiers
Scan the passage and identify each of the twelve items. Note that not all are explicitly enumerated; the passage elaborates on the major ones.
The list includes exiting of anything from the two passages, childbirth, flowing impurity, vomiting, blood, sleep, touching, etc.
2
Analyze the condition for vomiting
Vomiting only nullifies if it fills the mouth (mil'u al-fam). Multiple vomits are combined if they arise from the same nausea without full recovery.
This is a key Hanafi condition.
3
Analyze the condition for sleep
Sleep nullifies if one is lying down, leaning such that he would fall if support removed, or sitting without buttocks firmly on ground. In prayer, standing, bowing, prostrating, sleep does not nullify.
Based on hadith: 'No wudu on one who sleeps standing, bowing, or prostrating.'
4
Examine the dispute on wind from the front
Abu Hanifa: wind from front (prepuce) does not nullify because it is just muscle contraction. Muhammad: qiyas with back. The soundest view is Abu Hanifa's.
The dispute is based on whether the exit is considered a 'hadath'.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a person feels a sensation from the front, or vomits twice quickly), determine if wudu is nullified using the conditions.
Always check the conditions and the mufta bihi position.

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸٥] ينقض: اعلم أن النقض إذا أضيف إلى الأجسام كنقض الحائط يراد به إبطال تأليفها، وإذا أضيف إلى المعاني كالوضوء يراد به إخراجها عن إقامة المطلوب بها والمطلوب من الوضوء استباحة الصلاة ونحوها مراقي الفلاح و حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٦] من السبيلين إلا ريح القبل في الأصح وينقضه ولادة من غير رؤية دم، ونجاسة سائلة من ذكر وفرج غيرهما كدم وقيح، وقيء طعام أو ماء أو علق أو مرة إذا ملأ الفم، وهو ما لا ينطبق عليه الفم إلا بتكلف على الأصح، ويجمع متفرق القيء إذا اتحد سببه، ودم غلب على البزاق، أو ساواه، ونوم ماض من المساواة. من السبيلين: سمي الأنف. القبل والدبر سبيلا؛ لكونه طريقا للخارج، وسواء المعتاد وغيره كالدودة والحصاة. مراقي الفلاح : ٨٦] إلا ريح القبل: أي الريح الخارج من قبل المرأة وذكر الرجل لا ينقض الوضوء؛ لأنه اختلاج وليس بريح، وعن محمد أنه حدث من قبلها قياساً على الدبر. [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٦/١] الأصح وفي رواية عن محمد الله: أنه لا ينقض. سائلة: اعلم أن السيلان في غير السبيلين بتجاوز النجاسة إلى محل يطلب تطهيره ولو ندباً، فلا ينقض دم سال في داخل العين إلى جانب آخر منها، بخلاف ما صلب من ا مراقي الفلاح: ۸۷] وقيء إلخ : أطلقه فشمل جميع أنواع القيء، سواء قاء من ساعته أم لا. [مراقي الفلاح: ٨٧] إذا ملأ الفم: أي انتقاض الوضوء بأحد هذه الأشياء بشرط كونه ملء الفم. لا ينطبق من الانطباق: انضمام بعضه إلى بعض الأصح يعني ما ذكر من تفسير ملء الفم هو الأصح من التفاسير فيه، وقيل: حده ما يمنع الكلام ويجمع أي إن قاء متفرقاً بحيث لو جمع ملأ الفم، فالمعتبر اتحاد السبب وهو الغثيان وتفسيره : إذا قاء ثانياً قبل سكون النفس من الغثيان فهو متحد، وإن قاء ثانياً بعد سكون النفس فهو مختلف، وهذا هو عند محمد، والمعتبر عند أبي يوسف له اتحاد المجلس. وقال في "مراقي الفلاح" : وقول محمد هو الأصح، وقال أبو علي الدقاق: يجمع كيفما كان مراقي الفلاح: ۸۹] ودم: اعلم أن الدم إذا نزل من الأنف انتقض وضوؤه إذا وصل إلى ما لان منه؛ لأنه يجب تطهيره، وإن خرج من نفس الفم تعتبر الغلبة بينه وبين الريق وإن تساويا انتقض الوضوء؛ لأن البصاق سائل بقوة نفسه، فكذا مساويه، بخلاف المغلوب؛ لأنه سائل بقوة الغالب، ويعتبر ذلك من حيث اللون، فإن كان أحمر انتقض، وإن كان أصفر لا ينتقض، وذكر الإمام علاء الدين أن من أكل خبزاً ورأى أثر الدم فيه من أصول أسنانه، أن ينبغي إصبعه أو طرف كمه على ذلك الموضع، فإن وجد فيه أثر الدم انتقض وضوؤه وإلا فلا. تبيين الحقائق: ٤٨/١] ونوم: اعلم أن النائم لا يخلو : إما أن يكون مضطجعاً فينتقض وضوؤه أو متوركاً، وهو ملحق به؛ لزوال المقعدة من الأرض، أو مستنداً إلى شيء لو أزيل عنه لسقط، فهذا لا يخلو إما أن تكون مقعدته زائلة عن الأرض أو لا، فإن كانت زائلة نقض بالإجماع، وإن كانت غير زائلة فقد ذكر القدوري أنه ينتقض وهو مروي عن الطحاوي، والصحيح أنه لا ينتقض أو يكون قائماً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً، فإنه إن كان في الصلاة لا ينتقض وضوؤه؛ لقوله ل: "لا" وضوء على من نام قائما أو راكعا أو ساجدا، وإن كان خارج الصلاة فكذلك في الصحيح إن كان يضع
Book of Purification. Nullifiers of Wudu. And for continuity on wudu, and wudu on wudu, and after backbiting, lying, slander, and every sin, like insult, hypocrisy, reciting poetry, laughter outside prayer, washing a dead person, carrying him, and for the time of every prayer, and before washing from janabah, and for the junub when eating, drinking, sleeping, intercourse, anger, Quran, hadith and its narration, intention to read it, study of knowledge, adhan, iqamah, sermon, visiting the Prophet, standing at Arafah, for sa'i between Safa and Marwa, eating camel meat, and to exit from disagreement of scholars, like if he touches a woman. Then he said: Section on nullifiers of wudu: Wudu is nullified by twelve things: whatever exits from the two passages even if little, touching a woman or his own private part. ... [continued with extensive commentary]
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, covers two main topics: recommended occasions for wudu (mustahabbat al-wudu) and the nullifiers of wudu (nawaqid al-wudu). The first part lists situations where performing wudu is recommended, such as after sins, before sleep, for eating, etc. The commentary explains that wudu after wudu is only recommended if one has changed one's gathering or performed an act of worship, otherwise it is wasteful. The second part, beginning with 'Fasl fi Nawaqid al-Wudu', lists the twelve nullifiers. The commentary elaborates on each: (1) anything exiting from the two passages (front and back) except wind from the front (prepuce) according to the soundest view, though Imam Muhammad analogically considers it a nullifier; (2) childbirth without blood; (3) flowing impurity from elsewhere; (4) vomiting of food, water, blood, or bile filling the mouth; (5) blood from nose or mouth that equals or exceeds saliva; (6) sleep that is deep (lying down, leaning, etc.) and in certain postures; and others. The commentary details conditions: for vomiting, it must fill the mouth and multiple vomits are combined if from one cause (nausea without pause). For sleep, it nullifies if one is lying, leaning without support, or sitting without the buttocks firmly on the ground. The Hanafi view is presented with intra-madhhab disputes, particularly regarding wind from the front and the combination of vomit. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions are noted: wind from the front does not nullify, and multiple vomits are combined if the nausea persists.

Key Terms
نقض (naqd): In physical objects, it means destruction of structure; in legal terms, it means rendering wudu invalid such that it no longer permits prayer.
حدث (hadath): Legal impurity that prevents worship; nullifiers produce hadath.
ملء الفم (mil'u al-fam): Amount of vomit that fills the mouth, defined as that which does not close without effort.
إلا في الأصح (illa fi al-asahh): Except according to the soundest view; indicates a preferred opinion among Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does wind from the front nullify wudu?
A) Yes, by analogy with wind from the back.
B) No, because it is not considered a hadath.
C) Yes, but only if it makes a sound or smell.
D) No, but only if it occurs during prayer.

Key Takeaway
Wind from the front does not nullify wudu; the soundest view rejects qiyas with the back.

Nullifiers from the Two Passages and Childbirth
Ruling and commentary on nullifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which emissions nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain why wind from the front does not nullify in the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The two passages are the only path — but wind from the front is a twitch, not a nullifier.

In this lesson, we examine the nullifiers of wudu (nawaqid) related to exiting from the two passages (sabīlayn) and childbirth. The core principle is that anything exiting from the front or rear breaks wudu, with an important exception: wind from the urethra (rīḥ al-qabul) does not nullify in the relied-upon Hanafi view. We also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states: 'From the two passages...' meaning anything that exits from the front (urethra/anus) or rear (anus) nullifies wudu. This includes both usual excretions (urine, stool) and unusual ones (worms, pebbles).
The term 'sabīlayn' literally means 'the two ways' and is a technical term for the two excretory passages.
2
Recognize the exception
The exception is 'except wind from the front' (illa rīḥ al-qabul). Wind exiting from the urethra of a man or woman does not nullify wudu according to the most correct (al-ashahh) view.
This exception is specific to wind; other discharges from the front still nullify.
3
Understand the legal cause
The reason given is that such wind is not true wind from the intestines but rather a muscular twitch (ikhṭilāj) from the bladder area. Hence it is not considered a nullifier by the majority of Hanafis.
The source uses the term 'it is a twitch and not wind' to distinguish it from flatus.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (in some narrations) held that wind from the front does nullify by analogy (qiyas) to the rear. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf disagreed, and the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) follows the majority view that it does not nullify.
The phrase 'in the most correct view' (fī al-ashahh) indicates the preferred position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من السبيلين إلا ريح القبل في الأصح وينقضه ولادة من غير رؤية دم. من السبيلين: سمي القبل والدبر سبيلا؛ لكونه طريقا للخارج، وسواء المعتاد وغيره كالدودة والحصاة. [مراقي الفلاح : ٨٦] إلا ريح القبل: أي الريح الخارج من قبل المرأة وذكر الرجل لا ينقض الوضوء؛ لأنه اختلاج وليس بريح، وعن محمد أنه حدث من قبلها قياساً على الدبر. [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٦/١] الأصح وفي رواية عن محمد الله: أنه لا ينقض.
From the two passages except wind from the front in the most correct view, and childbirth without seeing blood nullifies it. From the two passages: they are called the front and the rear because they are a passage for what exits, and it is the same whether usual or otherwise like a worm or pebble. Except wind from the front: i.e., wind exiting from a woman's front and a man's penis does not nullify wudu because it is a twitch and not wind, and from Muhammad that it is an event from her front by analogy to the rear. The most correct: and in a narration from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, that it does not nullify.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah on the nullifiers of wudu. It states that anything exiting from the two passages (front and rear) nullifies wudu, except wind from the front (i.e., from the urethra of a man or woman) which does not nullify in the most correct view. Childbirth without seeing blood also nullifies wudu. The commentary explains that the two passages are called 'sabil' because they are pathways for excretion, and it applies to both usual excretions (urine, stool) and unusual ones like worms or pebbles. The exception for wind from the front is because it is considered a muscle twitch rather than actual wind. A narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it does nullify by analogy to the rear, but the relied-upon position (al-ashahh) is that it does not nullify.

Key Terms
سبيلين (sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (urethra/anus) and the rear (anus). Both are pathways for excretion.
ريح القبل (rīḥ al-qabul): Wind exiting from the front (urethra) of a woman or the penis of a man.
ولادة (wilādah): Childbirth; the act of giving birth. If no blood is seen, it still nullifies wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, does wind exiting from the front (urethra) nullify wudu?
A) Yes, it nullifies because it comes from a passage.
B) No, it does not nullify because it is considered a muscle twitch, not wind.
C) It nullifies only if it is audible.
D) It nullifies only in women.

Key Takeaway
Anything from the two passages nullifies wudu except wind from the front, which is a mere twitch.
