The Ruling on Thin Fluid After Sleep (Ghusl Obligation in Hanafi Fiqh)
Detailed ruling with 12-case classification and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of fluids after sleep (maniy, madhy, wady) to determine whether ghusl is obligatory, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on cases of doubt without a dream.

Core Idea
Ghusl depends on fluid type: certainty of maniy necessitates ghusl; certainty of wady never does; doubt requires dream memory.

Finding moisture after sleep is a common concern for Muslims. The Hanafi school provides a detailed framework to determine when ghusl is required based on the type of fluid and whether a dream is remembered. This lesson unpacks the classical 12-case classification, the condition of no prior erection, and an important intra-madhhab difference between the three eponymous imams. Mastering this will help you correctly identify when ghusl is actually obligatory versus when simple washing suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fluid type and certainty
What does the person find after sleep? Is he certain it is maniy, madhy, or wady, or is he doubtful?
Certainty here means preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), not absolute certainty.
2
Apply the dream memory factor
Does the person remember having a sexual dream? This distinguishes cases where ghusl is obligatory by agreement from those where there is dispute.
3
Check the condition of no prior erection
Was the penis erect before sleep? If yes, the fluid may be madhy, and ghusl is not required (only washing of the area).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
In cases of doubt between maniy and madhy/wady without dream, Abu Yusuf does not require ghusl, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Using the 12-case framework, determine the hukm for a given situation (e.g., person wakes up, finds thin fluid, no erection before sleep, uncertain between maniy and madhy, no dream: ghusl is required according to the majority, not according to Abu Yusuf).

('Existence of water etc.': i.e., among the causes of ghusl is the existence of thin water after awakening from sleep. The summary of the issue of sleep is twelve ways as in al-Bahr; because either he is certain it is maniy, madhy, or wady, or he doubts between the first and second, or the first and third — these are six. And in each of them, either he remembers a dream or not, so twelve are completed. Ghusl is obligatory by agreement when he is certain it is maniy, whether he remembers a dream or not; likewise when he is certain it is madhy and remembers the dream, or he doubts whether it is maniy or madhy, or doubts whether it is maniy or wady, or doubts whether it is madhy or wady and remembers the dream in all cases. Ghusl is not obligatory by agreement when he is certain it is wady absolutely, whether he remembers a dream or not, or when he doubts whether it is madhy or wady and does not remember, or when he is certain it is madhy and does not remember. And ghusl is obligatory according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) but not according to Abu Yusuf when he doubts whether it is maniy or madhy, or when he doubts whether it is maniy or wady and does not remember a dream in both cases. What is meant by certainty here is preponderance of opinion, because true certainty is impossible with sleep. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 99] 'Thin after sleep if his penis was not erect before sleep' — (Commentary:) 'His penis was not etc.' is the condition that the penis was not erect, because erection is a cause for madhy, so it is attributed to it. And it does not differentiate between sleeping lying down or otherwise, like other causes. Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned a distinction made by some: the place of non-obligation of ghusl is if he slept standing or sitting; but if he slept lying down, ghusl is obligatory whether his penis was erect before sleep or not — a non-obvious distinction. So the correct view is that it is unrestricted; there is no apparent difference between them. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 99]
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling regarding finding a thin fluid (similar to maniy) after sleep. The base text of Nur al-Idah states that ghusl is required if a thin fluid is found after sleep, provided the penis was not erect before sleep (to distinguish from madhy). The commentary from al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah provides a detailed 12-way classification based on what the person is certain or doubtful about (whether the fluid is maniy, madhy, or wady) and whether they remember a dream. In essence: if the fluid is certainly maniy, ghusl is always required; if certainly wady, never; if doubt, the ruling depends on remembering a dream. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf does not require ghusl in certain cases of doubt without dream, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do. The condition of no erection before sleep is to rule out madhy, which typically comes with erection. The commentary rejects a distinction between sleeping positions, holding that the ruling is uniform.

Key Terms
مذي (madhy): Pre-ejaculatory fluid; its exit does not require ghusl but only washing and wudu.
ودي (wady): A thick white fluid that sometimes exits after urination; not a factor for ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is there a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the obligation of ghusl after finding fluid?
A) When certain it is maniy and a dream is remembered.
B) When certain it is wady.
C) When there is doubt between maniy and madhy or maniy and wady without remembering a dream.
D) When certain it is madhy and a dream is remembered.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ghusl after sleep is obligatory only for maniy (certain or doubtful with dream) and in doubtful cases without dream according to the majority; madhy without dream or wady never require it.

The Hanafi Dispute on Ghusl for a New Muslim in Janaba
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl for new Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on whether a non-Muslim who becomes Muslim while in a state of janaba must perform ghusl, and identify the relied-upon position with its dalil.

Core Idea
A new Muslim in janaba must perform ghusl; the state of impurity continues and prayer requires purification.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute that arises after listing the causes of ghusl. While the basic causes are clear, a nuanced question emerges: if a non-Muslim accepts Islam while in a state of janaba (major impurity), is ghusl obligatory? Two narrations exist, and we will analyse their proofs and the final tarjih that settles the matter for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
Read the passage from 'قبل الإسلام' to 'فيجب الغسل'. Note the two positions: (1) no ghusl required, (2) ghusl required. Understand the reasoning behind each.
Both narrations are attributed to the Hanafi school; they are not from different schools.
2
Analyse the proof for the first narration
The first narration argues that non-Muslims are not addressed by the branches of Islamic law (furu'), so the obligation of ghusl does not apply to them before Islam. The analogy is a disbelieving woman who menstruates, becomes pure, then becomes Muslim – she does not need ghusl for past impurity.
This relies on the usul principle that kuffar are not mukallaf with furu'.
3
Analyse the proof for the second narration
The second narration argues that the obligation of ghusl arises when intending prayer, and after Islam the person intends prayer. The state of janaba is continuous, so it requires purification. The general verse 'If you are junub, purify yourselves' (5:6) includes him.
This relies on the continuity of the state and the generality of the command.
4
Follow the rebuttal of the first narration
Al-Shalabi and al-Badi' refute the 'not addressed' argument. They point out that the cause of ghusl is the intention to pray, which occurs after Islam. They also distinguish the case of a woman whose bleeding stops (no continuity) from a person who is still in janaba (continuity).
The key distinction: continuity of impurity vs. continuity of purity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that ghusl is obligatory. This is supported by the verse, the continuity argument, and the authority of later Hanafi masters like al-Shalabi and al-Badi'.
The mufta bihi is fard (obligatory), not just recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وهو ظاهر الرواية
مذي،
فصل: عشرة أشياء لا يغتسل منها
ووجود بلل أي إذا أفاق السكران من سكره أو المغمى عليه من إغمائه فوجد على بدنه أو ثوبه بللاً وظن مني، يفترض عليه الغسل. محمد إعزاز علي ظنه منيا يحترز به عما لو كان مذياً؛ فإنه لا غسل عليه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۰] وبحيض: أي يفترض الغسل بانقطاع حيض ونفاس؛ لأن المعدود هنا كما تقدم شروط لا أسباب، وإنما أضيف الوجوب إليهما تسهيلا، والشرط هو الانقطاع لا الخروج [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠٠] قبل الإسلام: اعلم أن الكافر إذا أسلم جنباً ففيه روايتان في رواية لا يجب؛ لأنه ليس مخاطباً بالشرائع، فصار كالكافرة إذا حاضت وطهرت ثم أسلمت وفي رواية: يجب عليه؛ لأن وجوب الغسل بإرادة الصلاة مخاطب، فصار كالوضوء، وهذا لأن صفة الجنابة مستدامة بعد إسلامه فدوامها بعده ،كإنشائها، فيجب الغسل كما في "تبيين الحقائق". [٧٤/١] وقال العلامة الشلبي: ينبغي أن يقول: فيفرض الغسل؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كُنتُمْ جُنُباً فَاطَّهَّرُوا (المائدة: ٦ شامل له لا محالة، وفيه أيضا قال أستاذنا فخر الأئمة البديع وقول من قال: "لا يجب؛ لأن الكفار لا يخاطبون بالشرائع" غير سديد؛ فإن سبب الغسل إرادة الصلاة، وزمان إرادتها مسلم، ولأن صفة الجنابة مستدامة بعد الإسلام، فيعطى لها حكم الإنشاء حتى لو انقطع دم الكافرة ثم أسلمت لا غسل عليها لتعذر استدامة الانقطاع، فلذا لو أسلمت حائضاً، ثم طهرت وجب عليها الغسل الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ٧٤/١] تغسيل وهل يشترط لهذا الغسل النية؟ الظاهر أنها شرط لإسقاط الوجوب عن المكلف لا لتحصيل طهارته. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۰] الميت: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا كان مسلماً غير موصوف بما يسقط غسله كالبغي والشهادة، وبما إذا لم يكن خنثى مشكلاً؛ فإن الخنثى قيل: يتيمم، وقيل: يغسل في ثيابه، والأول أولى.
And the existence of moisture he thinks is maniy after recovering from intoxication or unconsciousness, and by menstruation and postpartum, and if the mentioned things occurred before Islam in the correct view, and it is obligatory by washing the dead as a communal obligation. And that is the apparent narration. (Then a stray line: 'madhy, Chapter: Ten things ghusl is not performed for'.) And the existence of moisture: when the intoxicated person recovers from his intoxication or the unconscious person from his unconsciousness and finds on his body or garment moisture and thinks it is maniy, ghusl is obligatory for him. Muhammad I'zaz Ali: 'thinks it is maniy' to exclude if it was madhy; no ghusl for that. [Tahtawi: 100] And by menstruation: ghusl is obligatory upon cessation of menstruation and postpartum; because what is listed here are conditions, not causes, and obligation is attributed to them for ease; the condition is cessation, not exit. [Tahtawi: 100] Regarding before Islam: know that if a disbeliever becomes Muslim while in a state of janaba, there are two narrations: in one, it is not obligatory because he is not addressed by the laws, so he is like a disbelieving woman who menstruated and became pure then became Muslim; in another narration, it is obligatory because the obligation of ghusl for intending prayer addresses him, so it is like wudu, and because the state of janaba continues after his Islam, so its continuation is like its initiation, so ghusl is obligatory as in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq. [74/1] And al-Allama al-Shalabi said: he should say 'ghusl is obligatory' because the verse 'If you are in a state of janaba, purify yourselves' (5:6) includes him inevitably. And also our teacher Fakhr al-A'imma al-Badi' said: the statement of whoever says 'it is not obligatory because disbelievers are not addressed by the laws' is not sound; for the cause of ghusl is intending prayer, and the time of intending it is as a Muslim, and because the state of janaba continues after Islam, so it is given the ruling of initiation. Thus if the bleeding of a disbelieving woman stops then she becomes Muslim, no ghusl is upon her because continuation of stoppage is impossible; but if she becomes Muslim while menstruating, then she becomes pure, ghusl is obligatory. [Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 74/1] Washing the dead: is it conditional for this ghusl to have intention? Apparently it is a condition for removing obligation from the responsible person, not for achieving purity. [Tahtawi: 100] 'The dead': he made it absolute, but it is restricted to a Muslim who is not described by that which nullifies his washing, like a rebellious woman and martyrdom, and provided he is not a problematic hermaphrodite; for the hermaphrodite, some say tayammum, some say washing in his clothes; the first is preferable.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage covers additional causes of ghusl: (1) finding wetness after intoxication or unconsciousness, assuming it is maniy; (2) cessation of menstruation and postpartum bleeding; (3) washing the deceased (communal obligation). The main content is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a non-Muslim who becomes Muslim while in a state of janaba must perform ghusl. Two narrations are presented: one that no ghusl is required (based on the idea that non-Muslims are not addressed by Islamic laws), and the other that ghusl is obligatory (because the obligation arises from intending prayer, which occurs after Islam, and the state of janaba remains). The commentary by al-Shalabi and others strongly supports the latter, citing the verse from al-Ma'idah and the continuity of the state. The passage also discusses the conditions for washing the deceased: the person must be Muslim and not a martyr or rebellious; for problematic hermaphrodites, tayammum is preferred. Additionally, the requirement of intention for washing the dead is discussed: it is for discharging obligation, not for the validity of the act.

Key Terms
جنابة (janaba): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, typically from sexual intercourse or wet dream.
رواية (riwayah): Narration or transmission; here, a reported legal opinion within the Hanafi school.
مُخاطَب (mukhatab): One who is directly addressed by a legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position regarding a non-Muslim who becomes Muslim while in a state of janaba?
A) No ghusl is required because the person was not Muslim at the time the janaba occurred.
B) Ghusl is required because the state of janaba continues and the person must purify for prayer.
C) Ghusl is required only if the janaba occurred after becoming Muslim.
D) No ghusl is required; the person should perform tayammum instead.

Key Takeaway
A non-Muslim who accepts Islam while in janaba must perform ghusl before praying; this is the operative Hanafi ruling based on the Quran and the continuity of impurity.

The Three Cases of Fluids That Do Not Require Ghusl: Madhy, Wady, and Wet Dream
Listing three of the ten cases where ghusl is not obligatory, with linguistic definitions and the wet dream ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between madhy, wady, and semen, and state the Hanafi ruling that ghusl is not required for madhy and wady, nor for a wet dream without emission.

Core Idea
Not every fluid that exits the body requires ghusl; only semen with force and pleasure obligates the full bath.

In this lesson, we examine three of the ten cases listed in the matn: madhy (pre-ejaculate), wady (post-urine discharge), and a wet dream without any fluid emission. These are often confused with semen, but the Hanafi school clearly distinguishes them based on the absence of force and pleasure. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly identifying when ghusl becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three items
From the list, pick out madhy, wady, and wet dream without emission. Note that the wet dream case applies to both men and women per the apparent narration.
The wet dream without emission is item 3 in the list.
2
Analyze the definitions
Read the linguistic descriptions: madhy is thin, sticky, exits without force; wady is thick, turbid, follows urine. Note that both lack the characteristic force and pleasure of semen.
The text gives multiple correct pronunciations for madhy.
3
Contrast with semen
Semen exits with force and pleasure, and its exit obligates ghusl. The fluids in this lesson do not have those properties, so ghusl is not required.
The key distinguishing criteria: force and pleasure (or lack thereof).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a scenario: a person wakes up and finds a thin, sticky discharge. Use the definitions to identify it as madhy, then conclude that only wudu is required, not ghusl.
This step solidifies the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: عشرة أشياء لا يغتسل منها: المذي، والودي، والاحتلام بلا بلل، والولادة من غير رؤية دم بعدها في الصحيح، والإيلاج بخرقة مانعة من وجود اللذة، والحقنة، وإدخال إصبع ونحوه في أحد السبيلين، ووطء البهيمة أو الميتة من غير إنزال، وإصابة بكر لم تزل بكارتها من غير إنزال. مذي: وهو بفتح الميم وسكون الذال المعجمة وكسرها مع تخفيف الياء وهو أفصح كالأولى، وتشديدها. وودي بإسكان الدال المهملة وتخفيف الياء، وهو ماء أبيض كدر ثخين لا رائحة له، يعقب البول، وقد يسبقه. واحتلام والمرأة فيه كالرجل في ظاهر الرواية. في الصحيح وهو قولهما؛ لعدم النفاس، وقال الإمام عليها الغسل احتياطاً؛ لعدم خلوها عن قليل دم ظاهر. وإيلاج أي إدخال ذكر بعد ما لفه بخرقة تمنع من وجود اللذة. وإصابة أي مما لا يفترض الاغتسال جماع امرأة باكرة بحيث لا تزول بكارتها ولا ينزل المجامع.
Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed: al-Madhy, al-Wady, wet dream without wetness, childbirth without seeing blood after it according to the sound opinion, insertion with a cloth that prevents pleasure, enema, insertion of a finger or similar into one of the two passages, intercourse with an animal or a dead body without ejaculation, and hitting a virgin whose virginity has not been removed without ejaculation. Madhy: it is [pronounced] with fath of the meem and sukun of the dhal and kasr with tashdid of the ya, and it is more eloquent like the first pronunciation. Wady: with sukun of the daal and tashdid of the ya, it is a thick white water with no smell, following urine, sometimes preceding it. Wet dream: and the woman is like the man in the apparent narration. In the sound opinion, it is their saying due to absence of postpartum bleeding, and Imam [Abu Hanifa] said that ghusl is obligatory upon her as a precaution due to her not being free from a little apparent blood. Insertion: meaning inserting the penis after wrapping it with a cloth that prevents the sensation of pleasure. Hitting: meaning intercourse with a virgin woman such that her virginity is not removed and the man does not ejaculate, [which] does not necessitate ghusl.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing ten specific situations in which ghusl (full body wash) is not obligatory, contrary to what might be assumed. The text follows the Hanafi school's position, and the list is presented as a matn (core text) with brief explanatory notes. The first item, madhy (pre-ejaculate fluid), is defined linguistically as a thin white fluid that exits without force or pleasure. The second, wady, is a thick turbid fluid that comes after urine. The third, a wet dream without any emission of fluid, does not necessitate ghusl. The fourth, childbirth without seeing blood afterward, is ruled by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad not to require ghusl, while Abu Hanifa advises it as a precaution. The fifth, inserting the penis into a vagina (or anus) with a barrier that blocks pleasure, does not require ghusl because the essence of intercourse (the sensation) is missing. The sixth, an enema, does not cause janabah. The seventh, inserting a finger or similar object into the front or back passage, does not require ghusl. The eighth, intercourse with an animal or a dead body without ejaculation, does not cause janabah. The ninth, striking a virgin in a way that her hymen remains intact and no ejaculation occurs, does not require ghusl. All these rulings are based on the principle that ghusl is only obligatory when there is either a discharge of semen (with force and pleasure) or actual penetration of the glans into a private part with pleasure. The conditions for each item are carefully stated to avoid overextension.

Key Terms
المذي (al-madhy): A thin, sticky white fluid that exits at times of sexual excitement, without force or pleasure, and does not cause ghusl.
الودي (al-wady): A thick, turbid white fluid that follows urine or sometimes precedes it, does not require ghusl.
الاحتلام (al-ihtilam): A wet dream; if there is no emission of fluid, ghusl is not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does NOT require ghusl?
A) Ejaculation from a wet dream
B) Madhy (pre-ejaculate fluid)
C) Childbirth with blood
D) Intercourse with pleasure without ejaculation

Key Takeaway
Madhy and wady, as well as a wet dream without emission, do not require ghusl because they lack the force and pleasure characteristic of semen.

The Remaining Seven: When Ghusl Is Not Required Despite Penetration or Contact
Listing the remaining seven cases from the ten, with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on childbirth and a principle-based explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven additional cases in which ghusl is not obligatory, explain the underlying principle (absence of pleasure or emission), and analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on childbirth.

Core Idea
Ghusl is not required when there is no pleasure during insertion, no blood after childbirth, or no ejaculation with an animal or dead body.

This lesson covers the remaining seven items from the matn: childbirth without blood, insertion with a barrier, enema, finger insertion, intercourse with an animal or a dead body without ejaculation, and intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen or ejaculating. These cases all share a common theme: the absence of either pleasure or ejaculation, which are the essential triggers for janabah. We also explore a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding childbirth.

Guided Path
1
List the seven remaining cases
From the text, identify the items starting from 'childbirth without blood' through 'hitting a virgin without removing virginity or ejaculating'. There are seven distinct cases.
The passage continues with definitions for 'insertion' and 'hitting'.
2
Identify the common principle
For each case, determine why ghusl is not required. The common thread: either there is no pleasure (barrier, enema, finger, animal/mayyit) or no emission (childbirth without blood, virgin without ejaculation).
Pleasure and ejaculation are the two triggers for janabah.
3
Analyze the childbirth disagreement
The text presents the sound opinion (of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that if no blood is seen after childbirth, ghusl is not required because it is not nifas. However, Abu Hanifa recommends ghusl as a precaution. Note the reasoning.
This is a rare intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf within the matn.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a man who inserts his finger into another's anus. Use the principle: no pleasure (since it's not sexual), so no ghusl.
The text explicitly includes 'insertion of a finger or similar into one of the two passages'.

The Obligatory Acts of Ghusl (Fara'id al-Ghusl)
Enumeration of obligatory acts with conditions and explanation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eleven obligatory acts of ghusl in the Hanafi school and explain why they reduce to a single principle.

Core Idea
Eleven enumerated fard acts reduce to one: covering the entire body with water without hardship.

This lesson examines the fard (obligatory) components of ghusl as outlined in Nur al-Idah. While the Hanafi school enumerates eleven distinct acts, the author explains they are essentially a single obligation: complete coverage of the body with water, without hardship. The enumeration serves pedagogical purposes and highlights areas of ikhtilaf, particularly the mouth and nose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eleven enumerated acts
Read the list: washing the mouth, nose, body once, inside of foreskin (without difficulty), navel, open piercings, and inside of braided hair (for men). Note that these are not separate obligations but subdivisions of the single fard of body coverage.
The list is comprehensive and includes external body parts, mouth, nose, and treatment of hair and piercings.
2
Understand the unifying principle
The text states all eleven 'reduce to one': 'عموم الماء على الجسد بلا حرج' (covering the body with water without hardship). This means the obligation is simply to ensure every part of the body is wetted, with no requirement of water penetrating hair roots or extreme exertion.
The condition 'без hardship' (bila haraj) is key—it alleviates obligations in difficult cases (tight foreskin, closed piercings).
3
Analyze the conditions for each part
For the foreskin: it must be washed only if retraction is without difficulty. For piercings: only open ones need internal washing. For braided hair: the inside must be wetted even if water does not reach the roots. Mouth and nose are fard, but exaggeration is sunnah.
These conditions show the school's practical approach: obligation is tied to what is normally feasible without undue hardship.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf on mouth and nose
The author notes that mouth and nose are singled out because of disagreement: Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i consider them sunnah in ghusl. The Hanafi school insists they are fard, and denying them does not constitute kufr.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are respected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [في بيان الغسل] يفترض في الاغتسال أحد عشر شيئاً: غسل الفم والأنف، والبدن مرة، وداخل قلفة لا عسر في فسخها، وسرة، وثقب غير منضم، وداخل المضفور من شعر الرجل مطلقاً، وهو فرض اجتهادي. وكلها ترجع لواحد، وهو عموم الماء على الجسد بلا حرج، ولكن عدت للتعليم. غسل الفم إلخ أي بدون مبالغة فيهما؛ فإنها سنة فيه على المعتمد، وشرب الماء عباً يقوم مقام غسل الفم لا مصاً. والبدن [عطف عام على خاص ومنه الفرج الخارج؛ لأنه كفمها، لا الداخل؛ لأنه كالحلق فإن قلت: لا حاجة إلى ما ذكر الأنف والفم بل يكفي ذكر البدن، قلنا: إنما أفردهما لوقوع الخلاف فيهما؛ لأنهما سنتان عند الإمامين مالك والشافعي، ولأنهما لا يكفر جاحدهما. القلفة هي الجلدة الساترة للحشفة. لا عسر إلخ شرط عدم العسر؛ فإنه إن تعسر فهي لا يكلف بغسله كثقب انضم. المضفور الضفر: فتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض مطلقاً: أي سواء سرى الماء في أصوله أو لا.
Chapter [on explaining ghusl]: Eleven things are obligatory in ghusl: washing the mouth and nose, and the body once, and the inside of the foreskin without difficulty in retracting it, and the navel, and a piercing that is not closed, and the inside of braided hair of a man absolutely, and it is an ijtihadi fard. And all of them reduce to one: covering the entire body with water without hardship, but they are counted for teaching purposes. Washing the mouth etc.: that is without exaggeration in them; for exaggeration is sunnah according to the relied-upon view. And drinking water gulping takes the place of washing the mouth, not sipping. And the body: general specifically, and from it is the external private parts because it is like its mouth, not the internal because it is like the throat. If you say: there is no need to mention the nose and mouth—it suffices to mention the body, we say: they were singled out because there is disagreement regarding them; for they are sunnah according to Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, and because denying them does not constitute disbelief. The foreskin: it is the skin covering the glans. Without difficulty: condition of no difficulty; if it is difficult, he is not obliged to wash it, like a closed piercing. The braided: braiding is intertwining hair and inserting some into some absolutely: meaning whether water reaches its roots or not.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the fard (obligatory) acts of ghusl. According to the Hanafi school, ghusl has eleven obligatory components: washing the mouth, nose, and entire body once, including washing under the foreskin (for uncircumcised men) if it can be retracted without difficulty, the navel, any open piercings, and the inside of braided hair (for men, regardless of whether water reaches the roots). However, the commentator explains that these eleven are essentially reducible to a single obligation: covering the entire body with water without hardship. The enumeration is for educational purposes. Notably, the mouth and nose are specifically mentioned because there is a difference of opinion with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, who consider them sunnah rather than fard; in the Hanafi school, they are fard in ghusl. The commentary also clarifies that exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and nose is sunnah (recommended), not fard, and that drinking water by gulping suffices for washing the mouth during ghusl, but sipping does not. The body includes the external private parts, but not the internal parts (like the inner urethra). The foreskin must be washed unless it is too tight (difficulty), in which case it is excused. Similarly, closed piercings do not need to be opened. Braided hair must be washed on the inside even if water does not reach the roots—the obligation is simply to wet the braid, not to ensure water penetrates to the roots, which is a distinct difference from the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms
فرائض الغسل (fara'id al-ghusl): The obligatory components of the ritual bath (ghusl); in Hanafi fiqh, they are eleven items but essentially one: covering the body with water.
القلفة (al-qulfah): The foreskin; it must be retracted and washed if possible without difficulty.
المضفور (al-madfur): Braided hair; the inside of the braid must be washed, regardless of whether water reaches the roots.
البدن (al-badan): The entire body, including external private parts; internal parts are not included.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is fard whether or not water reaches the roots

D) It is not required at all if the hair is braided

Key Takeaway
Eleven enumerated fard acts of ghusl reduce to one: complete, hardship-free coverage of the body with water, including mouth, nose, and other specified parts.

Causes of Ghusl and Definitions of Madhy and Wady
Lists causes of ghusl and defines fluids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the causes that necessitate ghusl and distinguish between madhy and wady based on their properties and rulings.

Core Idea
Ghusl is required for specific causes; madhy and wady have distinct rulings and definitions.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary, enumerates the events that make ghusl obligatory and clarifies the characteristics of pre-seminal fluids. Understanding these distinctions is essential for proper purification according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the causes of ghusl
Scan the passage to list all actions or events that require ghusl. Note that the enumeration begins after 'فرائض الغسل' and includes items like wady, wet dream without fluid, insertion with a barrier, enema, and others.
There are about eleven items lumped together; the passage later says they all reduce to one.
2
Differentiate madhy and wady
Find the definitions of madhy and wady. Madhy is thin, white, emerges with desire, often without sensation. Wady is thick, turbid, odorless, follows urine. Note their gender differences.
Madhy is more common in women; wady is in both.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Look for the phrase 'في الصحيح وهو قولهما' regarding childbirth without blood. Identify that Abu Hanifa holds ghusl obligatory as a precaution, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is not obligatory because nifas is not confirmed.
The relied-upon view is that of the two companions.
4
Understand the overarching principle
The passage ends by stating that all eleven obligatory acts of ghusl revert to one: covering the entire body with water without hardship. The enumeration is for teaching.
This emphasizes that the essence of ghusl is complete washing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرائض الغسل وودي، واحتلام بلا بلل، وولادة من غير رؤية دم بعدها في الصحيح، وإيلاج بخرقة مانعة من وجود اللذة وحقنة وإدخال إصبع ونحوه في أحد السبيلين، ووطء بهيمة أو ميتة من غير إنزال، وإصابة بكر لم تزل بكارتها من غير إنزال. "وهو ماء أبيض رقيق يخرج عند شهوة، لا بشهوة ولا دفق ولا يعقبه فتور وربما لا يحس بخروجه"، وهو أغلب في النساء من الرّجال ويسمى في جانب النساء "قذي" بفتح القاف والذال المعجمة [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٠] وودي بإسكان الدال المهملة وتخفيف الياء، وهو ماء أبيض كدرٌ ثخين لا رائحة له، يعقب البول، وقد يسبقه. مراقي الفلاح (۱۰۱] :واحتلام والمرأة فيه كالرجل في ظاهر الرواية". (مراقي الفلاح) في الصحيح وهو قولهما؛ لعدم النفاس، وقال الإمام عليها الغسل احتياطاً؛ لعدم خلوها عن قليل دم ظاهر كما تقدم. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۰۱] وإيلاج أي إدخال ذكر بعد ما لفه بخرقة تمنع من وجود اللذة. وجود ود اللذة اقتصر على اللذة هنا، وزاد فيما تقدم وجود الحرارة، ولعلهما متلازمان [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠١] ونحوه كشبه ذكر مصنوع من نحو جلد مراقي الفلاح (۱۰۱] وإصابة أي مما لا يفترض الاغتسال جماع امرأة باكرة بحيث لا تزول بكارتها ولا ينزل المجامع أحد عشر وكلها ترجع لواحد، وهو عموم الماء ما الجسد بلا حرج، ولكن عدت للتعليم. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٢]
Obligatory acts of ghusl: and wady, and a wet dream without fluid, and childbirth without seeing blood after it in the correct view, and insertion (of the penis) wrapped in a cloth that prevents the sensation of pleasure, and an enema, and inserting a finger or similar into either of the two passages, and bestiality or necrophilia without ejaculation, and intercourse with a virgin whose virginity has not been removed without ejaculation. "It is a thin white fluid that emerges at desire, not with desire nor with force, and is not followed by lethargy, and perhaps one does not feel its exit." It is more common in women than men and is called 'qadhy' in women (with fatha on qaf and dhal). [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 100] And wady (with sukun on dal and tashdid on ya) is a thick, turbid, white fluid with no odor, following urine and sometimes preceding it. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 101] And a wet dream: a woman is like a man in the apparent narration. (Marāqī al-Falāḥ) In the correct view, it is the position of the two companions due to the absence of nifās, but Imam (Abu Hanifa) said she must perform ghusl as a precaution because she is not free from a small amount of apparent blood, as previously mentioned. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 101] And 'īlāj': inserting the penis after wrapping it in a cloth that prevents the sensation of pleasure. The sensation of pleasure was confined to pleasure here, and previously heat was added; they are probably inseparable. [Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī: 101] And 'naḥwihi': like an artificial penis made of leather, etc. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 101] And 'iṣābah': intercourse with a virgin that does not remove her virginity and the man does not ejaculate; the eleven (obligatory acts) all go back to one, which is covering the entire body with water without hardship, but they were enumerated for teaching. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 102]
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the causes (asbāb) that make ghusl obligatory. It begins by enumerating the main causes: emission of wady, a wet dream without actual fluid, childbirth without visible blood (in the relied-upon view), inserting the penis with a barrier preventing pleasure, enema, insertion of a finger or similar into the anus or urethra, bestiality or necrophilia without ejaculation, and intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen and without ejaculation. The author then provides definitions of madhy and wady, clarifying their characteristics and gender differences. An intra-Hanafi dispute is presented regarding a woman who gives birth without seeing blood: the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that ghusl is not obligatory because nifās is not confirmed, while Abu Hanifa holds it is obligatory as a precaution. The passage also explains that 'īlāj' even with a barrier necessitates ghusl, and that intercourse with a virgin without ejaculation or breaking the hymen necessitates ghusl. Finally, it notes that the eleven obligatory acts of ghusl all revert to one principle: covering the entire body with water without hardship, and the enumeration is for teaching purposes.

Key Terms
مَذْي (madhy): Thin white fluid that emerges at sexual desire, often without sensation.
وَدْي (wady): Thick turbid white fluid without odor that follows urine or sometimes precedes it.
قُلْفَة (qulfah): The foreskin covering the glans of the penis.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is obligatory for specific events; knowing the exact causes and the distinctions between fluids is essential for proper Taharah.

The Obligatory Acts of Ghusl (Farā'iḍ al-Ghusl)
Enumerates and explains the eleven obligatory acts of ritual bath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eleven obligatory acts of ghusl and identify which specific body parts must be washed, including the conditions for exceptions like difficulty.

Core Idea
All eleven obligatory acts of ghusl revert to one: covering the entire body with water without hardship.

The source text enumerates eleven farā'iḍ of ghusl. While the ruling seems detailed, the core principle is simple: ensure water reaches every part of the body. The specific items are pedagogical, highlighting areas often missed or debated. This lesson guides you through each obligatory act, its conditions, and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Recall the overriding principle
All obligations revert to covering the whole body with water without undue hardship. This is the essence of ghusl.
The enumeration is for teaching; the single principle unifies everything.
2
Identify the eleven obligatory acts
The text lists explicitly: washing the mouth, nose, entire body once, inside the foreskin (if not difficult), navel, non-closed piercings, and inside a man's braided hair unconditionally. The 'body' includes all external skin, private parts, beard, eyebrows, etc., which together make up the eleven.
The number eleven is pedagogical; focus on the principle and the specific areas.
3
Apply the condition of difficulty
Washing the inside of the foreskin and piercings is obligatory only if not difficult. If difficult (e.g., pain, swelling), it is excused and ghusl remains valid.
Difficulty is judged by 'urf (custom) and individual capability.
4
Distinguish between men's and women's braided hair
For a man, washing the inside of braided hair is obligatory regardless of whether water reaches the roots. For a woman, it is not obligatory if water reaches the roots; otherwise, she must undo it.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [في بيان الغسل] يفترض في الاغتسال أحد عشر شيئاً : غَسل الفم والأنف، والبدن مرة، وداخل قلفة لا عُسر في فسخها، وسُرَّة، وثقب غير منضم، وداخل المضفور من شعر الرجل مطلقاً، وكلها ترجع لواحد، وهو عموم الماء ما الجسد بلا حرج، ولكن عدت للتعليم. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٢] غسل الفم إلخ أي بدون مبالغة فيهما؛ فإنها سنة فيه على المعتمد، وشرب الماء عباً يقوم مقام غسل الفم لا مصاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۲] والبدن [عطف عام على خاص ومنه الفرج الخارج؛ لأنه كفمها، لا الداخل؛ لأنه كالحلق فإن قلت: لا حاجة إلى ما ذكر الأنف والفم بل يكفي ذكر البدن، قلنا: إنما أفردهما لوقوع الخلاف فيهما؛ أمكن من لأنهما سنتان عند الإمامين مالك والشافعي ، ولأنهما لا يكفر جاحدهما. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٢] القلفة هي الجلدة الساترة للحشفة. لا عسر إلخ شرط عدم العسر؛ فإنه إن تعسر فهي لا يكلف بغسله كثقب انضم. [مراقي الفلاح (۱۰۲] المضفور الضفر : فتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض مطلقاً: أي سواء سرى الماء في أصوله أو لا. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٣] لا المضفور من شعر المرأة إن سرى الماء في أصوله وبشرة اللحية، وبشرة الشارب، والحاجب، والفرج الخارج.
Section [on explaining ghusl]. Eleven things are obligatory in ghusl: washing the mouth and nose, and the entire body once, and the inside of the foreskin that is not difficult to retract, and the navel, and any non-closed piercing, and the inside of braided hair for a man absolutely. And all of them go back to one principle: covering the whole body with water without hardship, but they were enumerated for teaching. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 102] Washing the mouth etc. means without exaggeration in them; for exaggeration is sunnah in them according to the relied-upon view, and drinking water in gulps suffices for washing the mouth, not sipping. [Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī: 102] And the body: it is a general term that includes the specific; from it is the external private part because it is like the mouth of the woman, not the internal because it is like the throat. If you say: there is no need to mention the mouth and nose; mentioning the body suffices, we say: they were singled out because of the difference of opinion regarding them, since they are sunnah according to Imams Malik and Shafi'i, and because the one who denies them does not become a disbeliever. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 102] The qulfah is the skin covering the glans. 'No difficulty' etc. is a condition: if it is difficult, he is not required to wash it, like a closed piercing. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 102] Al-maḍfūr: twisting hair and intertwining it; for a man absolutely, whether water reaches the roots or not. [Marāqī al-Falāḥ: 103] Not the braided hair of a woman if water reaches the roots, and the skin of the beard, the skin of the moustache, the eyebrow, and the external private part.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that details the obligatory acts (farā'iḍ) of ghusl. It lists eleven specific items: washing the mouth, nose, entire body once, inside the foreskin (if not difficult), navel, any non-closed piercing, and inside braided hair for a man unconditionally. The author then notes that all eleven revert to one: covering the whole body with water without hardship; the enumeration is pedagogical. The commentary explains that washing the mouth and nose is fard in the Hanafi school, but without exaggeration; drinking water in gulps suffices for mouth. The body includes the external private parts by implication. The mouth and nose were singled out because other schools consider them sunnah. The qulfah must be washed unless it is difficult; if hard, it is excused like a closed piercing. A man's braided hair must be washed whether water reaches the roots or not, but a woman's braided hair need not be undone if water reaches the roots. The skin of the beard, moustache, eyebrows, and external private parts are included in the general body washing.

Key Terms
قُلْفَة (qulfah): Foreskin; must be washed in ghusl if not difficult.
مَضْفُور (maḍfūr): Braided hair; for a man, obligatory to wash inside regardless of water penetration.
سُرَّة (surrah): Navel; must be washed inside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 4
B) 7
C) 11
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The obligatory acts of ghusl all reduce to ensuring water covers every external and accessible internal part of the body without hardship, with specific emphasis on mouth, nose, foreskin, navel, piercings, and man's braided hair.

Twelve Sunnan of Ghusl and Their Details
Lists twelve sunnan with commentary on key disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the twelve sunnan of ghusl and distinguish between sunnah, fard, and disputed points within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Twelve acts are sunnah in ghusl; omitting them does not invalidate ghusl but reduces reward.

Ghusl has obligatory (fard) elements, but the Prophet ﷺ also performed recommended acts (sunnan). This lesson covers the twelve sunnan as enumerated in the Hanafi school, along with key details and intra-madhhab disputes on wiping the head and delaying foot washing. Understanding these sunnan helps you perfect your ghusl and avoid confusion between what is required and what is meritorious.

Guided Path
1
Identify the twelve sunnan
Read the list of twelve items in the Arabic text: tasmiyah, niyyah, washing hands, removing impurity alone, washing private part, wudu like for prayer (with three washes and wiping head), delaying feet if water collects, pouring water three times starting with head, then right shoulder, then left shoulder, rubbing body, and washing consecutively.
Some enumerate them differently; this is the standard list.
2
Clarify the ruling of each sunnah
Each is sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended) but not fard. For example, washing hands to wrists is sunnah even if clean. The text also mentions that undoing braided hair is not fard if water reaches roots.
This distinguishes sunnah from fard obligations like intention (niyyah is actually fard in ghusl? The text lists it as sunnah but intention is generally fard for all acts of worship. Clarify: the text lists niyyah as sunnah here, but that is a minority view; the relied-upon Hanafi position is that niyyah is fard. Check maraqi al-Falah. For this lesson, we follow the source's list.
3
Examine the dispute on wiping the head
The commentary indicates that wiping the head during wudu for ghusl is sunnah according to zahir al-riwayah, but al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is not done because the subsequent pouring of water over the head makes it redundant. The correct view (mufta bihi) is that it is sunnah.
This shows how later Hanafi masters resolved an ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the dispute on delaying foot washing
Most mashayikh hold it is sunnah to delay washing the feet until after pouring water if water collects. This is based on the hadith of Maymunah. Some do not delay based on Aisha's hadith. The preferred view (al-Mujtaba) is detail: delay if water collects, otherwise not.
This reconciles conflicting hadiths.
5
Apply the sunnan in practice
When performing ghusl, follow the sequence: make intention, say Bismillah, wash hands, remove impurity, wash private part, perform wudu (including wiping head, but do not wash feet yet if standing in water), then pour water over head three times, right shoulder three times, left shoulder three times, then rub body, and finally wash feet if not already done. Immersion in water with proper intent fulfills the sunnan.
The method of pouring water has variations; the author mentions starting with the head.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الغسل]
يسن في الاغتسال اثنا عشر شيئا الابتداء بالتسمية والنية وغسل اليدين إلى الرسغين، وإن لم يكن به نجاسة تثنية رسغ وغسل نجاسة لو كانت بانفرادها وغسل فرجه ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصلاة، فيثلث الغسل، ويمسح الرأس، ولكنه يؤخر غسل الرّجلين إن كان يقف في محل يجتمع فيه الماء، ثم يفيض الماء على بدنه ثلاثا ولو انغمس في الماء الجاري، أو ما في حكمه ومكث دخل كالعشر في العشر فقد أكمل السنة، ويبتدئ في صب الماء برأسه، ويغسل بعدها منكبه الأيمن، ثم الأيسر، الأولى التذكير
لا المضفور: أي لا يفترض نقض المضفور من شعر المرأة إلخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۰۳] وغسل اليدين: واعلم أنه يقال: غسل الجمعه وغسل الجنابة بضم الغين وغسل الميت وغسل الثوب بفتحها وضابطه: إنك إذا أضفت إلى المغسول فتحت، وإذا أضفت إلى غيره ضممت لو كانت بانفرادها إلخ أي لو كانت النجاسة على بدنه يغسلها بانفرادها، فإن قلت: إن مطلق إزالة القدر المانع من النجاسة فرض سواء كانت على بدنه أو غيره، فلم عدّها الشيخ من سنن الاغتسال؟ قلت : المراد أن إزالتها قبل الوضوء والاغتسال هو السنة؛ لئلا تزداد بإضافة الماء. کوضوئه : فيه إشارة إلى أنه يمسح رأسه، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يمسح؛ لأنه لا فائدة فيه؛ لأن الإسالة تقدم المسح والصحيح أنه يمسحه الجوهرة النيرة : ۱۲/۱] ولكنه يؤخر إلخ: فيه اختلاف المشائخ، فقيل: لا يؤخر؛ لأن عائشة لها أطلقت في روايتها صفة غسله ، فلم تذكر تأخير الرجلين كما أخرجه الشيخان، وأكثرهم على أنه يؤخر؛ لحديث ميمونة ، فإن فيه تنصيصاً على التأخير، قال في "المجتبى": والأصح التفصيل و به يحصل التوفيق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠٤] ثم يفيض إلخ وأما كيفية الإفاضة فقال الحلواني يفيض الماء على منكبه الأيمن ثلاثاً، ثم الأيسر ثلاثاً، ثم على رأسه وعلى سائر جسده ثلاثاً، وفي بعضها يبدأ بالأيمن ثلاثاً، ثم بالرأس، ثم بالأيسر، وقيل: يبدأ بالرأس. الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ٦٢/١] ولو انغمس أي المغتسل أي بعدما تمضمض واستنشق. ومكث : أي مكث منغمساً قدر الوضوء والغسل أو مكث في المطر قدر الوضوء أو الغسل، فإنه يكون آتياً بكمال السنة فيه.
ويدلك جسده، ويوالي غسله. أي يغسل متواليا
Section on the sunnan of ghusl: It is sunnah in ghusl twelve things: beginning with tasmiyah and niyyah, washing the hands to the wrists even if there is no impurity, washing impurity if present separately, washing his private part, then performing wudu like his wudu for prayer, repeating the wash three times, wiping the head, but he delays washing the feet if he is standing in a place where water collects, then pouring water over his body three times, and if he immerses himself in flowing water or the like and remains for the duration of [the ghusl], he has completed the sunnah, and he begins pouring water on his head, then washes his right shoulder, then left. The first is masculine. The braided [hair]: it is not obligatory to undo the braided hair of a woman, etc. [Maraqi al-Falah: 103] And washing the hands: know that one says 'ghusl al-jumu'ah' and 'ghusl al-janabah' with damm on the ghayn, and 'ghusl al-mayyit' and 'ghusl al-thawb' with fatha. The rule: if you add to the washed object, you open; if you add to something else, you double. 'If it is separate' etc.: meaning if impurity is on his body, he washes it separately. If you say: removing the preventer of impurity is fard whether on his body or otherwise, why did the shaykh count it among the sunnan of ghusl? I say: the intent is that removing it before wudu and ghusl is sunnah so that it does not increase by adding water. 'Like his wudu': there is indication that he wipes his head, and that is the apparent narration, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not wipe because there is no benefit, as the washing precedes wiping, and the correct view is that he wipes it [al-Jawhara al-Nira: 2/12]. 'But he delays' etc.: there is ikhtilaf among the mashayikh. It is said: he does not delay because Aisha described his ghusl and did not mention delaying the feet as narrated by the two shaykhs, and most say he delays due to the hadith of Maymunah which explicitly mentions delay. Al-Mujtaba says: the most correct is detail, and that achieves reconciliation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 104] 'Then he pours' etc.: as for the method of pouring, al-Halwani says: he pours water on his right shoulder three times, then left three times, then on his head and all his body three times; in some narrations, he begins with the right three times, then head, then left; and it is said he begins with the head. [al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/62] 'And if he immerses himself': i.e. the one doing ghusl after rinsing his mouth and nose. 'And remains': i.e. remains immersed for the measure of wudu and ghusl, or remains in rain for the measure of wudu or ghusl, then he has fulfilled the sunnah completely. And he rubs his body, and performs it consecutively, i.e. he washes consecutively.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage lists the twelve recommended acts (sunnan) of ghusl according to the Hanafi school, followed by detailed commentary. The sunnan include: intention, saying Bismillah, washing hands, removing impurity from the body, washing the private part, performing wudu as for prayer (including washing each part three times and wiping the head), but delaying washing the feet if water pools, then pouring water over the body three times, starting with the head, then right shoulder, then left, then rubbing the body, and washing consecutively. The commentary clarifies several points: it is not fard to undo braided hair if water reaches the roots; washing impurity before wudu is sunnah to prevent spreading; there is a dispute about wiping the head during wudu for ghusl (Abu Hanifa said no, but the relied-upon view is yes); and there is a dispute about delaying the foot washing (some say no delay based on Aisha's hadith, others say delay based on Maymunah's hadith; the preferred view is a detailed one depending on context). The method of pouring water (right shoulder first or head first) is also discussed. Finally, immersion in water fulfills the sunnan if done properly.

Key Terms
المضفور (al-maḍfūr): Braided hair of a woman; it is not fard to undo it as long as water reaches the roots.
الرسغين (al-rasghayn): Wrists (dual); washing hands to wrists is sunnah in ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on undoing braided hair during ghusl?
A) It is fard (obligatory) to undo it always.
B) It is not fard as long as water reaches the roots.
C) It is sunnah to undo it.
D) It is makruh to undo it.

Key Takeaway
The twelve sunnan of ghusl are recommended acts that perfect the ritual bath; omitting them does not invalidate ghusl, and internal Hanafi disputes on details have been resolved by later authorities.

Adab and Makruhat of Ghusl: Same as Wudu with One Exception
States that the etiquettes of ghusl mirror those of wudu except facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the adab and makruhat of ghusl mirror those of wudu, and explain the exception regarding facing the qibla and the condition for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Ghusl's adab match wudu's, except facing qibla — due to 'awrah exposure; covering allows it.

This brief passage from Nur al-Idah establishes a convenient rule: you already know the recommended and disliked acts for ghusl if you know wudu. Only one element is different — facing the qibla. Understanding why and when this exception applies will help you practice ghusl correctly and avoid unnecessary restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Recall the adab of wudu
Think about the recommended acts (adab) in wudu, such as using a miswak, rinsing the mouth, sniffing water, and reciting du'as.
2
Apply the general rule
The text says the adab of ghusl are the same as wudu. So all those recommended acts carry over to ghusl.
3
Identify the exception
Unlike wudu, facing the qibla is not recommended during ghusl. The text gives the reason: ghusl often involves uncovering the 'awrah.
4
Understand the condition
The commentary clarifies that if the 'awrah is covered (e.g., with a cloth or partition), then facing qibla is not disliked — it is permissible.
The ruling is conditional on covering the 'awrah.

فصل في آداب الاغتسال ومكروهاته]

Commentary
This short passage establishes that the recommended acts (adab) for ghusl are identical to those for wudu, such as using a miswak, rinsing the mouth, sniffing water, etc. The only exception is that facing the qibla is not recommended during ghusl because the private parts are typically exposed. However, as the commentary clarifies, if the 'awrah is covered (e.g., with a cloth or partition), then facing qibla is permissible and not disliked. The disliked acts (makruhat) of wudu also apply to ghusl, such as excessive water usage or splashing water wastefully.

Key Terms
آداب (ādāb): Etiquettes or recommended acts; performing them increases reward but omission does not invalidate.
مكروهات (makrūhāt): Disliked acts; doing them is not sinful but reduces reward.

Recommended Occasions for Ghusl and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Friday Ghusl
List of recommended ghusl occasions with intra-school dispute on Friday ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four occasions when ghusl is sunnah and explain the practical consequence of the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether Friday ghusl is for the day or for the prayer.

Core Idea
Friday ghusl is sunnah, but does it belong to the day or the prayer? The answer changes who should do it.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the occasions when ghusl is recommended (sunnah or mustahabb). While the four main occasions are clear, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute emerges over Friday ghusl: is it for the day itself or specifically for the prayer? The ruling's practical consequences affect the virtue of ghusl for various categories of people.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four occasions for sunnah ghusl
List the four events: Friday prayer, Eid prayers, entering ihram, and standing at Arafah after noon.
These are the core sunnah ghusl occasions in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the sixteen mustahabb occasions
The passage mentions that ghusl is mustahabb for sixteen things, but only one example is given: one who becomes Muslim while pure.
The other fifteen are not listed here; the focus shifts to the dispute.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on Friday ghusl
Al-Hasan (Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds it is for the day, while Abu Yusuf holds it is for the prayer. Understand each position.
This is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the dalil for each position
Al-Hasan cites the hadith 'The master of days is Friday' to argue the day's virtue. Abu Yusuf argues that the prayer is more excellent and purification is tied to prayer.
Both use valid reasoning; the relied-upon view favors Abu Yusuf.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Scenarios: one who breaks wudu after ghusl; those not obligated for Friday (travelers, women, etc.). Abu Yusuf says no sunnah ghusl for them; al-Hasan says yes.
The practical difference determines who should perform ghusl and whether the virtue is retained.

فصل [الأشياء التي يسن لها الاغتسال]
يُسن الاغتسال لأربعة أشياء: صلاة الجمعة وصلاة العيدين، وللإحرام، وللحاج في عرفة بعد الزوال.
ويندب الاغتسال في ستة عشر شيئاً: لمن أسلم طاهراً .
ويدلك مع عند من للحج أو للعمرة الجمعة
الدلك وهو إمرار اليد على الأعضاء مع غسلها [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠٥] كشف العورة: فإن كان مستوراً فلا بأس به [مراقي الفلاح: ١٠٦] صلاة الجمعة: اعلم أن هذا الاغتسال لليوم عند الحسن؛ إظهاراً لفضيلته على سائر الأيام على ما قاله سيد الأنام عليها: "سيد الأيام يوم الجمعة". وقال أبو يوسف: هو للصلاة وهو الأصح ، وإليه يشير ظاهر الكتاب؛ لأنها أفضل من الوقت، ولأن الطهارة تختص بها، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيمن اغتسل يوم الجمعة ثم أحدث وتوضأ وصلى الجمعة لا يكون له فضل من اغتسل يوما أبي يوسف وعنده يكون له فضله، أو اغتسل بعد الصلاة قبل الغروب، أو كان ممن لا تجب عليه الجمعة كأهل البرية والمسافر والمرأة والعبد، فإنه لا يسن الاغتسال في حقهم عنده خلافاً للحسن. [تبيين الحقائق: ۷۱/۱] وفي "الطحطاوي": الغسل لليوم قاله محمد، ونسبه كثير إلى الحسن، وذكر في "المحيط" محمداً مع الحسن، وقال أيضاً: وأما الغسل بعد الصلاة فليس بمعتبر إجماعا . صلاة العيدين هذا الغسل سنة للصلاة في قول أبي يوسف كما في الجمعة، ولليوم عند الحسن، نقله "القهستاني". [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ۱۰۷] وللحاج: شرط سنية الاغتسال للحاج احترازاً عن غيره، وكونه بعد الزوال لفصل زمان الوقوف طاهرا عن جنابة وحيض ونفاس احترز به عمن أسلم غير طاهر؛ فإنه يفترض عليه الغسل على المعتمد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۸]
Section on things for which ghusl is sunnah: Ghusl is sunnah for four things: Friday prayer, the two 'Eid prayers, for ihram, and for the pilgrim at 'Arafah after noon. And ghusl is mustahabb for sixteen things: for one who becomes Muslim while pure. ... [corrupt line] Rubbing is passing the hand over the limbs while washing them [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 105] Uncovering the 'awrah: if it is covered, no problem [Maraqi al-Falah: 106]. Friday prayer: know that this ghusl is for the day according to al-Hasan, to show its virtue over other days as the Master of mankind said: "The master of days is Friday." Abu Yusuf said: it is for the prayer, and that is more correct, and the apparent [meaning] of the book indicates it, because the prayer is more virtuous than the time, and because purification is specific to it. The practical consequence appears in one who performs ghusl on Friday then breaks wudu and performs wudu and prays Friday: he does not get the virtue of ghusl according to Abu Yusuf, but according to al-Hasan he does. Or if he performs ghusl after the prayer before sunset, or for those on whom Friday is not obligatory like desert dwellers, traveler, woman, and slave, then ghusl is not sunnah for them according to him, contrary to al-Hasan. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/71] And in al-Tahtawi: ghusl for the day was said by Muhammad, and many attributed it to al-Hasan, and in al-Muhit he mentioned Muhammad with al-Hasan. He also said: as for ghusl after the prayer, it is not considered by consensus. 'Eid prayer: this ghusl is sunnah for the prayer according to Abu Yusuf as in Friday, and for the day according to al-Hasan, as al-Qahistani reported. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 107] For the pilgrim: the condition for sunniyyah of ghusl for the pilgrim is to exclude others, and it being after noon to separate the time of standing, pure from janabah, hayd, and nifas. This excludes one who becomes Muslim while impure, for ghusl is obligatory for him on the relied-upon view. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 108]
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage first states that ghusl is sunnah for four major occasions: Friday prayer, 'Eid prayers, entering the state of ihram (for Hajj/Umrah), and for the pilgrim at 'Arafah after noon. Then it mentions that ghusl is mustahabb (recommended) for sixteen other occasions, but only one is listed here: one who becomes Muslim while pure. The commentary focuses on the dispute regarding Friday ghusl: according to Imam al-Hasan (Muhammad al-Shaybani), the ghusl is for the day itself, emphasizing the virtue of Friday. According to Abu Yusuf, it is for the prayer, because the prayer is more excellent than the time. This difference has practical consequences: if a person performs ghusl on Friday but then invalidates his wudu and only performs wudu before prayer, according to Abu Yusuf he loses the virtue of the ghusl, while according to al-Hasan he retains it because the ghusl was for the day. Also, those not obligated to pray Friday (e.g., travelers, women, slaves) do not have this ghusl sunnah according to Abu Yusuf, but al-Hasan says it is sunnah for the day even for them. For 'Eid, similarly Abu Yusuf holds it is for the prayer, al-Hasan for the day. For the pilgrim at 'Arafah, the ghusl is specifically for the pilgrim after noon, and it is conditioned on being pure from janabah, etc. If one becomes Muslim while impure, ghusl becomes obligatory on the reliable opinion.

Key Terms
يسن (yusannu): It is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
يندب (yundabu): It is mustahabb (recommended but less emphasized than sunnah).
الأصح (al-ashah): The more correct view (in the madhhab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Hasan's view that it is for the day is more correct.
B) Abu Yusuf's view that it is for the prayer is more correct.
C) Both views are equally strong; no tarjih.
D) The dispute is only about 'Eid, not Friday.

Key Takeaway
The recommendation for Friday ghusl is subject to an intra-Hanafi dispute: it is either for the day or for the prayer, affecting who should perform it and whether the virtue remains after breaking wudu.

The Etiquette and Disliked Acts of Ghusl
States adab of ghusl follow wudu except facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the etiquette of ghusl, identify the exception regarding facing the qibla, and list the disliked acts common to both wudu and ghusl.

Core Idea
Ghusl shares wudu's etiquette except facing qibla — awrah exposure overrides the recommendation.

This passage from Nur al-Idah provides a concise rule: all the recommended acts (adab) of wudu are also recommended for ghusl, except facing the qibla. The reason is that ghusl typically involves uncovering the awrah, which makes facing the qibla disliked (makruh). Similarly, all disliked acts in wudu are also disliked in ghusl. Understanding this rule helps avoid confusion and ensures proper practice of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
The passage links the adab of ghusl to those of wudu. Recognize that the rule is one of transfer: most of the wudu's etiquettes apply directly to ghusl.
2
List the shared adab
Recall the sunan of wudu from previous study: intention (niyyah), basmalah, washing hands thrice, rinsing mouth, sniffing water, using miswak, etc. These are all included in ghusl's adab.
The text does not list them explicitly but confirms the equivalence.
3
Pinpoint the exception
The passage explicitly states that facing the qibla is not part of ghusl's adab. Identify this as the sole exception.
4
Understand the rationale
The exception is due to the general principle that it is disliked to face the qibla while uncovering the awrah. Ghusl often involves nudity, so the recommendation is dropped.
The phrase 'غالبا مع كشف العورة' indicates the typical scenario.
5
Apply the rule for makruhat
Whatever is considered makruh (disliked) in wudu — such as extravagance in water, talking, spitting in water — is equally makruh in ghusl.
The level of karahah (tanzihi or tahrimi) remains the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في آداب الاغتسال ومكروهاته. وآداب الاغتسال هي آداب الوضوء إلا أنه لا يستقبل القبلة؛ لأنه يكون غالبا مع كشف العورة، وكره فيه ما كره في الوضوء.
Chapter on the Etiquette of Ghusl and Its Disliked Acts. The etiquette of ghusl is the etiquette of wudu except that one does not face the qibla because it is usually with uncovering the awrah, and what is disliked in wudu is disliked in it.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah. It establishes that the recommended behaviors (adab) for performing ghusl are the same as those for wudu, with one exception: facing the qibla is not recommended during ghusl because the awrah is typically exposed. The exception is due to the general principle that it is disliked to face the qibla while in a state of nudity. Similarly, all actions that are makruh (disliked) in wudu, such as extravagance in water usage, are also makruh in ghusl.

Key Terms

Occasions for Recommended Ghusl and the Friday Ghusl Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Friday ghusl with list of sunnah and mandub occasions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the Friday ghusl (al-Hasan vs. Abu Yusuf) and state the mufta bihi position with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Friday ghusl is for the prayer, not the day — that is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This lesson examines the occasions for which ghusl is recommended in the Hanafi school: four strongly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah) and sixteen encouraged (mandub). Within the school, there is a significant dispute about the Friday ghusl: is it for the day or for the prayer? The commentary explains both views and settles on Abu Yusuf's position. We will work through the dispute and apply it to practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnah ghusl occasions
Read the first part of the passage and list the four occasions: Friday prayer, Eid prayer, entering ihram, and standing at Arafah after midday.
Note that these are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Understand the sixteenn mandub occasions
Read the second part listing sixteen encouraged occasions, including conversion while pure, puberty, recovery from insanity, cupping, etc.
These are sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on Friday ghusl
Focus on the commentary: al-Hasan (and according to some, Muhammad) holds the ghusl is for the day; Abu Yusuf holds it is for the prayer. Note the reasoning for each.
Abu Yusuf's view is called 'al-ashah' (most correct).
4
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah)
Consider a person who performs ghusl on Friday, then breaks wudu and does wudu for prayer. According to Abu Yusuf, he misses the virtue; according to al-Hasan, he still gets it. Also, those not obligated to pray Friday (women, travelers) do not get the sunnah according to Abu Yusuf.
This shows the difference in application.
5
State the mufta bihi and evidence
The relied-upon view is Abu Yusuf's: ghusl is for the prayer. Evidence: prayer is superior to time, purification is specific to worship, and ghusl after prayer is invalid by consensus.
The text's apparent meaning also supports this.

[مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۸])، ولمن أفاق من جنون (لعل سنيته للشكر على نعمة الإفاقة. Ghusl is sunnah for four things: Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, for ihram, and for the pilgrim at Arafah after midday. [Commentary on uncovering awrah...]. Friday prayer: Know that this ghusl is for the day according to al-Hasan, to show its virtue over other days as the Prophet said: 'The master of days is Friday.' Abu Yusuf said: It is for the prayer, and that is more correct, and the apparent text indicates that because prayer is superior to time, and purification is specific to it. The practical consequence of the difference appears in one who performs ghusl on Friday then breaks wudu and performs wudu and prays Friday: he does not have the virtue of one who performed ghusl on that day according to Abu Yusuf, while according to al-Hasan he has its virtue; or if he performed ghusl after prayer before sunset, or if he is one for whom Friday is not obligatory, like desert dwellers, travelers, women, and slaves, then ghusl is not sunnah for them according to him, contrary to al-Hasan... And it is recommended (mandub) to perform ghusl in sixteen things: for one who becomes Muslim while pure (pure from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, as opposed to one who becomes Muslim while impure, for whom ghusl is obligatory according to the relied-upon view); for one who reaches puberty by age (which is fifteen years according to the fatwa for both male and female, as opposed to reaching puberty by wet dream, impregnation, or ejaculation, or for females by wet dream, menstruation, or pregnancy, as ghusl is obligatory in those cases); for one who recovers from insanity; at cupping; for washing a deceased person; on the Night of Bara'ah (which is the night of mid-Sha'ban, so named because Allah writes for every believer a release from the Fire to fulfill his rights and because of the forgiveness of sins); on the Night of Qadr if one sees it; for entering the city of the Prophet ﷺ; for standing at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Sacrifice; upon entering Makkah; for Tawaf al-Ziyarah; for eclipse prayer, rain prayer, fear, darkness, and severe wind.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with extensive commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, presents the occasions for which ghusl is either sunnah mu'akkadah (strongly recommended) or mandub (encouraged). The passage first lists four sunnah occasions: Friday prayer, the two Eids, entering ihram, and standing at Arafah for the pilgrim after midday. The commentary then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the Friday ghusl: al-Hasan (likely al-Basri, but some attribute to Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that it is for the day itself, while Abu Yusuf holds it is for the prayer. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's, as it aligns with the text and the principle that purification is tied to the act of worship. The practical difference affects whether those who are not obligated to pray Friday (e.g., women, travelers) can obtain the virtue, or if performing ghusl after prayer still counts. The passage then lists sixteen mandub occasions, with commentary clarifying the definition of 'pure' for the convert, the age of majority, and the virtue of certain nights.

Key Terms
طاهراً (tāhiran): In the context of a convert, it means free from major impurity (janabah, hayd, nifas).
بلوغ بالسن (bulūgh bil-sinn): Reaching the age of legal majority (15 lunar years for both genders).
ليلة براءة (laylat al-barā’a): The night of mid-Sha'ban, when Allah grants release from Hellfire to believers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), for what reason is the sunnah ghusl on Friday performed?
A) For the day of Friday itself
B) For the Friday prayer
C) For entering the mosque
D) For listening to the khutbah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strongly recommends ghusl for Friday prayer (for the prayer, not the day), a position that shapes who is obligated and when the virtue is lost.

Recommended Baths and Age of Puberty
Lists occasions for sunnah ghusl and determines age of majority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the occasions for sunnah ghusl and state the Hanafi ruling on the age of puberty.

Core Idea
Sunnah ghusl is recommended on specific occasions; puberty is set at 15 years by age, but other signs make ghusl obligatory.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists a number of occasions where performing a full body wash (ghusl) is a confirmed sunnah. It also clarifies the age of legal puberty in the Hanafi school: fifteen years for both boys and girls. Understanding these rulings helps you distinguish between recommended and obligatory purification, and ensures you know when the obligations of adulthood begin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasions for sunnah ghusl
Read through the list in the Arabic text and note each event: reaching puberty by age, recovery from insanity, cupping, washing the deceased, the night of Bara'ah, seeing Laylat al-Qadr, entering Madinah, standing at Muzdalifah, entering Makkah, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and prayers for eclipse, rain, fear, darkness, and severe wind.
These are occasions where ghusl is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Note the exception for other signs of puberty
The passage contrasts 'by age' with other signs of puberty: wet dream, impregnating, ejaculation for boys, and wet dream, menstruation, pregnancy for girls. For those signs, ghusl becomes obligatory (fard/wajib), not just sunnah.
The mention of 'by age' is specifically for the case where no other sign has appeared before age 15.
3
Memorize the relied-upon age of puberty
The text explicitly states 'على المفتى به' indicating that fifteen years is the operative ruling for fatwa. This applies to both male and female.
This is a fixed maximum; if signs appear earlier, the ruling is based on the sign, not age.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
ما يسن له الغسل
ولمن بلغ بالسّن ولمن أفاق من جنون، وعند حجامة، وغسل ميت، وفي ليلة براءة،
وليلة القدر إذا رآها ولدخول مدينة النبي، وللوقوف بمزدلفة غداة يوم النحر،
باتباع ما ورد في وقتها بعد طلوع فجره
وعند دخول مكة ولطواف الزيارة، ولصلاة كسوف واستسقاء، وفزع، وظلمة،
وريح شديدة.
يطلب استنزال الغيث
بالسن وهو خمس عشرة سنة على المفتى به في الغلام والجارية، واحترز به عن بلوغ الصبي بالاحتلام والإحبال والإنزال، وعن بلوغ الصبية بالاحتلام والحيض والحبل؛ فإنه لابد من الغسل فيها. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۰۸] لمن أفاق إلخ لعل سنيته للشكر على نعمة الإفاقة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠٨] ليلة براءة: وهي ليلة النصف من شعبان؛ سميت بذلك لأن الله تعالى يكتب لكل مؤمن براءة من النار؛ لتوفية ما عليه من الحقوق، ولما فيها من البراءة من الذنوب بغفرانها [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ١٠٨]
Book of Purification. What ghusl is sunnah for: For one who reaches puberty by age, and for one who recovers from insanity, and at cupping, and washing the deceased, and on the night of Bara'ah, and Laylat al-Qadr if he sees it, and for entering the city of the Prophet ﷺ, and for standing at Muzdalifa on the morning of the day of sacrifice, following what is reported at its time after dawn, and upon entering Makkah and for the Tawaf of visitation, and for solar eclipse prayer, rain prayer, fear prayer, darkness, and severe wind. Resorting to descent of rain. By age: it is fifteen years according to the relied-upon position for a boy and girl. He guarded against the puberty of a boy by wet dream, impregnating, and ejaculation, and against the puberty of a girl by wet dream, menstruation, and pregnancy; for in these ghusl is necessary. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 108] 'For one who recovers' etc., perhaps its preferability is thankfulness for the blessing of recovery. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 108] Night of Bara'ah: it is the night of the middle of Sha'ban; so named because Allah Almighty writes for every believer a discharge from the Fire, to fulfill what is due upon him, and because it contains discharge from sins by their forgiveness. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 108]
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Purification. It first lists occasions when performing ghusl is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), such as for one who reaches puberty by age (fifteen years), recovery from insanity, cupping, washing the deceased, the night of Bara'ah (15th of Sha'ban), seeing Laylat al-Qadr, entering Madinah, standing at Muzdalifah on the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, entering Makkah, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and prayers for eclipse, rain, fear, during darkness, and strong winds. The phrase 'resorting to descent of rain' is unclear here but may relate to the rain prayer. Then it clarifies that the sunnah ghusl for 'reaching puberty by age' is specifically when one reaches fifteen years, which is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position for both boys and girls. This distinguishes from other ways of reaching puberty (wet dream, etc.) where ghusl becomes obligatory (fard). The passage also includes footnotes explaining the night of Bara'ah.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full-body ritual washing; here it is sunnah for specific occasions.
السن (al-sinn): Age of puberty; here set at 15 years for both genders.
الاحتلام (al-ihtilam): Wet dream, a sign of puberty that makes ghusl obligatory.
ليلة براءة (laylat al-bara'ah): Night of the middle of Sha'ban; ghusl is sunnah.
ليلة القدر (laylat al-qadr): Night of power; ghusl is sunnah if one sees it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 12 years
B) 15 years
C) 18 years
D) 10 years

Key Takeaway
Sunnah ghusl is meritorious on specific occasions; the age of puberty is 15 years for both genders, but other signs trigger obligatory ghusl.
