Definition and Eight Conditions of Tayammum
Defines tayammum and lists its conditions with emphasis on niyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tayammum and list its eight conditions, explaining the role of intention.

Core Idea
Tayammum is a substitute purification; its validity depends on eight conditions, beginning with intention.

This lesson establishes the foundational definition of tayammum as a dry purification substitute. We examine why it follows water purification in the text, its linguistic and legal meanings, and the eight conditions that must be fulfilled for it to be valid. Special attention is given to the first condition—intention (niyyah)—and its own sub-conditions.

Guided Path
1
Define tayammum
Identify the linguistic meaning (absolute intention) and the legal definition (wiping face and hands with pure earth). Note that it is a substitute (khalaf) for wudu/ghusl.
2
Locate tayammum in the text structure
Understand why the author placed tayammum after water purification and before wiping khuffs: tayammum is established by the Quran, wiping khuffs by Sunnah.
3
List the eight conditions
Enumerate the eight conditions mentioned in the matn. The first is niyyah; the rest are implied from the commentary (Islam, tamyiz, knowledge, pure earth, striking, wiping, proper intention).
4
Examine sub-conditions for niyyah
Identify the three requirements for a valid intention: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends.
5
Specify permissible intentions
For tayammum to permit salah, the intention must be either purification (taharah) or making prayer permissible (istibahah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم
[شروط صحته]
يصح بشروط ثمانية: الأول: النية، وحقيقتها عقد القلب على الفعل، ووقتها شرعا أي إيجاد الفعل جزما
النية عند ضرب يده على ما يتيمم به، وشروط صحة النية ثلاثة: الإسلام، والتمييز، والعلم بما ينويه
ويشترط لصحة نية التيمم للصلاة به أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما نية الطهارة، أو استباحة الصلاة.
باب: ذكره بعد طهارة الماء؛ لأنه خلف، وقدمه على مسح الخف وإن كان طهارة مائية؛ لثبوت هذا بالكتاب وذاك بالسنة، وثلث به تأتياً بالكتاب [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١١]
التيمم هو لغة: القصد مطلقاً، والحج لغة: القصد إلى معظم، وشرعاً: مسح الوجه واليدين عن صعيد مطهر، والقصد شرط له؛ لأنه النية. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١١]
مسح
ثم اعلم أن التيمم لم يكن مشروعاً لغير هذه الأمة، وإنما شرع رخصة لنا، والرخصة فيه من حيث الآلة حيث اكتفى بالصعيد الذي هو ملوث، وفي محله حيث اكتفى بشطر أعضاء الوضوء. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١١٦/١]
ضرب يده أو عند أعضائه بتراب أصابها. الإسلام أي كون الناوي للتيمم مسلماً. (محمد إعزاز علي)
والتمييز: أي كون الصبي مميزاً لفهم ما يتكلم به. (محمد إعزاز علي)
الطهارة أطلقها فشمل ما إذا نوى المتيمم المحدث الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو نوى الغسل، أو نوى المتيمم الجنب الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو الطهارة من الجنابة. قال الزيلعي: ولا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء جاز. وذكر الجصاص: أنه لابد من التمييز؛ لأن التيمم لهما يقع على صفة واحدة، فيتميز بالنية كصلاة الفرض. وليس بصحيح؛ لأن الحاجة إلى النية ليقع طهارة، فإذا وقع طهارة جاز له أن يؤدي به ما شاء؛ لأن الشروط يراعى وجودها لا غير، ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر يجوز له أن يؤدي به الظهر، بخلاف الصلاة حيث لا تتأدى إلا بالتعيين. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٢٤]
أو استباحة: أي نوى بالتيمم أن تكون الصلاة مباحة أو صيرورة الصلاة مباحة، فالسين والتاء زائدتان أو للصيرورة، ولا يصح للطلب. وصرحوا بأنه لو تيمم لدخول المسجد أو للقراءة ولو من المصحف، أو مسه، أو زيارة القبور، أو دفن الميت، أو الأذان أو الإقامة، أو السلام أو رده، أو الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة بذلك التيمم عند عامة المشائخ، إلا من شذ، وهو أبو بكر بن سعيد البلخي. [فتح القدير: ١١٤/١]
Chapter of Tayammum. [Conditions of its validity] It is valid with eight conditions: First: intention (niyyah), and its reality is resolve of the heart on the action, and its time legally is when he strikes his hands on what he performs tayammum with. Conditions of the validity of intention are three: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what he intends. For the validity of the intention of tayammum for prayer with it, one of three things is required: either intention of purification (taharah), or making prayer permissible (istibahah al-salat). 'Bab': He mentioned it after purification with water because it is a substitute, and he gave it precedence over wiping over the khuffs even though that is a water purification, because this (tayammum) is established by the Book and that by the Sunnah, and he arranged it to follow the Book. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 111] Tayammum linguistically: absolute intention. Hajj linguistically: intention to go to a great place. Legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth; intention is a condition for it because it is the niyyah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 111] Wiping. Then know that tayammum was not legislated for any other than this ummah; it was legislated as a concession for us. The concession in it is regarding the instrument where pure earth which is dirty suffices, and in its extent where a portion of the limbs of wudu suffices. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/116] Striking his hand or his limbs with earth that touched them. Islam: meaning the one intending tayammum must be Muslim. (Muhammad I'zaz Ali) Discernment: meaning the child must be discerning to understand what he says. (Muhammad I'zaz Ali) Purification is absolute, so it includes if the one with minor impurity intends purification from minor impurity or intends ghusl, or if the one in major impurity intends purification from minor impurity or from major impurity. Al-Zayla'i said: Distinguishing between minor and major impurity is not required, such that if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu, it is valid. Al-Jassas mentioned: Distinguishing is necessary because tayammum for both occurs in one form, so it is distinguished by intention like the fard prayer. But it is not correct because the need for intention is for it to occur as purification; when it occurs as purification, he may perform with it whatever he wishes, because conditions are observed for their existence only. Do you not see that if he performs tayammum for 'Asr, he may perform with it Zuhr, unlike prayer where it is not fulfilled except with specification. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 124] Or istibahah: i.e., he intends with tayammum that prayer becomes permissible, or the becoming of prayer permissible; the sin and ta are extraneous or for becoming, and it is not valid for request. They explicitly stated that if he performs tayammum for entering the mosque, or for recitation even from the mushaf, or touching it, or visiting graves, or burying the deceased, or the adhan or iqamah, or greeting or returning it, or Islam, prayer is not permissible with that tayammum according to the majority of the mashayikh, except for one who is aberrant, Abu Bakr ibn Sa'id al-Balkhi. [Fath al-Qadir: 1/114]
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on Tayammum in the book. It is a definition and ruling statement with expansion from the commentary. First, it notes why tayammum is placed after purification with water: it is a substitute (khalaf), and the author gave it precedence over wiping khuffs because tayammum is established by the Quran (verse 5:6) while wiping khuffs is by Sunnah. Then it defines tayammum: literally 'intention', and legally 'wiping the face and hands with pure earth'. Intention (niyyah) is a condition for it. It then details that tayammum is valid with eight conditions, and enumerates the first condition: niyyah. It explains the reality of niyyah, its time (at striking hands), and its own three sub-conditions: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. For the intention of tayammum to permit salah, it must be either for purification (taharah) or for making salah permissible (istibahah al-salah). The passage then discusses a scholarly dispute: Al-Zayla'i (Hanafi) holds that one need not distinguish between major and minor impurity in the intention; if a junub intends wudu, it suffices. Al-Jassas required distinction. The text sides with Zayla'i, arguing that once purification occurs, it suffices for any act, analogizing to the case of performing tayammum for one prayer and then using it for another. Finally, it clarifies that if one intends tayammum for acts other than salah (e.g., entering mosque, reciting Quran), the tayammum does not permit salah according to the general body of scholars, except Abu Bakr al-Balkhi's minority view.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl.
النية (al-niyyah): Resolve of the heart; its time is at striking hands. For tayammum, it must be for taharah or istibahah.
استباحة الصلاة (istibahah al-salah): Intending to make prayer permissible. This is one of the valid intentions for tayammum.
التمييز (al-tamyiz): Discernment, the child's ability to understand speech. A condition for valid intention.
الطهارة (al-taharah): Purification; includes both minor and major impurity in the context of intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many conditions are required for the validity of tayammum according to this passage?
A) Five
B) Eight
C) Three
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a substitute purification with eight conditions; intention is the first and must be for purification or making prayer permissible.

Intention (Niyyah) for Tayammum: Sub-Conditions and the Dispute on Specifying Impurity
Details the sub-conditions of niyyah and the intra-Hanafi dispute on distinguishing impurity types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three sub-conditions of intention for tayammum, apply the ruling on distinguishing major/minor impurity, and evaluate the dispute between Al-Zayla'i and Al-Jassas.

Core Idea
For tayammum, intention must be for purification or istibahah; one need not distinguish between minor and major impurity.

This lesson delves into the first condition of tayammum—intention (niyyah). It explores the three sub-conditions required for a valid intention: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. It then examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Al-Zayla'i and Al-Jassas regarding whether one must distinguish between minor and major impurity when intending purification. The text adopts Al-Zayla'i's view, and we analyze the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sub-conditions for valid intention
From the text: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. Understand how each applies.
Tamyiz means the child understands speech; age 7 is typical.
2
Distinguish permissible intentions
For tayammum to permit salah, intention must be either taharah (purification) or istibahah (making permissible). Note that taharah is absolute and includes both minor and major impurity.
3
Analyze the dispute on distinguishing impurity types
Al-Zayla'i says no distinction needed; Al-Jassas requires it. Identify each position and their proofs.
Al-Jassas analogizes to fard prayer requiring specification; Al-Zayla'i analogizes to tayammum for one prayer sufficing for another.
4
Examine the Hanafi response and tarjih
The text declares Al-Zayla'i's view correct, arguing that the need for intention is simply for the act to be purification; once attained, it suffices for any act.
5
Understand practical implications
Tayammum performed for other purposes (e.g., entering mosque, reciting Quran) does not permit salah, per the majority of mashayikh, except the aberrant view of Abu Bakr al-Balkhi.

Source Text

يصح بشروط ثمانية: الأول: النية، وحقيقتها عقد القلب على الفعل، ووقتها شرعا أي إيجاد الفعل جزما
النية عند ضرب يده على ما يتيمم به، وشروط صحة النية ثلاثة: الإسلام، والتمييز، والعلم بما ينويه
ويشترط لصحة نية التيمم للصلاة به أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما نية الطهارة، أو استباحة الصلاة.
باب: ذكره بعد طهارة الماء؛ لأنه خلف، وقدمه على مسح الخف وإن كان طهارة مائية؛ لثبوت هذا بالكتاب وذاك بالسنة، وثلث به تأتياً بالكتاب [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١١]
التيمم هو لغة: القصد مطلقاً، والحج لغة: القصد إلى معظم، وشرعاً: مسح الوجه واليدين عن صعيد مطهر، والقصد شرط له؛ لأنه النية. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١١]
مسح
ثم اعلم أن التيمم لم يكن مشروعاً لغير هذه الأمة، وإنما شرع رخصة لنا، والرخصة فيه من حيث الآلة حيث اكتفى بالصعيد الذي هو ملوث، وفي محله حيث اكتفى بشطر أعضاء الوضوء. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١١٦/١]
ضرب يده أو عند أعضائه بتراب أصابها. الإسلام أي كون الناوي للتيمم مسلماً. (محمد إعزاز علي)
والتمييز: أي كون الصبي مميزاً لفهم ما يتكلم به. (محمد إعزاز علي)
الطهارة أطلقها فشمل ما إذا نوى المتيمم المحدث الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو نوى الغسل، أو نوى المتيمم الجنب الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو الطهارة من الجنابة. قال الزيلعي: ولا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء جاز. وذكر الجصاص: أنه لابد من التمييز؛ لأن التيمم لهما يقع على صفة واحدة، فيتميز بالنية كصلاة الفرض. وليس بصحيح؛ لأن الحاجة إلى النية ليقع طهارة، فإذا وقع طهارة جاز له أن يؤدي به ما شاء؛ لأن الشروط يراعى وجودها لا غير، ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر يجوز له أن يؤدي به الظهر، بخلاف الصلاة حيث لا تتأدى إلا بالتعيين. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٢٤]
أو استباحة: أي نوى بالتيمم أن تكون الصلاة مباحة أو صيرورة الصلاة مباحة، فالسين والتاء زائدتان أو للصيرورة، ولا يصح للطلب. وصرحوا بأنه لو تيمم لدخول المسجد أو للقراءة ولو من المصحف، أو مسه، أو زيارة القبور، أو دفن الميت، أو الأذان أو الإقامة، أو السلام أو رده، أو الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة بذلك التيمم عند عامة المشائخ، إلا من شذ، وهو أبو بكر بن سعيد البلخي. [فتح القدير: ١١٤/١]
Chapter of Tayammum. [Conditions of its validity] It is valid with eight conditions: First: intention (niyyah), and its reality is resolve of the heart on the action, and its time legally is when he strikes his hands on what he performs tayammum with. Conditions of the validity of intention are three: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what he intends. For the validity of the intention of tayammum for prayer with it, one of three things is required: either intention of purification (taharah), or making prayer permissible (istibahah al-salat). 'Bab': He mentioned it after purification with water because it is a substitute, and he gave it precedence over wiping over the khuffs even though that is a water purification, because this (tayammum) is established by the Book and that by the Sunnah, and he arranged it to follow the Book. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 111] Tayammum linguistically: absolute intention. Hajj linguistically: intention to go to a great place. Legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth; intention is a condition for it because it is the niyyah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 111] Wiping. Then know that tayammum was not legislated for any other than this ummah; it was legislated as a concession for us. The concession in it is regarding the instrument where pure earth which is dirty suffices, and in its extent where a portion of the limbs of wudu suffices. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/116] Striking his hand or his limbs with earth that touched them. Islam: meaning the one intending tayammum must be Muslim. (Muhammad I'zaz Ali) Discernment: meaning the child must be discerning to understand what he says. (Muhammad I'zaz Ali) Purification is absolute, so it includes if the one with minor impurity intends purification from minor impurity or intends ghusl, or if the one in major impurity intends purification from minor impurity or from major impurity. Al-Zayla'i said: Distinguishing between minor and major impurity is not required, such that if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu, it is valid. Al-Jassas mentioned: Distinguishing is necessary because tayammum for both occurs in one form, so it is distinguished by intention like the fard prayer. But it is not correct because the need for intention is for it to occur as purification; when it occurs as purification, he may perform with it whatever he wishes, because conditions are observed for their existence only. Do you not see that if he performs tayammum for 'Asr, he may perform with it Zuhr, unlike prayer where it is not fulfilled except with specification. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 124] Or istibahah: i.e., he intends with tayammum that prayer becomes permissible, or the becoming of prayer permissible; the sin and ta are extraneous or for becoming, and it is not valid for request. They explicitly stated that if he performs tayammum for entering the mosque, or for recitation even from the mushaf, or touching it, or visiting graves, or burying the deceased, or the adhan or iqamah, or greeting or returning it, or Islam, prayer is not permissible with that tayammum according to the majority of the mashayikh, except for one who is aberrant, Abu Bakr ibn Sa'id al-Balkhi. [Fath al-Qadir: 1/114]
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on Tayammum in the book. It is a definition and ruling statement with expansion from the commentary. First, it notes why tayammum is placed after purification with water: it is a substitute (khalaf), and the author gave it precedence over wiping khuffs because tayammum is established by the Quran (verse 5:6) while wiping khuffs is by Sunnah. Then it defines tayammum: literally 'intention', and legally 'wiping the face and hands with pure earth'. Intention (niyyah) is a condition for it. It then details that tayammum is valid with eight conditions, and enumerates the first condition: niyyah. It explains the reality of niyyah, its time (at striking hands), and its own three sub-conditions: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. For the intention of tayammum to permit salah, it must be either for purification (taharah) or for making salah permissible (istibahah al-salah). The passage then discusses a scholarly dispute: Al-Zayla'i (Hanafi) holds that one need not distinguish between major and minor impurity in the intention; if a junub intends wudu, it suffices. Al-Jassas required distinction. The text sides with Zayla'i, arguing that once purification occurs, it suffices for any act, analogizing to the case of performing tayammum for one prayer and then using it for another. Finally, it clarifies that if one intends tayammum for acts other than salah (e.g., entering mosque, reciting Quran), the tayammum does not permit salah according to the general body of scholars, except Abu Bakr al-Balkhi's minority view.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Resolve of the heart; its time is at striking hands. For tayammum, it must be for taharah or istibahah.
استباحة الصلاة (istibahah al-salah): Intending to make prayer permissible. This is one of the valid intentions for tayammum.
التمييز (al-tamyiz): Discernment, the child's ability to understand speech. A condition for valid intention.
الطهارة (al-taharah): Purification; includes both minor and major impurity in the context of intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) regarding the need to distinguish between minor and major impurity when intending tayammum?
A) One must distinguish, as held by Al-Jassas.
B) One need not distinguish, as held by Al-Zayla'i.
C) One must distinguish for minor impurity only.
D) The text does not give a preference.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a general intention for purification (taharah) or making prayer permissible (istibahah) is sufficient for tayammum; specifying the type of impurity is not required.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Intention (Niyyah) as the First Condition of Tayammum
Ruling statement listing conditions for tayammum intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three subconditions for a valid intention in tayammum and identify which intentions for tayammum permit salah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention in tayammum must be for purification, making salah permissible, or a worship requiring purification.

Tayammum is a substitute purification when water is unavailable. Like wudu, it requires intention. But what exactly must one intend? This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out the first condition: intention, its subconditions, and the specific intentions that make tayammum valid for salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is tayammum, and the first condition is intention (niyyah). Note that intention is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn).
Intention is required for the validity of tayammum.
2
List the three subconditions for intention
The subconditions are: Islam (the person must be Muslim), discernment (tamyiz, understanding the intention), and knowledge of what one intends.
These ensure the intention is legally valid.
3
Enumerate the three valid intentions for tayammum to permit salah
The intention must be one of: (1) purification (taharah) from impurity, (2) making salah permissible (istibahah al-salah), or (3) a purposeful worship (ibadah maqsudah) that requires purification.
Any other intention, like entering a mosque, does not permit salah.
4
Identify invalid intentions
Examples from the text: tayammum for entering mosque, reciting Quran without being junub, touching mushaf, teaching others, etc. These do not permit salah.
The key is whether the intended act is a worship that requires purification.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Al-Zayla'i holds that distinguishing between minor and major impurity in intention is not required; al-Jassas argues it is necessary. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is al-Zayla'i's.
The principle: conditions are for existence, not specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم شروط صحته يصح بشروط ثمانية: الأول: النية، وحقيقتها عقد القلب على الفعل، ووقتها شرعا أي إيجاد الفعل جزما النية عند ضرب يده على ما يتيمم به وشروط صحة النية ثلاثة: الإسلام، والتمييز، والعلم بما ينويه ويشترط لصحة نية التيمم للصلاة به أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إما نية الطهارة، أو استباحة الصلاة . باب: ذكره بعد طهارة الماء؛ لأنه خلف، وقدمه على مسح الخف وإن كان طهارةً مائية؛ لثبوت هذا بالكتاب وذاك بالسنة، وثلث به تأتياً بالكتاب [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١١] التيمم هو لغة: القصد مطلقاً، والحج لغة: القصد إلى معظم، وشرعاً: مسح الوجه واليدين عن صعيد مطهر، والقصد شرط له؛ لأنه النية. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١١] مسح ثم اعلم أن التيمم لم يكن مشروعاً لغير هذه الأمة، وإنما شرع رخصةً لنا، والرخصة فيه من حيث الآلة حيث اكتفى بالصعيد الذي هو ملوث، وفي محله حيث اكتفى بشطر أعضاء الوضوء. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١١٦/١] ضرب يده أو عند أعضائه بتراب أصابها. الإسلام أي كون الناوي للتيمم مسلماً. (محمد إعزاز علي) والتمييز : أي كون الصبي مميزاً لفهم ما يتكلم .به محمد إعزاز علي الطهارة أطلقها فشمل ما إذا نوى المتيمم المحدث الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو نوى الغسل أو نوى المتيمم الجنب الطهارة من الحدث الأصغر أو الطهارة من الجنابة قال الزيلعي ولا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريد به الوضوء جاز، وذكر الجصاص: أنه لابد من التمييز ؛ لأن التيمم لهما يقع على صفة واحدة، فيتميز بالنية كصلاة الفرض، وليس بصحيح؛ لأن الحاجة إلى النية ليقع طهارة، فإذا وقع طهارة جاز له أن يؤدي به ما شاء؛ لأن الشروط يراعى وجودها لا غير ، ألا ترى أنه لو تيمم للعصر يجوز له أن يؤدي به الظهر، بخلاف الصلاة حيث لا تتأدى إلا بالتعيين تبيين الحقائق: ١٢٤] أو استباحة أي نوى بالتيمم أن تكون الصلاة مباحة أو صيرورة الصلاة مباحة، فالسين والتاء زائدتان أو للصيرورة، ولا يصح للطلب، وصرحوا بأنه لو تيمم لدخول المسجد أو للقراءة ولو من المصحف، أو مسه، أو زيارة القبور، أو دفن الميت، أو الأذان أو الإقامة، أو السلام أو رده، أو الإسلام لا تجوز الصلاة بذلك التيمم عند عامة المشائخ، إلا من شذ، وهو أبو بكر بن سعيد البلخي. [فتح القدير: ١١٤/١] صفة أو نية عبادة مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة، فلا يصلى به إذا نوى التيمم فقط موصوف أو نواه لقراءة القرآن ولم يكن جنباً. صفة إلخ وهي التي لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية، فتكون قد شرعت ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله تعالى كالصلاة، بخلاف المس فإنه وجب له بطريق التبع للتلاوة، وهو في الحقيقة ليس عبادة ولا يتقرب به ابتداءً ولا تصح ولا تحل بدون طهارة كقراءة القرآن لنحو الجنب فظهر أن المنوي لا يكون إلا صلاة أو جزء للصلاة في حد ذاته، أي بالنظر إلى ذاته، والمراد أنه جزء في الجملة، وإن كان يتحقق غير جزء لسبب آخر كالسجود، كقوله: نويت التيمم للصلاة، أو لصلاة الجنازة، أو سجدة التلاوة، أو لقراءة القرآن وهو جنب أو نوته لقراءة القرآن بعد انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها؛ لأن كلا منهما لابد له من الطهارة، وهو عبادة [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ١١٣] فلا يصلى به تفريع على اشتراط أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، أما عدم صحة الصلاة إذا نوى التيمم فقط، أي مجرداً من غير ملاحظة شيء مما تقدم، فظاهر؛ لفقدان الأمور الثلاثة المذكورة، وأما إذا تيمم لقراءة القرآن وهو محدث حدثاً أصغر ولم يكن جنباً؛ فلأنه وإن نوى عبادة مقصودة لكنها تصح بدون طهارة لغير الجنب. ومن ههنا ظهر أنه إذا تيمم الجنب لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجد أو تعليم الغير لا تجوز به صلاته، أما في الصورة الأولى فلفقد الشرط الأول فيه وهو كونه عبادة مقصودة، وأما في الثانية؛ فلأن دخول المسجد وإن كان لا يحل بدون طهارة من الحدث الأكبر إلا أنه ليس بعبادة، وأما في الثالثة؛ لأن تعليم الغير وإن كان عبادة مقصودة لكنه فقد فيه الشرط الثالث، وهو كونه لا يصح أو لا يحل بدون طهارة. فقط أي مجرداً من غير ملاحظة شيء مما تقدم
The Book of Purification. Chapter of Tayammum. [Conditions of Its Validity] It is valid with eight conditions: First: Intention, its reality is to bind the heart to the action, and its time legally is at the striking of the hand on what is used for tayammum. Conditions for the validity of intention are three: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. For the validity of intention of tayammum for prayer, one of three things is required: either the intention of purification (taharah), or of making prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah). Chapter: He mentioned it after water purification because it is a substitute, and he placed it before wiping over khuff, even though it is a water purification, because this is established by the Book and that by the Sunnah, and he began with it to follow the Book. Tayammum lexically means absolute intention, and hajj lexically means intention to a majestic place, and legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth, and intention is a condition for it because it is the intention. Then know that tayammum was not legislated for other than this nation, and it was legislated as a license for us, and the license regarding the instrument is that it suffices with earth which is impure, and regarding its scope is that it suffices with half the limbs of wudu. He strikes his hand or his limbs with earth that touches them. Islam: meaning that the one intending tayammum is Muslim. Tamyiz: meaning that the boy is discerning, understanding what he says. 'Taharah' is unrestricted so it includes if the one in need of tayammum intends purification from minor impurity or intends ghusl, or if the junub intends purification from minor impurity or from janabah. Al-Zayla'i said: It is not necessary to distinguish between hadath and janabah, so even if a junub performs tayammum intending wudu, it is permissible. Al-Jassas mentioned that distinction is necessary because tayammum for both occurs in one manner, so it is distinguished by intention like obligatory prayer, but this is not correct because the need for intention is to make it a purification, so if it occurs as a purification, it is permissible for him to perform with it whatever he wishes because conditions are observed for their existence only. Do you not see that if he performed tayammum for 'asr, it is permissible for him to perform dhuhr with it, unlike prayer which is not performed except with specification. Or 'istibahah' meaning he intended to make prayer permissible or the becoming of prayer permissible, so the sin and ta are extra or for becoming, and it is not valid for requesting. They explicitly stated that if he performs tayammum for entering the mosque, or for recitation even from the mushaf, or touching it, or visiting graves, or burying the dead, or the adhan or iqamah, or greeting or returning it, or Islam, his prayer is not permitted with that tayammum according to the general masters, except one who deviated: Abu Bakr ibn Sa'id al-Balkhi. 'Sifah' or 'or an intention of a purposeful worship that is not valid without purification.' So it is not prayed with if he intends tayammum only, described, or intends it for reciting Quran and he is not junub. 'Sifah' etc, which is that which is not obligatory within something else by way of following, so it is legislated initially as a means of drawing near to Allah like prayer, unlike touch which is obligatory for him by way of following for recitation, and it is in reality not a worship, nor does one draw near with it initially, and it is not valid nor permissible without purification, like reciting Quran for a junub. So it appears that the intended is only prayer or a part of prayer in itself, i.e., with respect to its essence, and what is meant is that it is a part in general, even if it is realized as non-part for another reason like prostration. For example, he says: I intend tayammum for prayer, or for funeral prayer, or for prostration of recitation, or for reciting Quran while junub, or she intends it for reciting Quran after the cessation of her menses or postpartum bleeding, because each of them necessarily requires purification, and it is a worship. So it is not prayed with, as a branch of requiring one of these three things. As for the invalidity of prayer if he intends tayammum only, i.e., bare without observing anything mentioned, it is apparent because of the absence of the three mentioned things. And if he performs tayammum for reciting Quran while having minor impurity and not being junub, because even though he intended a purposeful worship, it is valid without purification for other than the junub. From here it appears that if a junub performs tayammum for touching the mushaf, entering the mosque, or teaching others, his prayer is not permissible with it. As for the first case, because the first condition is lost: it being a purposeful worship. As for the second, because entering the mosque, even though it is not permissible without purification from major impurity, it is not a worship. As for the third, because teaching others, even though it is a purposeful worship, it lacks the third condition: that it is not valid or permissible without purification. 'Only' i.e., bare without observing anything preceding.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, providing the first condition for the validity of tayammum: intention (niyyah). The author defines intention as the binding of the heart to the act, and its time is at the moment of striking the hand on the earth for tayammum. Three subconditions are required for a valid intention: Islam (the person must be Muslim), discernment (tamyiz, i.e., being able to understand the intention), and knowledge of what one intends. Furthermore, for the tayammum to permit salah, the intention must be one of three: (1) intending purification (taharah) from either minor or major impurity, (2) intending to make prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah), or (3) intending a purposeful worship (ibadah maqsudah) that is not valid without purification, such as praying or reciting Quran for a junub. The text gives examples: if a junub intends tayammum for touching the mushaf, entering the mosque, or teaching others, the tayammum does not permit salah because these actions either are not worship or do not require purification. An intra-Hanafi difference is noted: al-Zayla'i holds that distinguishing between minor and major impurity is not required, while al-Jassas argues it is necessary; the preferred view is that of al-Zayla'i.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention of the heart to perform an act, specifically here the intention to perform tayammum as a purification.
تمييز (tamyiz): Discernment: the ability of a child to understand speech and the nature of the act intended.
استباحة الصلاة (istibahah al-salah): Intending to make prayer permissible by lifting the state of ritual impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following intentions for tayammum does NOT permit salah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Intending purification from janabah
B) Intending to make salah permissible
C) Intending to enter the mosque
D) Intending to recite the Quran while junub

Key Takeaway
The first condition of tayammum is intention; it must be for purification, making salah permissible, or a worship requiring purification; without such intention, salah is not permitted.

Taharah — Purification

The Excuse for Tayammum: Distance and City Rulings
Defines the mile and gives the city ruling for tayammum's excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a mile as the distance that excuses tayammum and identify the relied-upon ruling regarding tayammum inside a city.

Core Idea
A mile of distance from water permits tayammum, even inside a city — custom does not override the legal license.

This lesson clarifies the second condition for the validity of tayammum: the excuse of distance from water. We will first define the mile in traditional Hanafi units, then examine a key difference of opinion on whether tayammum is allowed inside a city. Understanding this dispute will help you apply the ruling correctly in both rural and urban settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse condition
Recognize that the absence of water is an excuse for tayammum, and the required distance is defined as a mile.
The text defines a mile in detail using cubits, handspans, fingers, barley grains.
2
Define the mile per Hanafi measurement
Memorize the hierarchical units: 1 mile = 1000 cubits, 1 cubit = 4 handspans, 1 handspan = 20 fingerwidths, 1 finger = 6 barley grains, 1 barley grain = 6 hairs from a mule's tail.
The last comparison is traditional, not critical for the ruling.
3
Note the dispute on tayammum in a city
Contrast the sahih view (tayammum allowed inside city if distance condition is met) with the view from Sharh al-Tahawi (restricted to emergencies).
4
Reconcile the two views
Understand that the restriction was based on the custom of cities where water was normally available, not on a fundamental legal difference. The relied-upon view is the broader one.
This is an example of 'urf (custom) influencing a ruling without altering the legal principle.

Source Text

ميلا ضبط بعضهم الميل والفرسخ والبريد في قوله: إن البريد من الفراسخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضعوا و الميل ألف أي . من ثم الذراع من الأصابع أربع من بعدها العشرون ثم الإصبع ست شعيرات فظهر شعرة منها إلى بطن الأخرى توضع الباعات قل والباع أربع أذرع فتتبعوا ثم الشعيرة ست شعرات فقط من ذيل بغل ليس عن ذا مرجع [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٤] ولو في المصر: أي ولو كان بعده عن ماء طهور في المصر، وهذا على الصحيح من المذهب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" أنه لا يجوز التيمم في المصر إلا لخوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد وللجنب من البرد، والحق الأول، والمنع بناء على عادة الأمصار، فليس خلافاً حقيقياً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥]
A mile: some scholars defined the mile, farsakh, and barid in his saying: 'Indeed the barid is four farsakhs, and a farsakh is three miles.' They placed the mile as one thousand [cubits]. Then the cubit is four handspans, after it twenty [fingers], then the finger is six barley grains, so a barley grain appears from one to the other, they place the paces, the pace is four cubits, so follow. Then the barley grain is only six hairs from the tail of a mule, not from this reference. And even in the city: i.e., even if his distance from pure water is in the city, and this is the correct (sahih) view in the madhhab. In 'Sharh al-Tahawi' it is stated that tayammum is not permitted in the city except for fear of missing a funeral or Eid prayer, and for the junub due to cold. The first view is correct, and the prohibition is based on the custom of cities, so it is not a real disagreement.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the sharh of Nur al-Idah, explaining the second condition for the validity of tayammum: the excuse (al-udhr al-mubih). Specifically, it details the definition of a mile—the distance that excuses one from using water—and discusses the ruling on tayammum within a city (al-misr). The text defines a mile as 1000 cubits, with the cubit being 4 handspans, the handspan 20 fingerwidths, the finger 6 barley grains, and the barley grain as 6 hairs from a mule's tail (though this is poetic). The relied-upon view (sahih) is that tayammum is permitted even inside a city if one is a mile away from water. However, an alternative view from 'Sharh al-Tahawi' restricts it to emergencies like missing a funeral or Eid prayer, or for a junub due to extreme cold. The commentary reconciles this by noting that the prohibition was based on the custom of cities, not a principled legal difference, the first view is correct.

Key Terms
ميل (mil): A unit of distance defined as 1000 cubits, approximately 1.6 km, used to determine the excuse for tayammum.
مصر (misr): A city or large town; here, a populated area with access to water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only if one fears missing a funeral or Eid prayer
B) Only for a junub suffering from extreme cold
C) Whenever one is a mile away from water, even inside the city
D) Tayammum is never permitted inside a city

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a valid license when water is a mile away, even inside a city, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Intention for Tayammum: Specifying the Worship
Explains the requirement of intention for a specific act needing purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct intention for tayammum and distinguish between valid and invalid intentions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tayammum's intention must target a specific worship that cannot be performed without purification – general intent is insufficient.

When using tayammum for prayer, it is not enough to merely intend purification. The Hanafi school requires that the intention be linked to a specific act of worship, such as prayer or recitation for a junub person. This lesson unpacks that condition from Nur al-Idah and clarifies common pitfalls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that the first condition for valid tayammum is the intention (niyyah) for a specific worship (ibada maqsuda).
The intention is a shart (condition), not a rukn.
2
Define ibada maqsuda
Understand that it is an act performed for its own sake as an act of drawing near to Allah, not as subordinate to another act. Examples include prayer, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation.
Touching the mus-haf is subordinate to recitation, so it is not an ibada maqsuda.
3
Apply to scenarios
Test different cases: a junub intending tayammum for reading Quran is valid; a person with minor impurity intending it for reading Quran is invalid because reading Quran is valid without purification for the non-junub.
For a junub, reading Quran requires purification, so it qualifies.
4
Identify invalid intentions
Recognize intentions that do not fulfill the condition: intending only tayammum, intending for touching mus-haf, entering mosque, or teaching others, because these are either not worship or do not require purification.
Entering mosque is not a worship in itself, so it lacks the 'ibada' element.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط صحة التيمم
صفة
أو نية عبادة مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة، فلا يصلى به إذا نوى التيمم فقط موصوف أو نواه لقراءة القرآن ولم يكن جنباً. الثاني: العذر المبيح للتيمم كبعده ميلاً عن ماء
ولو في المصرة

وفيها: الشرط الأول: أن ينوي الشخص عبادة مقصودة إلخ وهي التي لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية، فتكون قد شرعت ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله تعالى كالصلاة، بخلاف المس فإنه وجب له بطريق التبع للتلاوة، وهو في الحقيقة ليس عبادة ولا يتقرب به ابتداءً ولا تصح ولا تحل بدون طهارة كقراءة القرآن لنحو الجنب فظهر أن المنوي لا يكون إلا صلاة أو جزء للصلاة في حد ذاته، أي بالنظر إلى ذاته، والمراد أنه جزء في الجملة، وإن كان يتحقق غير جزء لسبب آخر كالسجود، كقوله: نويت التيمم للصلاة، أو لصلاة الجنازة، أو سجدة التلاوة، أو لقراءة القرآن وهو جنب أو نوته لقراءة القرآن بعد انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها؛ لأن كلا منهما لابد له من الطهارة، وهو عبادة [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ١٣١] فلا يصلى به تفريع على اشتراط أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، أما عدم صحة الصلاة إذا نوى التيمم فقط، أي مجرداً من غير ملاحظة شيء مما تقدم، فظاهر؛ لفقدان الأمور الثلاثة المذكورة، وأما إذا تيمم لقراءة القرآن وهو
محدث حدثاً أصغر ولم يكن جنباً؛ فلأنه وإن نوى عبادة مقصودة لكنها تصح بدون طهارة لغير الجنب. ومن ههنا ظهر أنه إذا تيمم الجنب لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجد أو تعليم الغير لا تجوز به صلاته، أما في الصورة الأولى فلفقد الشرط الأول فيه وهو كونه عبادة مقصودة، وأما في الثانية؛ فلأن دخول المسجد وإن كان لا يحل بدون طهارة من الحدث الأكبر إلا أنه ليس بعبادة، وأما في الثالثة؛ لأن تعليم الغير وإن كان عبادة مقصودة لكنه فقد فيه الشرط الثالث، وهو كونه لا يصح أو لا يحل بدون طهارة. فقط أي مجرداً من غير ملاحظة شيء مما تقدم
Conditions for validity of tayammum. Attribute: or intention of a specific worship that is not valid without purification. So one cannot pray with it if he intends only tayammum without specification, or intends it for reading Quran and he is not junub. Second: the excuse permitting tayammum, like being a mile away from water, even if in the city. The first condition: that the person intends a specific worship, which is that which is not obligated as part of something else by way of subordination, but rather is initiated as an act of drawing near to Allah, like prayer. Unlike touching (the mus-haf), which is obligated as subordinate to recitation, and is not actually a worship nor is it initiated as such, nor is it valid or permissible without purification, like reading Quran for the junub. So it appears that what is intended is only prayer or a part of prayer in itself, i.e., in consideration of its essence, meaning that it is a part in a general sense, even if it may be realized as non-part for another reason like prostration. So one says: I intend tayammum for prayer, or for funeral prayer, or for prostration of recitation, or for reading Quran while junub, or for reading Quran after her menstruation or postpartum bleeding ends; because each of these requires purification and is a worship. So one cannot pray with it, branching off from stipulating one of these three things. As for the invalidity of prayer if he intends only tayammum, i.e., devoid of considering any of the aforementioned, it is apparent due to the lack of the three mentioned things. And if he performs tayammum for reading Quran while he has minor impurity and is not junub, then because although he intended a specific worship, it is valid without purification for one who is not junub. From here it appears that if a junub performs tayammum for touching the mus-haf, or entering the mosque, or teaching others, his prayer is not valid by it. In the first case, due to lacking the first condition that it be a specific worship; in the second, because entering the mosque, although not permissible without purification from major impurity, is not a worship; in the third, because teaching others, although a specific worship, lacks the third condition that it is not valid or permissible without purification. Only i.e., devoid of considering any of the aforementioned.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage explains the first condition for tayammum to be valid for subsequent prayer: the intention (niyyah) must be for a specific worship that is not valid without purification. The worship must be 'maqsudah' (intentional), meaning it is performed as an act of drawing near to Allah, not as a subservient act like touching the mus-haf. Examples include prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, or reading Quran for a junub person. If one intends tayammum without specifying any such act, prayer is invalid. Similarly, tayammum for reading Quran by someone in minor impurity is insufficient because reading Quran is valid without purification for non-junub. For a junub, tayammum for touching mus-haf or entering mosque is not sufficient because those are not acts of worship in the required sense. The commentary elaborates that the intention must be for an act that is either prayer itself or a part of prayer, like prostration. The discussion highlights the Hanafi precision in defining 'ibadah maqsudah'.

Key Terms
نية عبادة مقصودة (niyyat 'ibada maqsuda): Intention for a specific act of worship that is not valid without purification and is performed for its own sake.
شروط صحة التيمم (shurut sihhat al-tayammum): Conditions that must be fulfilled for tayammum to be valid for subsequent worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'I intend tayammum for Dhuhr prayer'
B) 'I intend tayammum for prostration of recitation'
C) 'I intend tayammum for reading Quran' (performer is junub)
D) 'I intend tayammum for touching the mus-haf' (performer is junub)

Key Takeaway
Intention for tayammum must specify a worship that is not valid without purification; general or inappropriate intentions invalidate the tayammum for prayer.

Valid Excuse 1: Distance from Water
Establishes distance as a valid excuse and clarifies city ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distance threshold for tayammum and explain the Hanafi ruling when water is far, even within a city.

Core Idea
Distance from water (a mile or more) is a valid excuse for tayammum, even in a city.

The second condition for tayammum is the presence of a valid excuse (udhr mubih). Among the most commonly encountered excuses is being at a distance from a water source. This lesson explores the minimum distance required and the ruling when one is in a city but far from water, including a key intra-Hanafi difference on the matter.

Guided Path
1
Determine the distance threshold
Identify the distance that triggers the excuse: a mile or more from water. The text defines a mile as a thousand cubits (approx. 1.6 km).
The exact measurements may vary, but the principle is a significant distance.
2
Apply the standard for city dwelling
Even if one is in a city, if water is far (a mile or more), tayammum is allowed according to the correct view of the school (sahih).
3
Distinguish the opposing narration
Some narrations, notably in Sharh al-Tahawi, restrict the city excuse to special cases like fear of missing funeral prayer. The commentary explains this restriction is based on the custom ('urf) of cities where water is usually nearby, so it is not a real difference in principle.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The correct and relied-upon position is that tayammum is permissible for distance in the city. This is the operative fatwa.
Per Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الإدام
مرض: اعلم أن المريض أربعة أنواع من يضره الماء، أو التحرك لاستعماله، والثالث: من لا يضره شيء من ذلك، ولكن لا يقدر على الفعل بنفسه، فحاله لا يخلو إما يجد من يوضئه أو لا، فإن لم يجد جاز له التيمم إجماعاً ولو في المصر على ظاهر المذهب، وإن وجد فإما أن يكون من أهل طاعته كعبده وولده وأجيره أو لا، فإن كان أهل طاعته اختلف فيه المشائخ على قول الإمام بناءً على اختلاف الرواية عنه، وإن لم يكن من أهل طاعته و لم يعنه بغير بدل جاز له التيمم عنده مطلقاً. وقالا: لا يجوز في الفصول كلها، إلا إذا كان الأجر كثيراً، وهو ما زاد على ربع درهم، والرابع: من لا يقدر على الوضوء ولا على التيمم، لا بنفسه ولا بغيره قال بعضهم: لا يصلي على قياس قول الإمام حتى يقدر على أحدهما، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي تشبهاً ويعيد، وقول محمد مضطرب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥] وبرد: يشير إلى أنه يجوز للمحدث أيضًا حيث لم يشترط أن يكون جنباً، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. تبيين الحقائق (١١٩/١] وخوف أي إذا خاف من يريد التوضؤ أن يقتله عدو إن خرج إلى الغدير للتوضؤ. (محمد) إعزاز علي عدو أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان العدو آدميا أو غيره، وما إذا خافه على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، وما إذا خافت فاسقا عند الماء أو خاف المديون المفلس ،الحبس ولا إعادة عليهم ولا على من حبس في السفر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٦]
عطش: [أي إن خاف من عنده ماء إن صرفه في التوضؤ أن يهلكه العطش جاز له التيمم.] أطلقه فشمل ما إذا خاف حالا أو مآلا على نفسه أو رفيقه في القافلة أو دابته ولو كلبا وتعذر حفظ الغسالة لعدم الإناء، ولو أمكن حفظ الغسالة في الإناء لا يجوز التيمم لأجل الخوف على دابته واعلم أن الإنسان إذا عطش وكان عند آخر ماء، فإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه لعطشه فهو أولى به ، وإلا وجب دفعه للمضطر، فإن لم يدفعه أخذه منه وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل صاحب الماء فدمه هدر، وإن قتل الآخر كان مضموناً، وينبغي أن يضمن المضطر قيمة الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي : ١١٦]
قهراً،
خوف فوت إلخ أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها تفوت بلا خلف، والأصل في هذا الباب أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا يتيمم له عند خوف فوته كالوقتية، فإنها تفوت إلى خلفه و وهو القضاء، أو كالجمعة فخلفه الظهر، وما لا خلف له يتيمم له كالعيدين وصلاة الجنازة. صلاة جنازة قيل: لا يجوز التيمم للولي في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ينتظر، ولو صلوا له حق الإعادة، قال صاحب "الهداية" : هو الصحيح، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز للولي أيضاً؛
لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه، ولو لم ينتظروه، جاز له التيمم، قال شمس الأئمة هو الصحيح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣١/١]
A mile: some fixed the mile, farsakh, and barid in his saying: the barid is four farsakhs, and the farsakh is three miles they placed. And the mile is a thousand... then the cubit is four fist-lengths, then twenty-four finger-breadths, then each finger is six barleycorns, so a hair appears from one to the belly of another placed. The yards? Say: and the yard is four cubits, so follow. Then the barleycorn is six hairs only from the tail of a mule, not about this reference. Even in the city: i.e., even if he is at a distance from pure water in the city, and this is according to the correct view of the school. In Sharh al-Tahawi, it says tayammum is not allowed in the city except for fear of missing funeral prayer or Eid, and for the junub due to cold. The correct is the first opinion, and the prohibition is based on the custom of cities, so it is not a real difference. And occurrence of illness and cold from which he fears destruction or illness, fear of enemy, thirst, and need to knead dough not for cooking broth, loss of implement, and fear of missing funeral prayer. Illness: Know that the sick person is four types: one whom water harms, or movement to use it; the third: one whom none of that harms but cannot do it himself; his case is either he finds someone to perform ablution for him or not. If he does not find, tayammum is permissible for him by consensus, even in the city according to the apparent school. If he finds, then either that person is among those obedient to him like his slave, his child, or his hired worker, or not. If he is among those obedient, the mashayikh differed based on the Imam's statement based on differing narrations. If he is not among those obedient and he does not help him without compensation, tayammum is permissible for him absolutely. And the two said: it is not permissible in all cases, except when the wage is great, which is more than a quarter dirham. The fourth: one who cannot perform ablution nor tayammum, neither by himself nor with the help of another. Some said: he does not pray by analogy with the Imam's statement until he is able to do one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays by way of resemblance and repeats. And Muhammad's statement is inconsistent. And cold: indicates that it is permissible for the one with minor impurity also where he did not stipulate being junub, and that is the statement of some mashayikh, but the correct is that it is not permissible for him. And fear: i.e., if one who wants to perform ablution fears that an enemy will kill him if he goes out to the pond to perform ablution. (Muhammad) It is general, includes whether the enemy is human or other, and whether he fears for his life, property, or trust, and whether a woman fears a wicked person at water, or the indebted bankrupt person fears imprisonment, and no repetition is required from them nor from one imprisoned while traveling. Thirst: i.e., if he fears that if he uses water for ablution he will die of thirst, tayammum is permissible for him. It is general, includes whether he fears immediately or eventually for himself, his fellow traveler, or his animal, even a dog, and it is difficult to preserve the wastewater due to lack of container. If it is possible to preserve the wastewater in a container, then tayammum is not permissible for fear for his animal. And know if a person is thirsty and someone else has water: if the owner needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled; otherwise, he must give it to the desperate person. If he does not give it, the desperate person may take it from him by force and may fight him. If the desperate person kills the owner, his blood is wasted; if the owner kills the desperate person, it is guaranteed. The desperate person should pay the value of the water. Fear of missing, etc.: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing funeral prayer because it is missed without replacement. The principle in this chapter is that what is missed with a substitute (like fard prayers made up later) cannot be performed by tayammum when fear of missing it arises, because it has a substitute, i.e., make-up (qada), or like Friday prayer, whose substitute is Zhuhr. What has no substitute, tayammum is performed for it, like the two Eids and funeral prayer. Funeral prayer: it is said that tayammum is not permissible for the guardian according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa because he can wait, and if they pray, he has the right to repeat. The author of al-Hidayah said: that is the correct view. In the manifest narration, it is permissible for the guardian also because waiting in it is disliked, and if they do not wait, tayammum is permissible for him. Shams al-A'imma said that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage lists the second condition for tayammum: a valid excuse (udhr). It begins with the measurement of distance (a mile or more from water) and notes that even in a city, if water is far, tayammum is allowed according to the correct view, though some narrations restrict it to special cases. It then enumerates excuses: illness (detailed into four categories of patients), cold where death is feared, fear of enemy, thirst (including for animals), necessity for kneading dough (not for broth), lack of vessel, and fear of missing funeral prayer. For each, it provides detailed rulings and some intra-Hanafi differences. For example, regarding illness, it discusses who can assist and the wage threshold. For thirst, it elaborates on taking water from others and consequences of fighting. For funeral prayer, it notes the principle that tayammum is only for acts with no substitute, and discusses the guardian's case with a difference between narrations. The passage is a comprehensive statement of the valid excuses for tayammum according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عذر مبيح (udhr mubih): A legal excuse that permits tayammum, such as distance from water.
بعد الماء (bu'd al-ma'): Distance from water, typically a mile or more, as a valid excuse for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, is tayammum permissible if a person is in a city but the nearest water is 2 miles away?
A) No, because tayammum in a city is only for fear of missing funeral prayer or Eid.
B) Yes, because distance is a valid excuse and the correct view allows it even in the city.
C) Yes, but only if the person is also sick.
D) No, because the threshold is 1 mile; 2 miles is too far.

Key Takeaway
Distance from water (a mile or more) is a valid excuse for tayammum, even when residing in a city.

Valid Excuse 2: Illness and Cold
Details four types of sick persons and cold excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of sick persons regarding tayammum and state the ruling for fear of death from cold.

Core Idea
Illness and extreme cold are valid excuses, but the ruling depends on the type of sickness and availability of assistance.

The second major category of excuses for tayammum includes illness and fear of harm from cold. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced classification of patients, distinguishing between those harmed by water, those who cannot move, and those who cannot perform wudu themselves. Additionally, the cold excuse involves a difference between minor and major impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of sick persons
1) One whom water harms; 2) One harmed by movement; 3) One not harmed but cannot do wudu alone; 4) One unable to do wudu or tayammum even with help.
Type 4 is the most severe.
2
Apply the rule for each type
For types 1 and 2: tayammum allowed. For type 3: if no helper, tayammum; if a helper from obedient persons (slave, child, hired) is available, there is ikhtilaf; otherwise tayammum. For type 4: difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The wage threshold for hired helper is more than 1/4 dirham.
3
Evaluate the cold excuse
Fear of death or severe illness from cold is a valid excuse. However, there is a difference: is it allowed only for junub (major impurity) or also for minor impurity? The correct view restricts it to junub.
4
Distinguish the rulings for type 4
Abu Hanifa's qiyas suggests no prayer until able; Abu Yusuf allows prayer and requires repetition.
Muhammad's view is inconsistent per the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ميلا ضبط بعضهم الميل والفرسخ والبريد في قوله: إن البريد من الفراسخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضعوا
والميل ألف أي . من ثم الذراع من الأصابع أربع من بعدها العشرون ثم الإصبع ست شعيرات فظهر شعرة منها إلى بطن الأخرى توضع
الباعات قل والباع أربع أذرع فتتبعوا
ثم الشعيرة ست شعرات فقط من ذيل بغل ليس عن ذا مرجع
[مراقي الفلاح: ١١٤]
ولو في المصر: أي ولو كان بعده عن ماء طهور في المصر، وهذا على الصحيح من المذهب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" أنه لا يجوز التيمم في المصر إلا لخوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد وللجنب من البرد، والحق الأول، والمنع بناء على عادة الأمصار، فليس خلافاً حقيقياً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥]

وحصول مرض وبرد يخاف منه التلف أو المرض، وخوف عدو وعطش واحتياج
موصوف لغلبة الظن
تلف بعض الأعضاء
لعجن لا لطبخ مرق ولفقد آلة وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة .
من
الإدام
مرض: اعلم أن المريض أربعة أنواع من يضره الماء، أو التحرك لاستعماله، والثالث: من لا يضره شيء من ذلك، ولكن لا يقدر على الفعل بنفسه، فحاله لا يخلو إما يجد من يوضئه أو لا، فإن لم يجد جاز له التيمم إجماعاً ولو في المصر على ظاهر المذهب، وإن وجد فإما أن يكون من أهل طاعته كعبده وولده وأجيره أو لا، فإن كان أهل طاعته اختلف فيه المشائخ على قول الإمام بناءً على اختلاف الرواية عنه، وإن لم يكن من أهل طاعته و لم يعنه بغير بدل جاز له التيمم عنده مطلقاً. وقالا: لا يجوز في الفصول كلها، إلا إذا كان الأجر كثيراً، وهو ما زاد على ربع درهم، والرابع: من لا يقدر على الوضوء ولا على التيمم، لا بنفسه ولا بغيره قال بعضهم: لا يصلي على قياس قول الإمام حتى يقدر على أحدهما، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي تشبهاً ويعيد، وقول محمد مضطرب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥] وبرد: يشير إلى أنه يجوز للمحدث أيضًا حيث لم يشترط أن يكون جنباً، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. تبيين الحقائق (١١٩/١] وخوف أي إذا خاف من يريد التوضؤ أن يقتله عدو إن خرج إلى الغدير للتوضؤ. (محمد) إعزاز علي عدو أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان العدو آدميا أو غيره، وما إذا خافه على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، وما إذا خافت فاسقا عند الماء أو خاف المديون المفلس ،الحبس ولا إعادة عليهم ولا على من حبس في السفر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٦]
عطش: [أي إن خاف من عنده ماء إن صرفه في التوضؤ أن يهلكه العطش جاز له التيمم.] أطلقه فشمل ما إذا خاف حالا أو مآلا على نفسه أو رفيقه في القافلة أو دابته ولو كلبا وتعذر حفظ الغسالة لعدم الإناء، ولو أمكن حفظ الغسالة في الإناء لا يجوز التيمم لأجل الخوف على دابته واعلم أن الإنسان إذا عطش وكان عند آخر ماء، فإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه لعطشه فهو أولى به ، وإلا وجب دفعه للمضطر، فإن لم يدفعه أخذه منه وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل صاحب الماء فدمه هدر، وإن قتل الآخر كان مضموناً، وينبغي أن يضمن المضطر قيمة الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي : ١١٦]
قهراً،
خوف فوت إلخ أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها تفوت بلا خلف، والأصل في هذا الباب أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا يتيمم له عند خوف فوته كالوقتية، فإنها تفوت إلى خلفه و وهو القضاء، أو كالجمعة فخلفه الظهر، وما لا خلف له يتيمم له كالعيدين وصلاة الجنازة. صلاة جنازة قيل: لا يجوز التيمم للولي في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ينتظر، ولو صلوا له حق الإعادة، قال صاحب "الهداية" : هو الصحيح، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز للولي أيضاً؛
لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه، ولو لم ينتظروه، جاز له التيمم، قال شمس الأئمة هو الصحيح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣١/١]
A mile: some fixed the mile, farsakh, and barid in his saying: the barid is four farsakhs, and the farsakh is three miles they placed. And the mile is a thousand... then the cubit is four fist-lengths, then twenty-four finger-breadths, then each finger is six barleycorns, so a hair appears from one to the belly of another placed. The yards? Say: and the yard is four cubits, so follow. Then the barleycorn is six hairs only from the tail of a mule, not about this reference. Even in the city: i.e., even if he is at a distance from pure water in the city, and this is according to the correct view of the school. In Sharh al-Tahawi, it says tayammum is not allowed in the city except for fear of missing funeral prayer or Eid, and for the junub due to cold. The correct is the first opinion, and the prohibition is based on the custom of cities, so it is not a real difference. And occurrence of illness and cold from which he fears destruction or illness, fear of enemy, thirst, and need to knead dough not for cooking broth, loss of implement, and fear of missing funeral prayer. Illness: Know that the sick person is four types: one whom water harms, or movement to use it; the third: one whom none of that harms but cannot do it himself; his case is either he finds someone to perform ablution for him or not. If he does not find, tayammum is permissible for him by consensus, even in the city according to the apparent school. If he finds, then either that person is among those obedient to him like his slave, his child, or his hired worker, or not. If he is among those obedient, the mashayikh differed based on the Imam's statement based on differing narrations. If he is not among those obedient and he does not help him without compensation, tayammum is permissible for him absolutely. And the two said: it is not permissible in all cases, except when the wage is great, which is more than a quarter dirham. The fourth: one who cannot perform ablution nor tayammum, neither by himself nor with the help of another. Some said: he does not pray by analogy with the Imam's statement until he is able to do one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays by way of resemblance and repeats. And Muhammad's statement is inconsistent. And cold: indicates that it is permissible for the one with minor impurity also where he did not stipulate being junub, and that is the statement of some mashayikh, but the correct is that it is not permissible for him. And fear: i.e., if one who wants to perform ablution fears that an enemy will kill him if he goes out to the pond to perform ablution. (Muhammad) It is general, includes whether the enemy is human or other, and whether he fears for his life, property, or trust, and whether a woman fears a wicked person at water, or the indebted bankrupt person fears imprisonment, and no repetition is required from them nor from one imprisoned while traveling. Thirst: i.e., if he fears that if he uses water for ablution he will die of thirst, tayammum is permissible for him. It is general, includes whether he fears immediately or eventually for himself, his fellow traveler, or his animal, even a dog, and it is difficult to preserve the wastewater due to lack of container. If it is possible to preserve the wastewater in a container, then tayammum is not permissible for fear for his animal. And know if a person is thirsty and someone else has water: if the owner needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled; otherwise, he must give it to the desperate person. If he does not give it, the desperate person may take it from him by force and may fight him. If the desperate person kills the owner, his blood is wasted; if the owner kills the desperate person, it is guaranteed. The desperate person should pay the value of the water. Fear of missing, etc.: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing funeral prayer because it is missed without replacement. The principle in this chapter is that what is missed with a substitute (like fard prayers made up later) cannot be performed by tayammum when fear of missing it arises, because it has a substitute, i.e., make-up (qada), or like Friday prayer, whose substitute is Zhuhr. What has no substitute, tayammum is performed for it, like the two Eids and funeral prayer. Funeral prayer: it is said that tayammum is not permissible for the guardian according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa because he can wait, and if they pray, he has the right to repeat. The author of al-Hidayah said: that is the correct view. In the manifest narration, it is permissible for the guardian also because waiting in it is disliked, and if they do not wait, tayammum is permissible for him. Shams al-A'imma said that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage lists the second condition for tayammum: a valid excuse (udhr). It begins with the measurement of distance (a mile or more from water) and notes that even in a city, if water is far, tayammum is allowed according to the correct view, though some narrations restrict it to special cases. It then enumerates excuses: illness (detailed into four categories of patients), cold where death is feared, fear of enemy, thirst (including for animals), necessity for kneading dough (not for broth), lack of vessel, and fear of missing funeral prayer. For each, it provides detailed rulings and some intra-Hanafi differences. For example, regarding illness, it discusses who can assist and the wage threshold. For thirst, it elaborates on taking water from others and consequences of fighting. For funeral prayer, it notes the principle that tayammum is only for acts with no substitute, and discusses the guardian's case with a difference between narrations. The passage is a comprehensive statement of the valid excuses for tayammum according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مرض (marad): Illness that warrants tayammum, classified into four types.
برد (bard): Extreme cold that may cause death or illness, excusing tayammum for junub only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a type 3 sick person (not harmed by water but cannot perform wudu alone), if a hired worker demands 1/3 dirham to help, what is the ruling according to the Sahibayn?
A) Tayammum is not allowed because the helper is available.
B) Tayammum is allowed because the wage exceeds 1/4 dirham.
C) Tayammum is allowed only if the helper is a slave.
D) Tayammum is not allowed because the wage is less than 1 dirham.

Key Takeaway
Illness and cold are valid excuses, but the ruling varies by the type of sickness and availability of affordable help.

Valid Excuse 3: Fear, Thirst, and Necessity
Details excuses of fear, thirst, and necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings for tayammum when facing fear of enemy, thirst (for self, companion, or animal), necessity for dough, and lack of utensils.

Core Idea
Fear of harm, thirst, and dire necessity permit tayammum, even if water is present but its use would lead to loss.

Beyond sickness, the Hanafi school recognizes various urgent situations that permit tayammum. These include fear of an enemy (human or animal), thirst that threatens life or property, the need to use water for dough (not for broth), and the lack of a vessel to hold water. Each has detailed conditions and some carry rules about taking water from others by force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of fear that permit tayammum
Fear of enemy includes fear for life, property, or trust, whether the enemy is human or animal. Also includes fear of imprisonment for debt.
The text generalizes to any type of enemy.
2
Understand the thirst excuse
If using water for ablution would cause death from thirst (for self, companion, or animal), tayammum is allowed. If the wastewater can be saved in a container, tayammum is not allowed unless the container is absent.
Also covers the right to take water from another if necessary, with potential fighting and blood money rules.
3
Apply the necessity for dough and lack of utensils
If water is needed for kneading dough (for food, not broth) and no other water is available, tayammum is allowed. Similarly, if one lacks a vessel to fetch water, tayammum is permitted.
The dough exception is specific to food necessity, not cooking broth.
4
Recognize the principle of no repetition
For those who perform tayammum due to these excuses, no qada (repetition) is required, unlike some other excuses.
The text explicitly says 'la i'ada alayhim' for the imprisoned traveler.

Source Text

And the two said: it is not permissible in all cases, except when the wage is great, which is more than a quarter dirham. And know if a person is thirsty and someone else has water: if the owner needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled; otherwise, he must give it to the desperate person. If he does not give it, the desperate person may take it from him by force and may fight him. If the desperate person kills the owner, his blood is wasted; if the owner kills the desperate person, it is guaranteed. The desperate person should pay the value of the water. Fear of missing, etc.: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing funeral prayer because it is missed without replacement. The principle in this chapter is that what is missed with a substitute (like fard prayers made up later) cannot be performed by tayammum when fear of missing it arises, because it has a substitute, i.e., make-up (qada), or like Friday prayer, whose substitute is Zhuhr. What has no substitute, tayammum is performed for it, like the two Eids and funeral prayer. Funeral prayer: it is said that tayammum is not permissible for the guardian according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa because he can wait, and if they pray, he has the right to repeat. The author of al-Hidayah said: that is the correct view. In the manifest narration, it is permissible for the guardian also because waiting in it is disliked, and if they do not wait, tayammum is permissible for him. Shams al-A'imma said that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage lists the second condition for tayammum: a valid excuse (udhr). It begins with the measurement of distance (a mile or more from water) and notes that even in a city, if water is far, tayammum is allowed according to the correct view, though some narrations restrict it to special cases. It then enumerates excuses: illness (detailed into four categories of patients), cold where death is feared, fear of enemy, thirst (including for animals), necessity for kneading dough (not for broth), lack of vessel, and fear of missing funeral prayer. For each, it provides detailed rulings and some intra-Hanafi differences. For example, regarding illness, it discusses who can assist and the wage threshold. For thirst, it elaborates on taking water from others and consequences of fighting. For funeral prayer, it notes the principle that tayammum is only for acts with no substitute, and discusses the guardian's case with a difference between narrations. The passage is a comprehensive statement of the valid excuses for tayammum according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خوف عدو (khawf 'aduw): Fear of an enemy (human or animal) that justifies tayammum.
عطش (atsh): Thirst that threatens life or welfare of self, companion, or animal, excusing tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person has water but fears losing his property to a thief if he leaves to fetch water, may he perform tayammum?
A) No, only fear of physical harm counts.
B) Yes, because the excuse includes fear for property.
C) Yes, but only if the thief is a human.
D) No, because property can be recovered later.

Key Takeaway
Fear of harm, thirst, and necessity are valid excuses for tayammum, with specific conditions and consequences.

Valid Excuse 4: Fear of Missing Funeral Prayer
Explains the principle for tayammum regarding substitute acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle that tayammum is allowed for acts with no substitute, and apply it to funeral prayer and the guardian's case.

Core Idea
Fear of missing a prayer that has no substitute (like funeral prayer) allows tayammum; this is the key principle distinguishing from regular fard prayers that can be made up.

The final major excuse listed in the passage is the fear of missing the funeral prayer (salat al-janaza). This leads to a foundational principle in Hanafi law: tayammum is only permitted for acts that have no substitute (khalaf). Regular fard prayers can be made up (qada), so tayammum is not allowed to avoid missing them. Funeral prayer, Eid prayer, and others cannot be made up, so tayammum is permitted. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the guardian (wali) of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The text states: 'What has a substitute cannot be performed by tayammum when fear of missing it arises; what has no substitute can.'
Substitute = qada (make-up) for fard prayers, or Zhuhr for Jumu'ah.
2
Apply to funeral prayer
Funeral prayer has no substitute; if you miss it, it is gone. Therefore, fear of missing it is a valid excuse for tayammum.
Also applies to Eid prayers.
3
Analyze the guardian's case
The guardian (next of kin) has a special right to lead the funeral prayer. If he fears missing it, can he do tayammum? There are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one says he can wait or repeat, so tayammum not allowed; the other says waiting is disliked, so tayammum is allowed.
Al-Hidayah prefers the permissive view (tayammum allowed for guardian).
4
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that tayammum is permissible for the guardian as well, per Shams al-A'imma.

Source Text

ميلا ضبط بعضهم الميل والفرسخ والبريد في قوله: إن البريد من الفراسخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضعوا
والميل ألف أي . من ثم الذراع من الأصابع أربع من بعدها العشرون ثم الإصبع ست شعيرات فظهر شعرة منها إلى بطن الأخرى توضع
الباعات قل والباع أربع أذرع فتتبعوا

ولو في المصر: أي ولو كان بعده عن ماء طهور في المصر، وهذا على الصحيح من المذهب، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" أنه لا يجوز التيمم في المصر إلا لخوف فوت صلاة جنازة أو عيد وللجنب من البرد، والحق الأول، والمنع بناء على عادة الأمصار، فليس خلافاً حقيقياً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥]
