الإدام
مرض: اعلم أن المريض أربعة أنواع من يضره الماء، أو التحرك لاستعماله، والثالث: من لا يضره شيء من ذلك، ولكن لا يقدر على الفعل بنفسه، فحاله لا يخلو إما يجد من يوضئه أو لا، فإن لم يجد جاز له التيمم إجماعاً ولو في المصر على ظاهر المذهب، وإن وجد فإما أن يكون من أهل طاعته كعبده وولده وأجيره أو لا، فإن كان أهل طاعته اختلف فيه المشائخ على قول الإمام بناءً على اختلاف الرواية عنه، وإن لم يكن من أهل طاعته و لم يعنه بغير بدل جاز له التيمم عنده مطلقاً. وقالا: لا يجوز في الفصول كلها، إلا إذا كان الأجر كثيراً، وهو ما زاد على ربع درهم، والرابع: من لا يقدر على الوضوء ولا على التيمم، لا بنفسه ولا بغيره قال بعضهم: لا يصلي على قياس قول الإمام حتى يقدر على أحدهما، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي تشبهاً ويعيد، وقول محمد مضطرب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥] وبرد: يشير إلى أنه يجوز للمحدث أيضًا حيث لم يشترط أن يكون جنباً، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. تبيين الحقائق (١١٩/١] وخوف أي إذا خاف من يريد التوضؤ أن يقتله عدو إن خرج إلى الغدير للتوضؤ. (محمد) إعزاز علي عدو أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان العدو آدميا أو غيره، وما إذا خافه على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، وما إذا خافت فاسقا عند الماء أو خاف المديون المفلس ،الحبس ولا إعادة عليهم ولا على من حبس في السفر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٦]
عطش: [أي إن خاف من عنده ماء إن صرفه في التوضؤ أن يهلكه العطش جاز له التيمم.] أطلقه فشمل ما إذا خاف حالا أو مآلا على نفسه أو رفيقه في القافلة أو دابته ولو كلبا وتعذر حفظ الغسالة لعدم الإناء، ولو أمكن حفظ الغسالة في الإناء لا يجوز التيمم لأجل الخوف على دابته واعلم أن الإنسان إذا عطش وكان عند آخر ماء، فإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه لعطشه فهو أولى به ، وإلا وجب دفعه للمضطر، فإن لم يدفعه أخذه منه وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل صاحب الماء فدمه هدر، وإن قتل الآخر كان مضموناً، وينبغي أن يضمن المضطر قيمة الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي : ١١٦]
قهراً،
خوف فوت إلخ أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها تفوت بلا خلف، والأصل في هذا الباب أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا يتيمم له عند خوف فوته كالوقتية، فإنها تفوت إلى خلفه و وهو القضاء، أو كالجمعة فخلفه الظهر، وما لا خلف له يتيمم له كالعيدين وصلاة الجنازة. صلاة جنازة قيل: لا يجوز التيمم للولي في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ينتظر، ولو صلوا له حق الإعادة، قال صاحب "الهداية" : هو الصحيح، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز للولي أيضاً؛
لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه، ولو لم ينتظروه، جاز له التيمم، قال شمس الأئمة هو الصحيح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣١/١]
A mile: some fixed the mile, farsakh, and barid in his saying: the barid is four farsakhs, and the farsakh is three miles they placed. And the mile is a thousand... then the cubit is four fist-lengths, then twenty-four finger-breadths, then each finger is six barleycorns, so a hair appears from one to the belly of another placed. The yards? Say: and the yard is four cubits, so follow. Then the barleycorn is six hairs only from the tail of a mule, not about this reference. Even in the city: i.e., even if he is at a distance from pure water in the city, and this is according to the correct view of the school. In Sharh al-Tahawi, it says tayammum is not allowed in the city except for fear of missing funeral prayer or Eid, and for the junub due to cold. The correct is the first opinion, and the prohibition is based on the custom of cities, so it is not a real difference. And occurrence of illness and cold from which he fears destruction or illness, fear of enemy, thirst, and need to knead dough not for cooking broth, loss of implement, and fear of missing funeral prayer. Illness: Know that the sick person is four types: one whom water harms, or movement to use it; the third: one whom none of that harms but cannot do it himself; his case is either he finds someone to perform ablution for him or not. If he does not find, tayammum is permissible for him by consensus, even in the city according to the apparent school. If he finds, then either that person is among those obedient to him like his slave, his child, or his hired worker, or not. If he is among those obedient, the mashayikh differed based on the Imam's statement based on differing narrations. If he is not among those obedient and he does not help him without compensation, tayammum is permissible for him absolutely. And the two said: it is not permissible in all cases, except when the wage is great, which is more than a quarter dirham. The fourth: one who cannot perform ablution nor tayammum, neither by himself nor with the help of another. Some said: he does not pray by analogy with the Imam's statement until he is able to do one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays by way of resemblance and repeats. And Muhammad's statement is inconsistent. And cold: indicates that it is permissible for the one with minor impurity also where he did not stipulate being junub, and that is the statement of some mashayikh, but the correct is that it is not permissible for him. And fear: i.e., if one who wants to perform ablution fears that an enemy will kill him if he goes out to the pond to perform ablution. (Muhammad) It is general, includes whether the enemy is human or other, and whether he fears for his life, property, or trust, and whether a woman fears a wicked person at water, or the indebted bankrupt person fears imprisonment, and no repetition is required from them nor from one imprisoned while traveling. Thirst: i.e., if he fears that if he uses water for ablution he will die of thirst, tayammum is permissible for him. It is general, includes whether he fears immediately or eventually for himself, his fellow traveler, or his animal, even a dog, and it is difficult to preserve the wastewater due to lack of container. If it is possible to preserve the wastewater in a container, then tayammum is not permissible for fear for his animal. And know if a person is thirsty and someone else has water: if the owner needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled; otherwise, he must give it to the desperate person. If he does not give it, the desperate person may take it from him by force and may fight him. If the desperate person kills the owner, his blood is wasted; if the owner kills the desperate person, it is guaranteed. The desperate person should pay the value of the water. Fear of missing, etc.: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing funeral prayer because it is missed without replacement. The principle in this chapter is that what is missed with a substitute (like fard prayers made up later) cannot be performed by tayammum when fear of missing it arises, because it has a substitute, i.e., make-up (qada), or like Friday prayer, whose substitute is Zhuhr. What has no substitute, tayammum is performed for it, like the two Eids and funeral prayer. Funeral prayer: it is said that tayammum is not permissible for the guardian according to the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa because he can wait, and if they pray, he has the right to repeat. The author of al-Hidayah said: that is the correct view. In the manifest narration, it is permissible for the guardian also because waiting in it is disliked, and if they do not wait, tayammum is permissible for him. Shams al-A'imma said that is the correct view.

Commentary
This passage lists the second condition for tayammum: a valid excuse (udhr). It begins with the measurement of distance (a mile or more from water) and notes that even in a city, if water is far, tayammum is allowed according to the correct view, though some narrations restrict it to special cases. For thirst, it elaborates on taking water from others and consequences of fighting. The passage is a comprehensive statement of the valid excuses for tayammum according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or make-up for a missed act of worship.
ولي (wali): Guardian of the deceased, typically the closest male relative, who has priority in leading or joining the funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, may the guardian of the deceased perform tayammum for fear of missing the funeral prayer?
A) No, because he can wait for another funeral.
B) Yes, because waiting is disliked and tayammum is allowed.
C) No, because he must use water if available.
D) Yes, only if he is traveling.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permitted for fear of missing any act of worship that has no substitute, such as funeral and Eid prayers.

Tayammum for the Sick: The Four Types and the Dispute on Assistance
Lists conditions for tayammum with intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of sick persons regarding tayammum and state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the necessity of paying for wudu assistance.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted for the sick who cannot use water; the need to pay for help is disputed among Hanafi imams.

This lesson focuses on the first condition for tayammum: illness. The text from Nur al-Idah explains that sick persons fall into four categories. The key debate is whether a sick person must pay a hired helper to perform wudu when he cannot do it himself. We will clarify the four types and the differences between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of sick persons
The text describes four categories: those harmed by water, those harmed by movement, those who cannot do wudu themselves, and those who cannot do either wudu or tayammum.
These are not mutually exclusive but are graded.
2
Understand the consensus on absence of helper
If no helper is available, tayammum is allowed by consensus, even in the city according to the apparent madhhab.
3
Analyze the dispute when helper is available but not obedient
If the helper is not among those obedient (e.g., a hired stranger), Abu Hanifa allows tayammum absolutely if the helper refuses without payment. The Sahibayn require the fee to be large (over a quarter dirham) to permit tayammum.
Obedient helpers include slave, child, employee.
4
Note the ruling on the fourth type (unable altogether)
For one who cannot do wudu or tayammum, Abu Yusuf says he prays as a resemblance and repeats later. Muhammad's view is confused.
This case is exceptional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وحصول مرض وبرد يخاف منه التلف أو المرض، وخوف عدو وعطش واحتياج
موصوف لغلبة الظن
تلف بعض الأعضاء
لعجن لا لطبخ مرق ولفقد آلة وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة .
من
الإدام
مرض: اعلم أن المريض أربعة أنواع من يضره الماء، أو التحرك لاستعماله، والثالث: من لا يضره شيء من ذلك، ولكن لا يقدر على الفعل بنفسه، فحاله لا يخلو إما يجد من يوضئه أو لا، فإن لم يجد جاز له التيمم إجماعاً ولو في المصر على ظاهر المذهب، وإن وجد فإما أن يكون من أهل طاعته كعبده وولده وأجيره أو لا، فإن كان أهل طاعته اختلف فيه المشائخ على قول الإمام بناءً على اختلاف الرواية عنه، وإن لم يكن من أهل طاعته و لم يعنه بغير بدل جاز له التيمم عنده مطلقاً. وقالا: لا يجوز في الفصول كلها، إلا إذا كان الأجر كثيراً، وهو ما زاد على ربع درهم، والرابع: من لا يقدر على الوضوء ولا على التيمم، لا بنفسه ولا بغيره قال بعضهم: لا يصلي على قياس قول الإمام حتى يقدر على أحدهما، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي تشبهاً ويعيد، وقول محمد مضطرب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥] وبرد: يشير إلى أنه يجوز للمحدث أيضًا حيث لم يشترط أن يكون جنباً، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. تبيين الحقائق (۱۱۹/۱] وخوف أي إذا خاف من يريد التوضؤ أن يقتله عدو إن خرج إلى الغدير للتوضؤ. (محمد) إعزاز علي عدو أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان العدو آدميا أو غيره، وما إذا خافه على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، وما إذا خافت فاسقا عند الماء أو خاف المديون المفلس ،الحبس ولا إعادة عليهم ولا على من حبس في السفر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٦]
عطش: [أي إن خاف من عنده ماء إن صرفه في التوضؤ أن يهلكه العطش جاز له التيمم.] أطلقه فشمل ما إذا خاف حالا أو مآلا على نفسه أو رفيقه في القافلة أو دابته ولو كلبا وتعذر حفظ الغسالة لعدم الإناء، ولو أمكن حفظ الغسالة في الإناء لا يجوز التيمم لأجل الخوف على دابته واعلم أن الإنسان إذا عطش وكان عند آخر ماء، فإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه لعطشه فهو أولى به ، وإلا وجب دفعه للمضطر، فإن لم يدفعه أخذه منه وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل صاحب الماء فدمه هدر، وإن قتل الآخر كان مضموناً، وينبغي أن يضمن المضطر قيمة الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي : ١١٦]
Conditions for the validity of tayammum: occurrence of illness and cold from which death or illness is feared, fear of an enemy, and thirst, and need described by overwhelming probability [of] loss of some limbs, for kneading not for cooking broth, and lack of equipment, and fear of missing funeral prayer. Illness: Know that the sick person is of four types: one whom water harms, or movement to use it; the third: one whom none of that harms, but he cannot perform [wudu] himself; his case is not free from either finding someone to perform wudu for him or not. If he does not find, tayammum is permissible for him by consensus, even in a city according to the apparent madhhab. If he finds, then either he is among those obedient to him, like his slave, child, or hired worker, or not. If he is among those obedient to him, the mashayikh differed based on two narrations from the Imam. If he is not among those obedient to him and he does not assist him without payment, tayammum is permissible for him absolutely according to him [Abu Hanifa]. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: it is not permissible in all cases, unless the fee is large, which is more than a quarter dirham. The fourth: one who cannot perform wudu nor tayammum, neither himself nor by another. Some said: he should not pray on the analogy of the Imam's statement until he is able to do one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays by way of resemblance and repeats. The statement of Muhammad is confused. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 115] And cold: it indicates that it is permissible for one with minor impurity (hadath) as well, since it was not conditioned that he be in major impurity (junub). This is the statement of some mashayikh, and the correct [view] is that tayammum is not permissible for him. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (1:119). And fear: i.e., if the one who wants to perform wudu fears that an enemy will kill him if he goes out to the watering hole for wudu. [Muhammad] 'Izzaz 'Ali: enemy is unrestricted, so it includes whether the enemy is human or other, and whether he fears for himself, his wealth, or his trust, and whether he fears a transgressor at the water or the debtor fears imprisonment, and no repetition is required from them nor from one imprisoned on a journey. [Maraqi al-Falah: 116] Thirst: [i.e., if one who has water fears that if he uses it for wudu he will die of thirst, tayammum is permissible for him.] It is unrestricted, so it includes whether he fears immediately or eventually for himself, his companion in the caravan, or his animal, even a dog, and if saving the washing water is impossible due to lack of a vessel. If it is possible to save the washing water in a vessel, tayammum is not permissible due to fear for his animal. Know that if a person is thirsty and another has water: if the owner of the water needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled to it; otherwise, he must give it to the one in dire need. If he does not give it, he [the needy] can take it from him and is allowed to fight him. If he kills the owner of the water, his blood is shed without liability (hader); if the other is killed, it is guaranteed (mamun). It is appropriate that the needy person guarantee the value of the water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 116]
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions that make tayammum permissible when water is available but its use would cause harm. The author, 'Ibn 'Abidin in his commentary on Nur al-Idah, expands on each condition. The first condition is illness: the law distinguishes four types of sick persons regarding tayammum. The key point is that if water harms the person or he cannot use it himself and finds no one to assist him, tayammum is allowed. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if someone is available to help but not obedient (e.g., a stranger who demands a fee), Abu Hanifa allows tayammum unconditionally if the helper does not assist without payment, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) only allow it if the fee is exorbitant (over a quarter dirham). The second condition is cold: there is a dispute about whether one with minor impurity can do tayammum due to cold. The correct view is that it is not allowed; only a junub (major impurity) person may do so. The third condition is fear of an enemy: this includes any threat to life, wealth, or honor, and even a debtor fearing imprisonment. No repetition (i'ada) of prayer is required in these cases. The fourth condition is thirst: if using water for wudu would lead to death from thirst, tayammum is allowed for oneself, one's companion, or one's animal. If the water can be saved in a vessel, tayammum is not allowed for the animal's sake. The passage ends with a ruling: if a thirsty person takes water from another who is not in need, and a fight ensues, the killer's blood is subject to different rules depending on who is killed.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as substitute for wudu/ghusl when water unavailable or harmful.
أهل طاعته (ahl ta'atihi): Those who are obedient to him, such as his slave, child, or hired worker (who is expected to obey commands).
بدل (badal): Compensation or payment for a service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tayammum for a sick person who has a non-obedient helper that demands a fee of 0.1 dirhams?
A) Tayammum is not allowed because the fee is small.
B) Tayammum is allowed according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.
C) Tayammum is allowed according to both.
D) Tayammum is not allowed because the helper is available.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum due to illness is permitted when water is harmful or the person cannot use it; the availability of paid assistance creates a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute.

Tayammum due to Cold: The Hadath vs Junub Dispute
Lists conditions for tayammum with intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tayammum due to cold for a person with minor impurity (hadath) versus major impurity (junub).

Core Idea
Only a junub may perform tayammum due to cold; one with minor impurity must use water or wait.

This lesson addresses the second condition for tayammum: fear of cold. The text presents a dispute: some mashayikh permit tayammum for a person with minor impurity (hadath) due to cold, but the correct Hanafi view restricts it to the junub. We will analyze the basis for this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The text says: 'and cold: it indicates that it is permissible for one with minor impurity also, since it was not conditioned that he be junub. This is the statement of some mashayikh, and the correct is that it is not permissible for him.'
Some scholars extended the concession due to the absence of the word junub in the original condition.
2
Understand the reasoning of the opposing view
Those who permit it for hadath argue that the condition is general ('cold' without specifying impurity type).
3
Recognize the tarjih (preferred view)
The correct view, as stated in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, is that tayammum due to cold is not permissible for a person with minor impurity. It is only for the junub.
The passage explicitly says 'al-sahih' (the correct view).
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, a person with minor impurity (e.g., needing wudu) who fears cold must use warm water if available, or wait until he can, but cannot perform tayammum solely due to cold.
If he cannot use water due to cold, he may have another condition (e.g., illness) that permits tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

موصوف لغلبة الظن
تلف بعض الأعضاء
لعجن لا لطبخ مرق ولفقد آلة وخوف فوت صلاة جنازة .
من
الإدام
مرض: اعلم أن المريض أربعة أنواع من يضره الماء، أو التحرك لاستعماله، والثالث: من لا يضره شيء من ذلك، ولكن لا يقدر على الفعل بنفسه، فحاله لا يخلو إما يجد من يوضئه أو لا، فإن لم يجد جاز له التيمم إجماعاً ولو في المصر على ظاهر المذهب، وإن وجد فإما أن يكون من أهل طاعته كعبده وولده وأجيره أو لا، فإن كان أهل طاعته اختلف فيه المشائخ على قول الإمام بناءً على اختلاف الرواية عنه، وإن لم يكن من أهل طاعته و لم يعنه بغير بدل جاز له التيمم عنده مطلقاً. وقالا: لا يجوز في الفصول كلها، إلا إذا كان الأجر كثيراً، وهو ما زاد على ربع درهم، والرابع: من لا يقدر على الوضوء ولا على التيمم، لا بنفسه ولا بغيره قال بعضهم: لا يصلي على قياس قول الإمام حتى يقدر على أحدهما، وقال أبو يوسف يصلي تشبهاً ويعيد، وقول محمد مضطرب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١١٥] وبرد: يشير إلى أنه يجوز للمحدث أيضًا حيث لم يشترط أن يكون جنباً، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز له التيمم. تبيين الحقائق (۱۱۹/۱] وخوف أي إذا خاف من يريد التوضؤ أن يقتله عدو إن خرج إلى الغدير للتوضؤ. (محمد) إعزاز علي عدو أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان العدو آدميا أو غيره، وما إذا خافه على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، وما إذا خافت فاسقا عند الماء أو خاف المديون المفلس ،الحبس ولا إعادة عليهم ولا على من حبس في السفر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١١٦]
عطش: [أي إن خاف من عنده ماء إن صرفه في التوضؤ أن يهلكه العطش جاز له التيمم.] أطلقه فشمل ما إذا خاف حالا أو مآلا على نفسه أو رفيقه في القافلة أو دابته ولو كلبا وتعذر حفظ الغسالة لعدم الإناء، ولو أمكن حفظ الغسالة في الإناء لا يجوز التيمم لأجل الخوف على دابته واعلم أن الإنسان إذا عطش وكان عند آخر ماء، فإن كان صاحب الماء محتاجاً إليه لعطشه فهو أولى به ، وإلا وجب دفعه للمضطر، فإن لم يدفعه أخذه منه وله أن يقاتله، فإن قتل صاحب الماء فدمه هدر، وإن قتل الآخر كان مضموناً، وينبغي أن يضمن المضطر قيمة الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي : ١١٦]
Conditions for the validity of tayammum: occurrence of illness and cold from which death or illness is feared, fear of an enemy, and thirst, and need described by overwhelming probability [of] loss of some limbs, for kneading not for cooking broth, and lack of equipment, and fear of missing funeral prayer. Illness: Know that the sick person is of four types: one whom water harms, or movement to use it; the third: one whom none of that harms, but he cannot perform [wudu] himself; his case is not free from either finding someone to perform wudu for him or not. If he does not find, tayammum is permissible for him by consensus, even in a city according to the apparent madhhab. If he finds, then either he is among those obedient to him, like his slave, child, or hired worker, or not. If he is among those obedient to him, the mashayikh differed based on two narrations from the Imam. If he is not among those obedient to him and he does not assist him without payment, tayammum is permissible for him absolutely according to him [Abu Hanifa]. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: it is not permissible in all cases, unless the fee is large, which is more than a quarter dirham. The fourth: one who cannot perform wudu nor tayammum, neither himself nor by another. Some said: he should not pray on the analogy of the Imam's statement until he is able to do one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays by way of resemblance and repeats. The statement of Muhammad is confused. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 115] And cold: it indicates that it is permissible for one with minor impurity (hadath) as well, since it was not conditioned that he be in major impurity (junub). This is the statement of some mashayikh, and the correct [view] is that tayammum is not permissible for him. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (1:119). And fear: i.e., if the one who wants to perform wudu fears that an enemy will kill him if he goes out to the watering hole for wudu. [Muhammad] 'Izzaz 'Ali: enemy is unrestricted, so it includes whether the enemy is human or other, and whether he fears for himself, his wealth, or his trust, and whether he fears a transgressor at the water or the debtor fears imprisonment, and no repetition is required from them nor from one imprisoned on a journey. [Maraqi al-Falah: 116] Thirst: [i.e., if one who has water fears that if he uses it for wudu he will die of thirst, tayammum is permissible for him.] It is unrestricted, so it includes whether he fears immediately or eventually for himself, his companion in the caravan, or his animal, even a dog, and if saving the washing water is impossible due to lack of a vessel. If it is possible to save the washing water in a vessel, tayammum is not permissible due to fear for his animal. Know that if a person is thirsty and another has water: if the owner of the water needs it for his own thirst, he is more entitled to it; otherwise, he must give it to the one in dire need. If he does not give it, he [the needy] can take it from him and is allowed to fight him. If he kills the owner of the water, his blood is shed without liability (hader); if the other is killed, it is guaranteed (mamun). It is appropriate that the needy person guarantee the value of the water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 116]

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions that make tayammum permissible when water is available but its use would cause harm. The author, 'Ibn 'Abidin in his commentary on Nur al-Idah, expands on each condition. The first condition is illness: the law distinguishes four types of sick persons regarding tayammum. The key point is that if water harms the person or he cannot use it himself and finds no one to assist him, tayammum is allowed. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if someone is available to help but not obedient (e.g., a stranger who demands a fee), Abu Hanifa allows tayammum unconditionally if the helper does not assist without payment, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) only allow it if the fee is exorbitant (over a quarter dirham). The second condition is cold: there is a dispute about whether one with minor impurity can do tayammum due to cold. The correct view is that it is not allowed; only a junub (major impurity) person may do so. The third condition is fear of an enemy: this includes any threat to life, wealth, or honor, and even a debtor fearing imprisonment. No repetition (i'ada) of prayer is required in these cases. The fourth condition is thirst: if using water for wudu would lead to death from thirst, tayammum is allowed for oneself, one's companion, or one's animal. If the water can be saved in a vessel, tayammum is not allowed for the animal's sake. The passage ends with a ruling: if a thirsty person takes water from another who is not in need, and a fight ensues, the killer's blood is subject to different rules depending on who is killed.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Minor impurity requiring wudu.
جنب (junub): Person in major impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because cold is a valid excuse.
B) No, it is only for the junub.
C) Yes, but only if he is also ill.
D) No, never.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum due to cold is a dispensation specifically for the junub, not for those with minor impurity.

Tayammum due to Fear of Enemy and Thirst: General Rulings and Water Rights
Lists conditions for tayammum with intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions for tayammum due to fear and thirst, and state the ruling on taking water from another person when in dire need.

Core Idea
Fear of life, wealth, or honor, and risk of death from thirst permit tayammum; extreme thirst may justify forceful taking of water.

This lesson covers two more conditions for tayammum: fear of an enemy and fear of thirst. The text broadens the definition of 'enemy' to include any threat to person, property, or trust. For thirst, it extends the concern to companions and animals. It ends with a legal discussion on water rights: when a thirsty person may take water from another.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of 'enemy'
The passage says enemy is unrestricted: includes human or non-human, and fear for self, wealth, or trust. Also, a debtor fearing imprisonment is excused.
This is a broad interpretation, emphasizing the principle of necessity.
2
Apply the ruling on no repetition
Those who perform tayammum due to such fears do not need to repeat their prayers later, even if the fear subsides.
Marked by the phrase 'wa la i'adah' (no repetition).
3
Analyze the condition of thirst
If using water for wudu risks death by thirst, tayammum is allowed. This includes immediate or future threat, and extends to companions and animals.
The ability to save washing water (ghasala) affects the ruling for animals.
4
Examine the water rights ruling
If a person is thirsty and another has water: the owner has priority if he also needs it. Otherwise, he must give it. If he refuses, the needy may take it by force, with legal consequences.
This is a separate legal principle beyond tayammum.

Tayammum for Prayers with No Substitute: Funeral and Eid
Explains the principle that tayammum is allowed for prayers with no substitute, including funeral and Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that tayammum is allowed only for prayers with no substitute, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wali of the deceased.

Core Idea
Tayammum is only allowed to avoid missing a prayer that has no substitute, like Janazah and Eid.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes a key principle for the permissibility of tayammum: it is only legitimate when one fears missing an act of worship that has no substitute (khalaf). The author then applies this to funeral and Eid prayers, and presents an important intra-madhhab difference concerning the wali (guardian) of the deceased. Understanding this principle helps distinguish between prayers where tayammum is valid and those where it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
The passage states a general rule: tayammum is not allowed for acts that have a substitute, such as daily prayers (which have qada) and Friday prayer (which has Zuhr). Conversely, tayammum is allowed for acts that have no substitute, like funeral and Eid prayers. Identify this principle and locate it in the Arabic text.
Key Arabic phrase: 'ما يفوت إلى خلف لا يتيمم له' – whatever is lost to a substitute, tayammum is not performed for it.
2
Apply the principle to funeral and Eid prayers
Both funeral prayer and Eid prayer have no substitute, so tayammum is permissible to avoid missing them. The passage explicitly mentions both. Note that the principle applies whether the prayer is performed early or late (e.g., building upon previous prayer).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the wali
The passage presents a disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding the wali (guardian) of the deceased. One narration from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa holds that the wali cannot do tayammum because he can wait for others and has the right to repeat the prayer if he missed it. The apparent riwaya (zahir al-riwaya) holds that he can, because waiting is disliked. Identify both positions and their proofs.
The dispute is between two transmissions attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa himself.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the wali must repeat the funeral prayer if he did tayammum and prayed. According to the first view, he must repeat; according to the second, no repetition. The author of al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, considered the first view correct, while Shams al-A'imma preferred the second. Note that the mufta bihi today can vary based on later preference.
This is a case of legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Differentiate between prayers with and without substitute
Summarize: tayammum is valid for funeral and Eid (no substitute) and invalid for daily prayers (have qada) and Jumu'ah (has Zuhr). This step reinforces the principle and corrects the common misconception that tayammum can be used for any time-bound prayer.
Memorize the list: substitute prayers include daily fard and Jumu'ah; non-substitute include Janazah, Eidain, and perhaps other non-repeatable acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خوف فوت إلخ أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها تفوت بلا خلف، والأصل في هذا الباب أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا يتيمم له عند خوف فوته كالوقتية، فإنها تفوت إلى خلفه و وهو القضاء، أو كالجمعة فخلفه الظهر، وما لا خلف له يتيمم له كالعيدين وصلاة الجنازة. صلاة جنازة قيل: لا يجوز التيمم للولي في رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه ينتظر، ولو صلوا له حق الإعادة، قال صاحب "الهداية" : هو الصحيح، وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز للولي أيضاً؛ لأن الانتظار فيها مكروه، ولو لم ينتظروه، جاز له التيمم، قال شمس الأئمة هو الصحيح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣١/١] أو عيد ولو بناءً، وليس من العذر خوف فوت الجمعة والوقت.
Fear of missing etc.: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing funeral prayer, because it is lost with no substitute. The principle in this chapter is that whatever is lost to a substitute, tayammum is not performed for it when fearing its loss, like the time-bound [prayers], for they are lost to their substitute, which is qada, or like Friday, whose substitute is Zuhr. Whatever has no substitute, tayammum is performed for it, like the two Eids and funeral prayer. Funeral prayer: It was said that tayammum is not permissible for the guardian (wali) according to the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, because he waits [for others], and if they pray for him, he has the right to repeat. The author of al-Hidayah said: this is correct. In the apparent riwaya, it is also permissible for the guardian, because waiting in it is disliked, and if they do not wait, tayammum is permissible for him. Shams al-A'imma said this is correct. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:131] Or Eid, even if building [on the prayer], and it is not an excuse fear of missing Friday and [the time of] the obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage establishes a key principle for tayammum: it is only allowed to avoid missing a prayer that has no substitute (khalaf). For example, the five daily prayers have qada as a substitute, so one cannot do tayammum fearing the time will pass; similarly, Friday prayer has Zuhr as a substitute. However, funeral prayer and Eid prayer have no substitute, so tayammum is allowed to avoid missing them. The author then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wali (guardian) of the deceased. According to a narration from al-Hasan, Abu Hanifa held that the wali cannot do tayammum because he can wait for others, and if they pray he has the right to repeat. But according to the apparent riwaya (zahir al-riwaya), it is permissible for the wali because waiting is disliked, and if they do not wait, he can do tayammum. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah preferred the first view, while Shams al-A'imma preferred the second. The passage concludes that tayammum for Eid is allowed even if one is building upon the previous prayer (i.e., joining late), and that fear of missing Friday prayer or the time of an obligatory prayer is not a valid excuse for tayammum.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The legal guardian of the deceased, usually a close relative, who is responsible for arranging the funeral prayer.
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or replacement; in this context, a prayer that can replace the missed one, such as qada for daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, why is tayammum allowed for fear of missing funeral prayer but not for fear of missing the time of an obligatory daily prayer?
A) Because funeral prayer is shorter than daily prayers.
B) Because funeral prayer has no substitute (khalaf), while daily prayers have qada.
C) Because funeral prayer can only be performed once, while daily prayers can be repeated.
D) Because the reward of funeral prayer is greater.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid for funeral and Eid prayers because they have no substitute; internal Hanafi disagreement exists for the wali's case.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Conditions of Tayammum: Pure Earth and Complete Wiping
Ruling statement with conditions for tayammum validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three additional conditions for tayammum (pure earth, complete coverage, wiping with most of the hand) and apply them to determine validity.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires pure earth, full coverage, and wiping with most of the hand; any shortfall invalidates it.

In this lesson, we examine the third, fourth, and fifth conditions of tayammum as detailed in Nur al-Idah. These conditions specify the material allowed and the precise manner of wiping. Understanding them is essential to performing tayammum correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Locate the third, fourth, and fifth conditions: material (pure earth genus), coverage (isti'ab), manner (wiping with entire or most of hand).
Each is a shart for validity.
2
Specify valid and invalid materials
Valid: soil, sand, stone. Invalid: wood, silver, gold (burn or melt). A subtle point explains why only earth-derived materials work.
Impure earth also invalid.
3
Understand complete coverage (isti'ab)
The entire face and hands must be wiped. The ring must be moved, bracelet removed, fingers interlinked. Some scholars accept most of the area, but the relied-upon view requires full coverage.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists.
4
Distinguish from wudu's head wiping
In tayammum, wiping with only two fingers is invalid even if repeated to cover the area, unlike wudu where a small part suffices for the head.
The key difference: manner of wiping requires most of the hand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: أن يكون التيمم بطاهر من جنس الأرض، كالتراب والحجر والرمل، لا الحطب والفضة والذهب.
الرابع: استيعاب المحل بالمسح. الخامس: أن يمسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها حتى لو مسح بإصبعين لا يجوز، ولو كرر حتى استوعب، بخلاف مسح الرأس.
وصلية
وصلية
عيد: أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة عيد بتمامها فإن كان بحيث لو توضاً يدرك بعضها مع الإمام لا يتيمم. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۱۷] ولو بناء: أي ولو كان يبني بناء جاز له التيمم وصورته: أن يشرع مع الإمام في صلاة العيد، ثم يحدث المقتدي أو الإمام جاز له التيمم للبناء عند أبي حنيفة وقالا إن شرع بطهارة الوضوء لا يجوز له التيمم، وإن شرع بالتيمم جاز له البناء به تبيين الحقائق: ۱۳۲/۱] وليس من العذر إلخ: أي إذا خاف فوت الجمعة إلى أن يتوضأ لها، أو خاف خروج الوقت في سائر الأوقات إلى أن يشتغل بالطهارة لا يجوز له التيمم بل يتوضأ؛ لأنها تفوت إلى بدل والفوات إلى بدل كلا فوات [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣٢/١]
بطاهر: أي طيب، وهو الذي لم تمسه نجاسة، ولو زالت بذهاب أثرها. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۱۸] من جنس الأرض: اعلم أن الفاصل بين جنس الأرض وغيره: أن كل شيء يحترق بالنار ويصير رماداً ليس من جنس الأرض، وكذا كل شيء ينطبع ويذوب بالنار ، وكل شيء تأكله الأرض ليس من جنسها. (زيلعي بتصرف) لا الحطب إلخ أي لا يصح التيمم لنحو الحطب إلخ، وههنا ،لطيفة، وهي أن الله تعالى خلق درة ونظر إليها فصارت ماء، ثم تكاثف منه فصار تراباً، وتلطف منه فصار هواء، وتلطف منه فصار ناراً، فكان الماء أصلاً، ذكره المفسرون، وهو منقول عن التوراة، فإذا تعذر الطهارة بالأصل انتقل إلى التبع وأقيم مقامه، والنبات كالشجر ونحوه والمعدني كالحديد وشبهه ليس بتبع للماء وحده حتى يقوم مقامه، ولا للتراب كذلك، وإنما هو مركب من العناصر الأربعة، فليس له اختصاص بشيء منها حتى تقوم مقامه. (العناية) استيعاب المحل إلخ [وهو الوجه واليدان إلى المرفقين] اعلم أن الاستيعاب شرط في ظاهر الرواية حتى يحرك الرجل ،خاتمه، والمرأة سوارها، أو ينزعانهما، ويخلل الأصابع ويمسح جميع بشرة الوجه والشعر على الصحيح، وما بين العذار والأذن إلحاقا له بأصله، وقيل: يكفي مسح أكثر الوجه واليدين. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٠] أو بأكثرها أو بما يقوم مقامها كيد غيره. لا يجوز لفقد كون المسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها. ولو كرر إلخ أي لا يجوز التيمم ولو كرر المسح بإصبعين حتى استوعب الوجه واليدين؛ لفقد الشرط المذكور من كون المسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها. بخلاف مسح الرأس : أي حكم مسح الرأس مخالف للتيمم، فإنه لو مسح الرأس بإصبعين جاز مسحه، ولا كذلك التيمم.
Third: that the tayammum be with something pure (clean) from the genus of the earth, like soil, stone, and sand, not firewood, silver, and gold. Fourth: covering the area of wiping completely. Fifth: to wipe with the entire hand or most of it, such that if he wipes with two fingers it is not permissible, even if he repeats until he covers the area, contrary to wiping the head. [Marginal notes:] Eid: i.e., tayammum is permissible for fear of missing the entire Eid prayer; if by performing wudu he would catch part of it with the imam, he does not do tayammum. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 117] And even if building: i.e., even if he is building upon [the prayer], tayammum is permissible for him. Its form: he begins with the imam in the Eid prayer, then the follower or imam invalidates his wudu; it is permissible for him to do tayammum for the building (i.e., to continue) according to Abu Hanifa. The two said: if he began with the purity of wudu, tayammum is not permissible for him; but if he began with tayammum, it is permissible for him to build upon it. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:132] And it is not an excuse, etc.: i.e., if he fears missing Friday prayer by performing wudu for it, or fears the time passing in other prayers while engaging in purification, tayammum is not permissible for him; rather he should perform wudu, because they are lost to a substitute, and being lost to a substitute is like not being lost. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:132] 'With pure (tahir)': i.e., good (tayyib), that which no impurity has touched, even if its trace has disappeared. [Maraqi al-Falah: 118] 'From the genus of the earth': Know that the distinction between the genus of the earth and other things is that everything that burns with fire and becomes ash is not from the genus of the earth; likewise, everything that melts and dissolves with fire, and everything that the earth consumes is not from its genus. (Zayla'i with modification) 'Not firewood, etc.': i.e., tayammum is not valid with firewood, etc. And here is a subtle point: that Allah created a pearl and looked at it, and it became water; then it condensed and became soil; then it became subtle and became air; then it became subtle and became fire. So water was the original. The exegetes mentioned this, and it is transmitted from the Torah. When purification with the original is impossible, one transfers to the follower (tabe') and it takes its place. Plants like trees and the like, and minerals like iron and similar, are not followers of water alone to take its place, nor of soil in that way; rather they are composed of the four elements, so they have no specificity with any one of them to take its place. (al-'Inayah) 'Covering the area completely, etc.' [i.e., the face and the hands up to the elbows]: Know that covering completely is a condition in the apparent riwaya, such that a man should move his ring, and a woman her bracelet, or remove them, and interlace his fingers, and wipe all the skin of the face and the hair according to the correct view, and [the area] between the earlobe and the ear is attached to its origin. It was said: it is sufficient to wipe most of the face and hands. [Maraqi al-Falah: 120] 'or with most of it' or with what takes its place, like the hand of another. It is not permissible due to the lack of wiping with the entire hand or most of it. 'Even if he repeats, etc.': i.e., tayammum is not permissible even if he repeats wiping with two fingers until he covers the face and hands, because the mentioned condition of wiping with the entire hand or most of it is missing. 'Contrary to wiping the head': i.e., the ruling of wiping the head is opposite to tayammum, for if he wipes the head with two fingers, it is permissible, unlike in tayammum.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage details two additional conditions for tayammum: the material used must be clean (tahir, not najis) and from the genus of the earth, such as soil, sand, or stone, excluding things like wood or metals that burn or melt. A subtle cosmological point explains that water is the original element for purification, and earth is derived from it; plants and minerals are not purely of earth. The next condition is that the area of wiping (face and hands) must be completely covered (isti'ab) by wiping with the entire hand or at least most of it. Wiping with just two fingers is insufficient, even if repeated to cover the area. This is unlike wiping the head in wudu, where a small part suffices. The passage also repeats the ruling about Eid and building upon prayer, and reiterates that fear of missing Friday or the time of an obligatory prayer is not an excuse for tayammum. The commentator cites various sources like Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Maraqui al-Falah, and al-'Inayah.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti'ab): Complete coverage; in tayammum, it means wiping the entire face and both hands up to the elbows with the earth, leaving no dry spot.
مسح (mash): Wiping; in tayammum, it refers to passing the hands over the face and arms with earth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wiping the face and hands in tayammum using only two fingers?
A) It is permissible if the area is covered by repeating the wipe.
B) It is not permissible even if the area is fully covered.
C) It is permissible if no other means are available.
D) It is permissible only for the face, not the hands.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires three conditions: pure earth, complete coverage, and wiping with most of the hand; any violation invalidates it.
